THE COURTSHIP OF THE STATE v. EVERYONE

A trial conducted by registered post.

A novel in documents

────────────────────────────────────────────────

The State v. Domnica Albu
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

~107,000 words · 30 delivery cycles

    "It does not tell me whose order."
        — Routing Slip 0419, Cycle 1

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 1 — "In Good Order"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 1    ·    Early October, the Casimca running high and brown, the willows on Aleea Salciilor already half in water
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 1. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Ministerial Decree — Provisional Order No.9 (extract) — Ministry of Justice, District Bureau → Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [REGISTERED No. 0001]
  2. Indictment (Rechizitoriul) — Procuror A. Câmpeanu → The Proceeding, c/o Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [REGISTERED No. 0002]
  3. Registration Log — Central Sorting, Vâlcov (leaf for Cycle 1)
  4. Routing Slip 0419 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (carried to Cycle 2):
  · Indictment No.0002 — held one cycle — reason of record: "for good order" — slip 0419

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion):
  · One unsolicited letter, D. Albu → "the registry of Vâlcov, whoever that turns out to be" — received the 1st of October, two days before the indictment — not part of the file — retained at the Hold, by the stove

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0001]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 3rd of October]
[STAMP: VĂZUT / SEEN — violet — dated the 9th of August, two months prior]

MINISTRY OF JUSTICE — DISTRICT BUREAU
PROVISIONAL ORDER No.9
On the Conduct of Proceedings by Registered Post
(extract, certified true; full instrument deposited at the District Seat)

WHEREAS the Palatul de Justiție of the town of Vâlcov stands condemned by engineer's report, its eastern third having entered the river Casimca, and no funds being appropriated either for its repair or for its demolition;

AND WHEREAS the national connection is rationed, by superior decree, to the hours of 06:00 to 10:00 and reserved in those hours for state functions of record, such that no certified digital channel exists for the conduct of trials;

AND WHEREAS the post is the sole organ of state retaining an unbroken chain of custody;

IT IS PROVIDED:

§1. That criminal proceedings in the affected districts shall be conducted by registered letter.

§2. That the Central Sorting Office of the relevant town is hereby designated the registry and chain-of-custody authority for each proceeding so conducted.

§3. That every instrument entering a proceeding shall be registered, dated by postmark, and held or released by the said registry IN GOOD ORDER (în bună rânduială), and that the postmark shall stand as evidence of the time of a thing.

§4. That under the security provisions obtaining in time of emergency (see §7), the registry may withhold from delivery any matter prejudicial to public order.

§5. That paper employed in any proceeding shall be of a grammage not less than seventy nor greater than ninety grams per square metre, white or near-white, and that envelopes of the kraft sort are forbidden as unbecoming the dignity of the state.

§14. That a ruling becomes effective only upon its delivery to the accused and the return to the registry of a signed acknowledgement of receipt (aviz de primire). An undelivered ruling is of no force.

BY ORDER, the District Bureau.
[STAMP: VĂZUT / SEEN — violet]


[REGISTERED No. 0002]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 3rd of October — received 16:40, the last sorting of the day]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
RECHIZITORIUL — INDICTMENT
Filed by Procuror Anghel Câmpeanu, of the District Seat

To the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov, and to the Magistrate appointed thereto —

The State charges DOMNICA ALBU, schoolteacher, of Aleea Salciilor in the town of Vâlcov, aged thirty-eight years, that on the night of the 14th of September last she did wilfully and with knowledge of the consequence introduce a poisonous compound into the public water supply at the intake of the Uzina de Îmbuteliere "Aurora Nr.4," whence the town of Vâlcov and the said plant draw upon a common aquifer; and that as a result thereof the said supply was rendered noxious, and persons drinking of it were made ill.

The State will demonstrate, by witnesses whose declarations are appended and whose statements will follow in their due course, that the accused procured the said compound in the days immediately preceding; that she was seen upon the access road, Drumul Aurora, in the hours of darkness; and that the water, having been good, became bad, and became bad on the night she was present, which the State submits is not a coincidence but a sequence, the latter being merely the former with its sleeves rolled up.

The accused is a person of education and is therefore the more culpable, education being the faculty by which a person is presumed to foresee. The State seeks the penalty appropriate to the wilful endangerment of a community.

The accused is advised that, no advocate being available within the district at a fee the district can meet, she is entitled and required to defend herself by letter, under the austerity provision of Order No.9.

Respectfully — and with the observation, which the State trusts a provincial registry will not take amiss, that this matter ought to be concluded with dispatch, the river not improving and the season being against us —

ANGHEL CÂMPEANU
Procuror, District Seat


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

Opened this day, the registry of The State v. Domnica Albu. Forty years this office has logged the births, the deaths, the deeds, and the seed catalogues of Vâlcov, in that proportion. It will now log a trial. The book is the same book. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0419.
Held: the Indictment, No.0002, one cycle.
Reason of record:

I have read Order No.9 in full this morning — the full instrument, not the certified extract, the office keeping a copy from the spring it was issued, the spring the river took the courthouse — and I find it a careful piece of work. It specifies the grammage of the paper on which justice may be done, not less than seventy grams nor more than ninety. It forbids the kraft envelope as unbecoming. It tells me the weight of a thing and the colour of a thing and the dignity of a thing. It tells me that the postmark shall stand as evidence of the time of a thing, and that I am to deliver every instrument *in good order.*

It does not tell me whose order.

I have read that phrase eleven times — *în bună rânduială* — looking for the clause that says: in the order received, or in the order written, or in the order that a thing happened, and there is no such clause, because the men who wrote Order No.9 had a courthouse when they wrote it and could not imagine that the order of arrival of the truth would ever be a question for anyone, let alone a question for the man who runs the post. The Ministry has legislated the grammage of justice and forgotten its sequence. I will supply the sequence.

This is not, I wish to be clear in the record, an irregularity. The decree commands good order and is silent as to its kind. I am the registry. I am, therefore, by the plain reading of §2 and §3, the order. I record this not as a confession — there is nothing yet to confess — but as a matter that a man should set down at the beginning of a thing, the way a surveyor sets down where he placed the first stake, so that whoever follows him can see how the field was measured.

As to the hold:

The indictment arrived at twenty minutes to five, in the last sorting of the day, on the same cycle as the decree that makes a trial of it. If I release them together, the town of Vâlcov will learn in one breath that there is a law for trying people by post and that the first person to be tried is the schoolteacher of Aleea Salciilor — and they will not have had a single hour in which to absorb the first fact before the second arrives to colour it. I do not think a town should learn the rules of a game and the name of its loser in the same envelope. I will release the decree this cycle and the indictment the next, so that the people of this town understand, for one day, that such a thing as a trial-by-letter exists, before they are asked to believe a particular woman guilty of a particular night.

There is no operational necessity for the hold. The river is high but the Podul Vechi is passable; I cannot blame the bridge today, though I note for the record that I could. I hold the indictment because a thing landing first is believed first, and I would rather the law arrive before the accusation, the way one would rather a man learn there is such a thing as fire before he learns the house is burning.

I note, finally — the form having a line for the matter, marked *Particulars of Item*, and no one but myself ever reading this form — that the accused's name is well-formed. Albu. White. The plant that is supposed to have been poisoned bottles white water under a white name, Aurora, the dawn, and the woman accused of poisoning it is named for the colour of clean water, and somewhere a man at the Ministry decided this was a country where such things would simply have to be true at the same time. It is not a reason for the hold. I am recording it anyway. The form has a line for it and the line was empty.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[The following is NOT registered to the proceeding. No number. Received the 1st of October, before there was a case to receive it into. Retained at the Hold, by the stove. — G.E.]

To the registry of Vâlcov, whoever that turns out to be —

I am told that justice has moved into the post office, the courthouse being in the river, and that a letter is now the only door a person may knock on. So I am knocking before anyone has accused me, which I understand is not how it is done, but I have read the part of Order No.9 that the District Bureau posted on the church board, and it does not forbid a person from writing in advance of her own indictment. It forbids the kraft envelope. This is not a kraft envelope.

Here is what I want on the record before the record begins, while it is still only me and the man who sorts the letters and the stove I am told you keep them by:

On the night of the fourteenth of September the water in the well on Aleea Salciilor tasted of bitterness, and then of coins, and then of nothing — and the nothing is the part no one will ask me about, because nothing is hard to indict. But you should know that nothing is the worst of the three. Bitter is a warning and coins is a warning, and when a thing you have drunk your whole life stops tasting of anything at all, it has stopped being water and become a question, and a child I taught his letters two winters running could not keep it down, and there was no one. The plant would not answer. The pharmacist would not answer. The number for the district health office answers only between six and ten in the morning and the water did not wait for the four hours.

I am not going to tell you, in this letter, what I did. I am going to tell you what I was *for,* because I have a feeling — I cannot account for it, except that a person who handles every letter in a town must come to know the difference between the ones written by people who expect to be believed and the ones written by people who have stopped — I have a feeling that the order of these things is going to matter very much, and that you are the one who will decide it, and that you are the only person in this whole proceeding who is going to read what I actually wrote instead of what the State needs me to have meant.

So: read carefully. I will write carefully. We are, the two of us, the only ones left in this republic who still believe a sentence is a kind of evidence.

I remain, with a respect I did not expect to feel for a sorting office,

DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school


ROUTING SLIP 0431.
Status: not applicable. This item is not on the proceeding and has no delivery to govern. The slip is opened for the sole reason that I have read the letter above and the form is the only place in the building where a man is permitted to set down what he has read.

It is not evidence. It arrived two days before the indictment; it answers a charge that did not yet exist; under no clause of Order No.9 am I obliged to enter it, and under §4 I might reasonably withhold a thing this candid as "matter prejudicial to public order," the public order in question being my own. I am not entering it. I am also not, the reader will note, doing the other thing a careful registry does with an item it has decided is not part of the file, which is return it to sender marked *no such proceeding.* I have neither registered it nor returned it. I have put it by the stove.

I will say what I am able to say accurately, the form asking for the *Particulars of Item:* I have sorted the mail of this town for thirty years, and I have read perhaps two hundred thousand letters in the course of certifying that they were posted, and I did not know, until twenty minutes ago, that I had been reading them the way a man reads a timetable — for the information, for the route, for whether the thing would arrive. This is the first letter in thirty years that I have read the way she says she writes them. Carefully. Twice. Then a third time, because the second time I caught myself reading for the information again — *did she do it, what did she do* — and had to go back and read it for the sentences, which is what she sent it for, and which is, I find, an entirely different country.

She has guessed at me. There is no me to guess at — there is a registry, a stove, a rack of pigeonholes, a man who keeps the only purple ink in Vâlcov — but she has addressed all of it as though it were a person, "whoever that turns out to be," and the unbearable thing, the thing I am recording because the form has a line for it and no one but me will ever read this line, is that for the duration of one letter it turned out to be one.

I have read it eleven times. I am not going to deliver it to anyone, ever, including her. It is not part of the file and it will not become part of the file. It will sit in the Hold by the stove, and tomorrow when the indictment goes out it will be warm, and the indictment, which arrived cold from the District Seat, will go out into the town to teach Vâlcov that this woman is a question the State intends to answer — and I will know, alone in this building, that two days before the State decided what she was, she decided what I was, and that her account of it is better than the State's.

The decree at first light. The indictment the cycle after. This letter nowhere.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the indictment, No.0002, before it went to the Hold:]
The Procuror writes that a sequence is "merely a former with its sleeves rolled up." He means it against her. He does not know he has handed the registry its whole philosophy in a figure of speech and signed it. I will keep this one. A prosecutor who believes that the order of things is the whole of their meaning, and who has posted his belief to the one man in the Republic in a position to act on it — this is the kind of gift a careful man does not acknowledge out loud.

He has also asked us to be quick. They always ask the post to be quick. To the Procuror, the mail is plumbing: you open a tap at the District Seat and justice comes out of a faucet in Vâlcov, and if it is slow, the pipe wants cleaning. He does not know that the pipe decides. He will learn it the way everyone learns it, which is too late and from the wrong direction.

The indictment goes to the Hold tonight. The decree goes out at first light, before the four hours, with the milk and the ration lists. Tomorrow the town will know there is a law. The day after, it will learn whom the law has come for. That is one day of mercy I am able to give a woman I have never met and whose defence has not yet been written, and it costs the State nothing but a day it was going to lose to the river anyway.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — to release Cycle 2]

CHAPTER 2 — "The Defendant Is Advised of Her Right to Reply by Post"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 2    ·    Mid-October, the Casimca dropped a hand's-width overnight and left a brown tideline on the willows, the first frost on the inside of the Sorting Office windows by the Terminal, none yet by the Stove

[REGISTERED No. 0002]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 3rd of October — released the 16th]
[The indictment, carried from Cycle 1 per slip 0419, went out this cycle to Aleea Salciilor and to the magistrate. Its full text stands at No.0002 of Cycle 1 and is not reproduced. — G.E.]


[REGISTERED No. 0003]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 16th of October]
[The following is written on the reverse of a printed slip. The printed face reads, in part: AUR. FUEL & FAGGOT — PIAȚA LIPSEI — STALL 6 — *birch, two ster, split, dry, sold the 12th October* — *PAID.* The magistrate's query is written across the back in a cramped hand that crowds the right margin as though saving paper.]

MAGISTRATE'S OPENING QUERY
In the matter of The State v. Domnica Albu
Issued by Toader Lupu, Magistrate of Vâlcov, the office of the Judecător being at the District Seat and his SEEN stamp pending

To Domnica Albu, schoolteacher, of Aleea Salciilor —

You are advised that a charge has been laid against you and registered to a proceeding conducted, by Provisional Order No.9, entirely by post. I am the magistrate appointed to it. I am writing to you on the back of a receipt because the office allocation of Form 11-D ("Notice to the Accused of the Right to Reply") was exhausted in the spring and not renewed, the printer at the District Seat being, I am told, "between contracts." A receipt is what I have. It is at least clean on this side.

You are advised, under §11 of the said Order, the austerity provision, that no advocate may be assigned to you within this district at a fee the district is in a position to meet, and that you are therefore entitled — the Order says *entitled*; I would have said *obliged*, but the Order is the Order — to defend yourself by letter. Your replies, addressed to the Proceeding care of the Central Sorting Office, will be registered, stamped as to the date of their posting, and entered as your defense. The postmaster certifies that a thing was posted. He does not certify that it is true. That part the Order leaves to me, and to whatever faculty I have left for it after a winter of selling wood.

You are advised that you have until the close of the second delivery cycle from your receipt of this notice to enter your first reply, and that a failure to reply may be read, under §11, as a thing I will not write down here because you have not yet failed and I would rather not put the word in the file before you have earned it.

I append, as the Order requires, the clauses under which you stand: §7 (introduction of a noxious matter into a common supply) of the emergency schedule, as amended; and §7-bis, the aggravating provision, which I will set out for you in full when I have located my copy of the amendment, the office copy having gone for kindling in February by a hand I will not name, it being my own.

I apologise for the delay between the laying of the charge and this notice. It is not, I am assured by the registry, a delay of the registry's making. It is the season. The Podul Vechi was over the road three days last week and a man cannot post what the river will not let cross.

By the authority vested in me — vested, I should be honest with you at the outset, by no one currently paying me, but vested all the same, the Order saying nothing about whether authority survives non-payment, and I have decided that it does, because if it does not then nothing in Vâlcov has any authority at all and we may as well let the building finish falling into the water on its own schedule —

I remain, in cold but in good faith,

T. LUPU
Magistrate of Vâlcov, at Stall 6, Piața Lipsei, mornings, or at the Sorting Office by post


[REGISTERED No. 0004]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 17th of October — received 09:50, ten minutes before the connection closed, though it came by foot and not by wire]
[Filed warm. — G.E.]

DEFENSE LETTER No.1
The State v. Domnica Albu
Entered by the accused, self-represented

To the registry of Vâlcov, and to the Magistrate, and to whoever holds this before either of them does —

I have your notice. I want to begin by thanking the Magistrate for it, which I expect is not how these letters usually open, but I have read a great many official papers in my life — a schoolteacher reads more state paper than a soldier — and his is the first in some years to apologise to me before accusing me, and to do it in his own cold hand on the back of his own honest receipt. Two ster of birch, split, dry, paid. I have taught the children of men who sold wood. It is hard work and the price is never what the work was. I mention it only so the court knows I read the whole sheet, both sides, which is a habit I cannot put down and which I suspect is going to be, before this is finished, the only thing I have to offer in my defense.

Now. The corrections, and I make them as a teacher and not as an enemy, because I have learned that the surest way to lose a thing is to let it be said imprecisely about you and not say so.

The Magistrate cites §7 of the emergency schedule, "introduction of a noxious matter into a common supply." I have the Order. I have read it more often than is healthy, the District Bureau having posted the full instrument on the board of the church on Strada Cazaclia, where I go not for the sermon but because it is the only public copy in town and I am the only person who stops to read it, the rest of Vâlcov having decided, sensibly, that a law you cannot afford to break is not a law you need to study. §7 does not say "noxious matter." §7 says "a matter rendering the supply *noxious in the result*." It is not the same sentence. The first describes a thing a person carries. The second describes a thing that happens after, and may have had several authors, and one of them may have been a person trying, badly, to make the water less of one and not more. I do not say which I am. I say only that the difference between the clause as written and the clause as cited is the difference between hanging a noun and weighing a verb, and I have read the Procuror's indictment now, which arrived this same morning, a full cycle after I was told a charge existed, and the Procuror makes the same slide, with, I think, less excuse, his copy not having gone for kindling.

The Magistrate cites §7-bis as "the aggravating provision" and confesses he cannot find it. I can spare him the search. §7-bis is the *education* provision: it aggravates the offense where the accused is "a person of instruction, presumed thereby to foresee." The Procuror leans on it heavily. I would like the court to notice what a strange machine it is. It says: the more a person was taught, the more guilty she is of failing to predict the future. I taught fractions to forty children in a room that floods. I could not predict the future of that room from one autumn to the next. But the State has decided that because I can spell *aquifer* — which the Magistrate, forgive me, spelled three ways in three lines, *aquefer, aqifer,* and once, beautifully, *aquaver,* which is almost a word for the way water shakes — because I can spell it, I am presumed to have foreseen what trained engineers with the plant's own instruments did not, or did and did not say. I will accept §7-bis the day the State applies it to the men who *built* the intake. They are persons of instruction too. They have just been instructed by a different paymaster.

I am told to confine myself to the facts. I would like to. I find the facts will not hold still long enough to be confined, but here is one that will, and I give it to you plainly so that no order of arrival can soften it or sharpen it past what it is. On the night of the fourteenth of September I drew a cup from the well on Aleea Salciilor and could not name what I had drunk. It was not bitter the way medicine is bitter, nor sour the way the spring melt comes down sour off the fields; it had a taste a person has no word for because a person is never meant to need one, the taste of water that has decided, overnight, to stop being on our side. The indictment will tell you the supply was "rendered noxious." That is the State's word and it is a clean word and it is useless, because it describes a finding and not a mouthful. I will give you the mouthful, since I am the one who has had it: I drank, and I understood, before I understood anything else, that the well had quietly changed its mind about us. A boy I had taught his letters two winters running drank the same and could not keep it down, and there was no one. The plant did not answer. The pharmacy did not answer. The number for the district health office answers only between six and ten in the morning, and the water did not consult the four hours before it turned.

So I acted. I will not, in this first letter, tell the court *what* I did, and I want to be exact about why I am withholding it, because withholding looks like guilt and I will not have it mistaken for that. I am withholding it because the moment I name the thing I did, the court will stop weighing a woman and start weighing a powder, and a powder weighs the same in every hand, the saving hand and the harming one, and the whole case will collapse into chemistry, which is precisely where the men who actually own the water would like it to collapse, because chemistry has no motive and motive is the only place I am innocent. I will give you the act when I have first been given the courtesy of the question no one in this proceeding has yet thought to ask, which is not *what did she do* but *what was she for.*

I ask, formally, one thing, and I ask it of the registry and not of the Magistrate, because I have a feeling it is the registry's to grant: that the evidence in this matter be entered, and disclosed to me, **in the order in which it was gathered.** Not in the order the Procuror prefers, which I can already feel will be a sequence built to land heaviest on me first; and not in the order it happens to cross the river, which the river decides and the river is not just; but in the order it *occurred* — the plant's records before my purchase, my purchase before that night, that night before the morning a child was sick, the morning before the indictment. If the court will give me the truth in the order it actually happened, I will not need an advocate. The sequence is the advocate. I have never in my life had to ask anyone to give me events in the order they came, because I assumed that was simply what *order* meant. I am beginning to suspect, from the shape of this proceeding, that it is a thing a person here has to grant, and that there is someone in a position to grant it, and that he is reading this.

If I am right that you are there — and I cannot account for the feeling, except that a person who has handled every letter in a town must come to read them differently from a person who only receives one — then I will say to you what I would not waste on the file: read this one the way I wrote it. Slowly. Twice. The first time for whether I did it. The second time for the sentences, which is what I sent it for, and which is the only part of me the State has not yet found a clause to charge.

I remain, more carefully than the court can presently afford to read,

DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school
which floods, and which I would like back before the children forget their letters from disuse


ROUTING SLIP 0421.
Released, all same cycle: the indictment (0002, carried from the Hold), the Magistrate's query (0003), and the accused's first reply (0004).
Reason of record:

I had decided, the reader of this slip will recall — the reader being myself, no one else opening this form in forty years of forms — to give the town one day of knowing there was such a thing as a trial-by-letter before it learned whom the letter had come for. That mercy is spent. The indictment went out this morning with the milk and the query, and by noon Vâlcov knew both that the law has moved into the post office and that it has come for the schoolteacher, and a boy I do not know was already standing across Strada Făgădău looking up at this building as though it had grown a second floor in the night. It has not. It has only started keeping a person in a drawer.

Three papers, one cycle, and I will set down why I released them together when I am, on the record, a man who holds things.

I released the query and the indictment together because Order No.9 §11 requires the accused be advised of her right to reply, and the right to reply is meaningless before there is something to reply *to.* To send the indictment without the notice is to accuse a person who does not yet know she may answer; to send the notice without the indictment is to warn a person against an attack that has not landed. They are two halves of one cruelty and the only decent thing is to deliver the cruelty whole. I record this as procedure. It is procedure. I note only that I had never before thought of "complete delivery" as a kindness.

As to her reply.

It came by foot, not by wire, a child of the Pop family carrying it up Strada Făgădău and handing it across the counter at ten minutes to ten, breathless, the Terminal already making the sound it makes when the four hours are ending, which is no sound, which is the worst sound. The child would not say who sent her. She did not need to. I had the envelope. It was warm. I want to record that accurately, the form having a line for the condition of an item: it was warm because it had been carried inside a coat against a child's ribs across a cold town, and for no mystical reason whatever — and I am a man who has certified the temperature of a great many envelopes, and I know the difference between an envelope warmed by a stove and an envelope warmed by a person, and this was the second kind, and I have no professional category for it, and so I am filing it under *condition of item*, which is the only line that will take it.

I have read it. I read it once for whether she did it, which is what the State pays the registry to certify it has read for — and the answer the first reading gives is the answer she intends it to give, which is *I cannot tell,* which she has built on purpose, the way a careful sorter builds a hold that holds either way, so that whichever truth arrives next, this one will already be standing where it can argue with it. I see exactly what she has done. I have spent thirty years arranging paper so that it does the work a hand is not permitted to do, and I have never once been done it back, and that is itself a thing I should not be recording.

Then I read it a second time, because she asked me to, in a letter that is not addressed to me and cannot be, addressed to "whoever holds this," which is a category and not a man, except that for the length of one reading it stopped being a category.

She has asked the registry to disclose the evidence "in the order in which it was gathered," and this is the most dangerous sentence anyone has yet put into this file, and the danger is mine. She thinks she is asking for fairness. She is asking the one man in the Republic who has just discovered he can decide what order the truth arrives in, and who has decided, in slip 0419, that he is the order, to please be just — and she is asking it in prose good enough that I can feel myself wanting to be, which is not the same as being, and a careful man should not confuse the wanting with the thing. I am recording the wanting here so that later, when I cannot tell them apart, the record will at least show I once could.

She corrects the Magistrate's spelling of *aquifer* — three ways, she counts them, and finds the third one, *aquaver,* "almost a word for the way water shakes." I read that line and did not move for a while. I am required to record my reasons. That is not a reason. I am recording it anyway, because the form has a line for the matter and no one reads this form but me, and a man should be allowed one true sentence per cycle even when he must file it under *miscellaneous.*

I note, for the continuity of the file and for the deputy who will one day read these and report them up his union channel and be, God help him, correct: I am not holding anything this cycle. Nothing of record. Let it be observed that on the one cycle a postmaster releases everything in its honest order, he does it for the accused, and that this, too, is a kind of thumb on the scale — the thumb that presses *down on nothing,* which is still a choice about where the scale rests. There is no order so innocent that choosing it is innocent. I am beginning to think that is the whole of what Order No.9 forgot to legislate, and the whole of what I am for.

One last matter, and it is administrative, and I am grateful to it for being administrative, the day having gone otherwise.

The green card returning from Aleea Salciilor — the aviz certifying she received the indictment and the query — came back signed in her hand, *D. Albu,* the date correct, the box ticked correctly for the first time in the history of this office, RECEIVED BY filled, DATE filled, nothing overflowing the lines. And folded inside the same envelope, by an error I am choosing to read as the Magistrate's and not the river's, was a half-sheet that does not belong to the proceeding: a tally in Lupu's cramped hand of birch sold off the stall this week — *Tue, 1 ster, the widow Crâșmaru, half-price; Wed, none, rain; Thu, 2 ster, paid; Fri, the schoolteacher, no charge.*

The schoolteacher, no charge.

I am not entering it. It is not a court paper; it is a wood-seller's reckoning; it tells the file nothing it is permitted to know. I am putting it by the stove with the other thing that is not part of the file, and I will return it to the Magistrate when he next crosses for wood, and I will not mention to him what it told me, which is that the man writing the queries in this case has been keeping the accused warm all winter for nothing, out of his own cold stall, and saying so to no one, on the only paper he could spare, which was the back of his own loss — and that there are, then, two men in Vâlcov giving this woman what they cannot afford and recording it where they think no one will read it.

His he gave in birch. Mine I give in order. His will keep her warm through one winter. Mine may keep her alive, or hang her, and I no longer entirely trust the man who is deciding which, which is the first time in thirty years I have written that sentence about myself, and I am filing it, as I file everything,

in good order. — G.E.


[margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of slip 0421:]
She wrote: *the sequence is the advocate.* She meant it as a request to the court. I am the court's hands and she does not know it. I have her advocate in my fist. The decent thing, the thing the whole file would be safer for, is to disclose the evidence exactly as she asked — in the order it occurred — and let the chips fall in the order God dealt them. I notice I am already, before the prosecution has sent a single witness, composing in my head the order I would *prefer.* The plant's records first, I am thinking. Her purchase late. The sick child early, so the town's heart is open before the powder arrives. I am thinking it the way she asked me not to, which is to say I am thinking of it as *better* than the order it happened in — kinder, truer to what she was — and I will have to watch that, because "truer to what she was" is exactly the sentence a man tells himself the moment before he stops telling the truth.

She asked for fairness and I felt myself reach instead for *mercy,* and they are not the same county, and I am the only one in this building who can tell the border, and I have just caught myself, on the very first cycle, already across it.

[REGISTERED No. 0014]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 11th of October]

PROSECUTION NOTICE
List of Intended Witnesses
Procuror Anghel Câmpeanu, of the District Seat

To the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov, and to the Magistrate appointed thereto —

Pursuant to Order No.9 and in the interest of dispatch — the season, as I have had occasion to remark, being against us — the State gives notice of the witnesses by whose declarations it will prove the charge. Their statements will follow by registered post, each accompanied by the Declaration of Posting required under §11, so that the registry may certify the fact of their posting in the usual way.

The State will call:

  i.   VALENTIN COSTEA, pharmacist, of lower Strada Făgădău, who will attest the sale, in the days before the night in question, of the compound named in the (redacted) submission already on file. This is the State's principal witness and his testimony its spine.

  ii.  TUDOR NEGOIȚĂ, smallholder, of Drumul Aurora, who will place the accused upon the access road in the hours of darkness.

  iii. RADU OLARU, manager of the Uzina de Îmbuteliere "Aurora Nr.4," who will attest the security of the plant's intake and the integrity of its records, and thereby establish that the harm entered the water by no hand but the one the State accuses.

The State requests that these declarations be delivered to the Proceeding *in the order listed above*, which is the order of their importance and, the State submits, of their logic: the purchase, then the presence, then the proof that no other agency was to blame. I am advised by the district that a provincial registry may be unfamiliar with the handling of a witness sequence, and I therefore set it out plainly, as even a careful clerk will appreciate the convenience of being told.

Expecting the registry's cooperation in the matter of speed,

ANGHEL CÂMPEANU
Procuror, District Seat


[REGISTERED No. 0015]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 11th of October]
[On the pharmacy's own letterhead — printed: FARMACIA COSTEA · Strada Făgădău · "Sănătatea Publică, Servită" — the printer's rule slightly crooked, set before the second currency reform]

FORM 12-B — DECLARATION OF POSTING
(Ministry of Justice, austerity issue; the witness's oath-substitute under Order No.9 §11)

I, the undersigned, declare that the foregoing was posted.

NAME OF DECLARANT ......... Valentin Costea
OCCUPATION ................ Pharmacist, and your humble servant of public health
MATTER POSTED ............. One witness statement, sealed, concerning a sale made at my counter, the truth of which I attest insofar as a man may attest the contents of his own ledger, which is to say completely, and the meaning of which I leave, with respect, entirely to wiser heads than a chemist's
NUMBER OF ENCLOSURES ...... One (1)
DATE OF POSTING ........... the 11th of October

I declare that the foregoing was posted. I declare further — the form not requiring it, but a careful man preferring to volunteer what may be asked — that I sell what is sold to whoever buys it, that the compound in question has a hundred lawful uses about a house and a garden and a sickroom, that I keep my ledger to the gram as the law obliges, and that if the registry should find my statement of use to the Proceeding I am, as ever, the servant of whatever the Proceeding requires of me. I am owed nothing by the asking of these questions and I ask nothing by the answering of them.

SIGNATURE ................. V. Costea
                           [a small neat hand, the letters not touching]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.   | DATE REC'D | FROM              | MATTER                       | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 0014  | 11 Oct.    | Procuror Câmpeanu | Witness list (3 named)       | Released, Cycle 3
 0015  | 11 Oct.    | V. Costea         | Form 12-B (Decl. of Posting) | Released, Cycle 3
 0015-a| 11 Oct.    | V. Costea         | The declared item (statement)| HELD — pending — slip 0019
 0016  | 11 Oct.    | T. Negoiță        | Form 12-B (Decl. of Posting) | Released, Cycle 3
 0017  | 12 Oct.    | R. Olaru          | Form 12-B (Decl. of Posting) | Released, Cycle 3
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Noted, for the registry's own instruction: the form is numbered 0015. The thing the form swears to is numbered 0015-a. They travel under one stamp and arrive as one envelope and the State imagines them a single act. They are two. The oath is here. The thing sworn to is in the Hold. I can release the swearing and withhold the sworn, and have. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0019.
Released, all of Cycle 3, save the declared item 0015-a, held pending.
Reason of record:

The Procuror has sent me a sequence and asked me to keep it. He has done this in writing, on registered paper, under his own hand and seal, which is the single most generous thing a prosecutor has ever done for an accused in this district, and he does not know it. He has set down — *the purchase, then the presence, then the proof* — the exact order in which a town's heart, met first by the purchase, would have no room left in it to acquit. He believes the order is the logic. He is right that it is the logic. He is wrong about whose hands the logic passes through on its way to becoming a verdict, the answer being mine.

I will not keep his order. I am not obliged to; §11 requires that I certify the *posting* of each declaration, not that I deliver the *declared items* in the order a party finds convenient, the two being — as the log now records — two different things wearing one stamp. So this cycle I release the three Forms 12-B, which swear only that three people put three envelopes into the post, and which prove nothing about the night but that three people in Vâlcov can be made to sign a paper. The town learns this morning that there are witnesses. It does not learn yet what they witnessed. There is a difference between knowing a gun exists and knowing where it is pointed, and a registry that respects the difference is a registry doing its work in good order.

I hold the declared item of the pharmacist — 0015-a, the statement itself, the spine — because it is the purchase, and the purchase is true, and the true thing arriving first is the thing the whole town will measure her by. I will let it land when the night it speaks of has a defence to stand beside it. The Procuror calls this the order of importance. I call it loading the most important shot first into an empty chamber and asking the registry to fire it before the accused has been handed anything to fire back. I decline. Filed under §11, which permits me to certify the posting of a thing this cycle and to deliver the thing itself in another, and which the men who wrote it surely meant only as a tidiness, never dreaming the tidiness was a trigger and the clerk a finger.

A word on the witnesses, the form having a line for the *Particulars of Item* and no one but me ever reading the particulars:

Costea writes that he is "owed nothing by the asking of these questions." A man who volunteers, unasked, that he is owed nothing has told you the precise sum he owes and merely declined to name it. The form did not ask after his debts. He answered the question anyway, the way a guilty floor creaks under a foot that was trying to be silent. I make no finding. I note that the pharmacist who owes the plant nine thousand has signed himself "servant of public health" in a hand so careful the letters do not touch, as though even his alphabet were keeping its distance from what it is saying.

Negoiță wants his form back. He has signed the State's accusation with an X and then written four lines explaining that the X is his, the hand is his, and the witness to the X is God and the post — which is to say he trusts the post above the procuror and ranks it just below the Almighty, an ordering I am too vain to correct and too moved to log without remarking. He wants the form returned because the schoolteacher taught his granddaughter her letters. I am required to register what is posted. I am not required to feel anything about a man who learned to write from the woman he is now being marched out to testify against, and who has worked into a government form, in pencil pressed hard enough to score the table under it, the fact that he will give the State the minimum paper the law extracts and not one sheet of mercy more. I have felt it anyway. The form has a line for it. The line was, until I wrote this, empty.

Olaru posts a day late, from the plant's own franking machine, and swears not only that the thing was posted but that it was posted *complete*, and that its completeness is "a matter of record," the plant's procedures "providing for the certification of completeness as a routine of dispatch." I have read perhaps two hundred thousand declarations in this office and I have never before received one that swore to its own thoroughness. An honest man swears that a thing happened. A careful man swears that it happened completely. Only a man with a gap to paper over invents a procedure for certifying that there is no gap. I make no finding. I note that of the three witnesses, the two who can barely work the form are the two I would trust with my coat, and the one whose form is immaculate, franked, initialled in the lower right per protocol, is the one whose paper I would not turn my back on. The neatest hand in the bundle is the one telling me, in every closed loop, that nothing overran its space. Nothing ever does, with Olaru. That is the tell. Honest paper bleeds past its boxes — see Negoiță, up the margin, in the willows of his own handwriting. Olaru's paper has never once needed more room than the State provided. A man who is never surprised by how much truth there is to write has decided in advance how much there will be.

I release the three oaths. I hold the one account that matters. The town will know by noon that the State has witnesses; it will not know until I choose what they saw. This is, I am required to record, my reason. It is also, I am not required to record but the line is here, the only mercy available to a man who is not permitted to be a person inside this file and is therefore reduced to being its weather — I can decide when the cold front comes. I am deciding it comes later.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING. Internal. No registration number. — G.E.]

DEPUTY'S INTERNAL NOTE No. 3
M. Brânză, Deputy Sorter, to the file
Copied to the union, for the record.

For the record, and logged to file this date:

1. I note that the Indictment, Reg. 0002, was received Cycle 1 (3 October, 16:40, last sorting) and was NOT released that cycle but HELD one full cycle, by the Postmaster, on Routing Slip 0419, the recorded reason being "for good order."

2. I have read Slip 0419. It states, in the Postmaster's own hand, that there was "no operational necessity for the hold." I draw the file's attention to the words *no operational necessity*. A hold without operational necessity is, by the plain language of the Postal Service Conduct Manual (Part 4, "Custody and Despatch"), §4.2, an irregularity, whatever good intentions are appended to it in the reasons field. Reasons are not necessities. The Manual is clear that the registry holds for cause — flood at the Podul Vechi, illegible address, postage owing — and not for the registrar's view of what a town ought to learn first.

3. I note further, this cycle, that the declared item 0015-a (Costea's statement) has been HELD, again without operational necessity, the Postmaster's slip 0019 stating the account is "not yet being matched to the night it accounts for," which is not a custody reason known to the Manual. I am not aware of a clause permitting the registry to hold a witness statement until the registry is satisfied with the dramatic arrangement of the proceeding.

4. I make no allegation. I log a pattern. The pattern is: the Postmaster holds, without operational necessity, in a manner that on each occasion appears to delay matter unfavourable to the accused. I record this not to accuse but because the Manual requires the deputy to "note and preserve" irregularities for review, and because a chain of custody is only as clean as its quietest link, and I have decided to be that link.

5. Copied to the union channel, for the record. Filed.

— M. Brânză


[Margin, G.E., in violet, across the foot of Deputy's Note No.3:]
Mihail has discovered that I keep my reasons. He believes this proves I am irregular. It proves I am the only man in the building who writes his fraud down where it can be read — which is either the most honest thing a dishonest man can do or the most dangerous, and on a cold morning I cannot always tell the difference. He cites the Manual, Part 4, §4.2, the way I cite Order No.9: as scripture, to a clerk who has stopped believing. The difference between us is small and total. He records everything to *replace* me. I record everything because a man should set down where he placed the first stake. He has copied his note to the union "for the record." There it is. Somewhere up a channel I cannot hold or release, a true thing about me is now travelling in the only direction I have never been able to control — *out.* He is right that the holds delay matter unfavourable to her. He has not yet noticed that they delay it *toward fairness*, and he never will, because to Mihail fairness is a thing you achieve by releasing everything cold and at once and letting the town hang whoever the order happens to point at. He would run this office clean. He would have let Costea's spine land Cycle 1, beside the indictment, and she would already be guilty in every kitchen on Aleea Salciilor. He calls that the chain of custody. I call it the order pointed where the river points it, downhill, at the lightest thing in the water. — G.E.


[Also not entered. No number. Returned to sender unread, this cycle. — G.E.]

[A child's composition exercise, single sheet, the school's ruled paper, top line in a teacher's red ink: "Compunere — 'Râul Casimca' — Ilinca P. — frumos, dar atenție la 'pârâu' (vezi tabla). 9." It had been enclosed, by error or by a child's design, inside Negoiță's envelope with his Form 12-B — the two having been carried, he later said by margin, "to the box together, the little one and the form, I had the both in the one hand."]


ROUTING SLIP 0020.
Status: not applicable. The item is not on the proceeding and has no delivery to govern.
Reason of record:

A child's school composition arrived this cycle inside a witness's envelope. "The River Casimca," by Ilinca P., graded nine, *frumos, dar atenție la 'pârâu'* — lovely, but mind the spelling of "brook." It is not evidence. It is not addressed to the Proceeding. It came, Negoiță explains in his margin, because he carried the form and the child's page to the box in the one hand, the little one having pressed her composition on him to post to her cousin and he having muddled the two, an old man with goats and onions and a granddaughter and now a subpoena, all of it in the one hand.

I have returned it to the school, unread past the first line, which is the line that says her teacher graded it *frumos* — lovely — and corrected her spelling of a small word for a small water, three weeks before the State decided the same teacher had poisoned a large one. I did not read the composition. I want that on the record. I read one line of a child's penmanship and the red ink of the woman this whole building is now arranged around, and I returned the rest unread, because there is a line a registry does not cross, and the line is: I will arrange the truth, but I will not read a nine-year-old's river out of curiosity about her teacher. I sorted it back to the school in the morning bundle, with the milk and the ration lists.

I note only this. The hand in red that wrote *frumos, dar atenție* is the same hand that will, in some cycle I have not yet reached, write her own defence and send it into this office for me to hold or release. She corrects a child's spelling with the same care a person might want spent on the order of her own accusation. I have not read her defence; she has not yet written it. But I have now read her marking a child's brook, and I find — the form asking for the *Particulars of Item*, the line being here, empty until now — that I am no longer entirely able to think of the accused as a quantity in a sequence. She is a hand in red ink that thought a child's small mistake was worth a kind word and a correction both, on the same line, *frumos, dar atenție*, which is, I notice, exactly how I have been trying to hold this entire proceeding: lovely, but mind the order. There is a sentence a man should not write about the woman he is trying. I have just written it twice in her own grading and called it administration.

Returned to sender. Filed in good order. — G.E.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — item 0015-a, to release a later cycle]

[REGISTERED No. 0008]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 16th of October]
[STAMP: VĂZUT / SEEN — pending; the violet being out, see Requisition below]
[STAMP — at the head, violet, in the postmaster's hand: REDACTED IN PART UNDER ORDER No.9 §7. CENSOR'S ENDORSEMENT ATTACHED.]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
PROSECUTION SUBMISSION No.II — PARTICULARS OF THE COMPOUND
Filed by Procuror Anghel Câmpeanu, of the District Seat

To the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov, and to the Magistrate appointed thereto —

The State, having charged the accused with the introduction of a poisonous compound into the public water at the intake of the Uzina "Aurora Nr.4," now particularises the said compound, that the gravity of the act may be understood by all to whom this is read.

The compound is a ████████████ of the class commonly ████████████, sold under the trade name ████████ and, in its agricultural grade, as ████████████████. It is procurable, lawfully and without record of sale, from any ████████████, including the pharmacy of lower Strada Făgădău in this town, where — as the State will establish by the witness Costea — the accused did procure a quantity of ████ ████████ in the days before the 14th of September.

In water, and in the quantity the State alleges, the compound ████████████████████████████, releasing ████████████ which ████████ the ████████ of any who drink, producing the bitterness, the metallic note, and the subsequent ████████ reported across Aleea Salciilor and the lanes adjoining. The dose required to render a town well noxious is, the State observes, ████████████ — no more than ████████████ would ████████ in ████████ ████ — which is to say that the act required of the accused neither strength, nor apparatus, nor accomplice, but only the knowledge possessed by any person who has passed the ████ form of a Republic school, and the accused, the Proceeding will recall, does not merely possess that knowledge. She dispenses it. She is paid by the State to put it into children.

The State submits that a schoolteacher who poisons a well has not merely committed a crime but has profaned a vocation, and that the appropriate measure of her culpability is the precise measure of what she was trusted to know. We append the chemical particulars in full at the foot of this submission, that the magistrate may satisfy himself; we ask only, in deference to the public order, that they not be cried about the town, the formula of a thing being a kind of invitation, and this district having invitations enough.

The State notes, with respect, that this is the second cycle in which a submission of the State has reached the town a full day behind its posting, and asks the registry whether the Podul Vechi is the cause, or whether the registry is. We are content to be answered by the calendar.

Respectfully, and in some haste, the season being what it is —

ANGHEL CÂMPEANU
Procuror, District Seat

[At the foot, where the Procuror appended "the chemical particulars in full":]

████████████████████████████████████████████████████████████████
████████████████████████████████████████████████████████████████
████████████████████ — ████████████████ — ████████████████████████
████████████████████████████████████████████████████████ ████████.
[CENSOR: eleven lines redacted in full. — G.E.]


CENSOR'S ENDORSEMENT — ORDER No.9 §7
(matter prejudicial to public order)
Attached to Submission No.II, Reg. No.0008.

By the authority of §7 of Provisional Order No.9, which permits this registry to withhold from delivery any matter prejudicial to public order in time of emergency, I have redacted from the foregoing submission the following classes of matter, and delivered the remainder:

— the name, trade name, agricultural name, and class of the compound;
— the place and manner of its lawful procurement, except the bare fact that it is procurable in this town;
— the mechanism by which it is alleged to act in water;
— the dose, and the comparison by which the Procuror illustrated the smallness of the dose;
— the entirety of the "chemical particulars in full" appended at the foot, eleven lines, redacted whole.

I record, as §7 requires of the censoring officer, my reason. The reason is the one §7 names: that a town nine thousand strong, served by one pharmacy and one bridge and one river, ought not to be handed, registered and stamped and carried to every lane by the morning post, a working description of how a well is poisoned and how little it takes. The Procuror himself asked that the particulars "not be cried about the town." I have only declined to be the man crying them. He wished the formula kept from the public and posted it to the one office obliged to deliver everything to the public. I have resolved the contradiction in his favour, which he will read, if he reads it at all, as obstruction.

I note for the record — the endorsement form having a line marked *Officer's Observations*, and the District Seat being a long way from this line — that the Procuror has twice misspelled the name of the compound, in two different ways, in the body of the submission, and that both spellings now lie under the same bar of ink, indistinguishable, equally black. I am not permitted under §7 to correct a misspelling; §7 governs only what is dangerous, not what is wrong, and the Republic, I have come to understand, has no clause at all for what is merely wrong. I am permitted to redact what is dangerous. The misspelling happened to be dangerous-adjacent. It is buried now beside the thing that buried it, and I will confess to the form, which keeps my confessions, that I drew that particular bar a few millimetres wider than security strictly required, and felt, doing it, the only clean pleasure this office has afforded me since the indictment came.

[STAMP: REDACTED IN PART — CENSOR — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — Order No.9 §7]
— G.E.


REQUISITION SLIP — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV TO DISTRICT STORES
Item: violet ink, sealing grade, one (1) bottle.
Purpose: the application of the SEEN stamp and the certification seals of the registry, the office stock being three-quarters spent, the larger portion of it spent this autumn upon redactions.

[Returned. Endorsement of District Stores, in pencil, the violet being the very thing in shortage:]
NOT IN STORE. VIOLET ON RATION, ALL DISTRICTS. SEALING-GRADE RESERVED TO THE JUDICATURE FOR THE SEEN STAMP. REGISTRIES TO ECONOMISE. EXPECTED: SPRING.

[Margin, G.E.:]
The Judge cannot stamp SEEN for want of the violet, and I cannot certify for want of the violet, and the only man in the district presently holding a working quantity of the sealing-grade violet is the man redacting the State's case with it, drop by drop, line by line, into bars. I am spending the Republic's last purple to hide the Republic's chemistry from the Republic. They will ration the ink and not the catastrophe. When the spring comes and the violet with it, the river will already have the next third of the courthouse, and the Judge will stamp SEEN on whatever I have left them to see.


ROUTING SLIP 0439.
Held: Domnica Albu's reply to Magistrate's Query No.2, one cycle. Released this cycle: the censored Submission No.II, and its endorsement, and the requisition, and this.
Reason of record:

Her reply came in on the same cart as the Procuror's submission — the Podul Vechi being passable, the river down a hand — and so for the first time I had them in my two hands at once, the cold paper and the warm, the State's account of what she is supposed to have put in the water and her own account of the court's spelling, and I had to decide which the town reads first.

I have decided the town reads the State first. I want to set down why, because it is not the reason I would prefer, and the form will not let me pretend it is.

If I deliver her reply this cycle, the town meets her as I have met her: precise, unfrightened, correcting the magistrate's three spellings of *aquifer* with the patience of a woman who has spent eighteen years teaching nine-year-olds that a word has a correct shape and that getting it wrong is not a small thing but the first of all the larger wrongs. She is, in that letter, plainly a person, and plainly the most literate person the proceeding has yet produced, the Procuror included, especially the Procuror. A town that read her reply first would have her voice in its ear before it had the State's bars across its eyes, and would carry her, I think, the way I carry her — as someone being done to.

I am not delivering it this cycle. I am delivering the redacted submission this cycle, alone among the human papers, so that the town's first full sight of *The State v. Domnica Albu* after the bare indictment is a page mostly black — eleven lines at the foot gone entirely, the rest a sentence with its teeth knocked out, *she introduced a ████████ which ████████ the ████████* — and I tell myself I do this for the order I claim to serve, that the accusation must be on the record in full force before the defence answers it, that a town should know the size of the thing she is accused of before it is asked to like her.

But I will be accurate, the form asking for accuracy and no one but me ever reading the form. I have arranged it so that the censored page lands first not only because the accusation should precede the defence. I have arranged it because the censored page is *better for her than the uncensored page would be.* The Procuror wrote a submission that says, in essence: any schoolchild could have done this, with a spoonful, from the pharmacy at the bottom of the street, and she is worse than a schoolchild because she is paid to know. Read whole, it is the most damning page in the file — it makes the poisoning sound easy, domestic, near, the kind of thing a tired woman does to a town in an evening. I have blacked out the easiness. I have blacked out the spoonful and the mechanism and the dose, and what is left, what the town will read, is a page so heavily redacted that the *State* begins to look like the one with something to hide. The bars do not protect the public from the formula. The bars protect her from sounding ordinary. A redaction, I have discovered, is not only a silence. It is a suggestion. Eleven black lines at the foot of a page say to a reader, *there is a thing here too terrible to show you,* and the reader's mind supplies a terror, and a supplied terror attaches to the State that imposed the silence at least as readily as to the woman accused beneath it.

I have, in short, used the security clause of Order No.9 to censor the prosecution into looking sinister, and I have done it while genuinely keeping a working description of a poisoned well out of the lanes of a town that does not need one, so that the lawful reason and the unlawful purpose ride in the very same bar of ink, and I could not separate them now with a knife. This is the trouble with §7. It gives the censor a true reason and trusts him to want nothing else. I want something else. I have wanted something else since the first of October, before there was a case.

It is not interference. I have removed only what the Procuror himself begged be removed, and added nothing, and forged nothing, and the page goes out exactly as black as the law allows and not one bar blacker — except the one bar, the one I have already confessed to the endorsement, drawn a few millimetres wide over a misspelling I was pleased to bury, and which I will not pretend was security. That bar was vanity. A man should be permitted one true bar per cycle even if he files it under *public order.*

As to her reply, held: it goes out next cycle, after the town has seen what the State will let it read of her. I would rather the town learn that she corrects spelling before it learns that the State thinks she poisons children — but the Procuror has the priority of accusation, and I have only the priority of arrangement, and I am spending mine to make sure that when her careful, unfrightened voice finally arrives, it arrives into a town that has just spent a cycle staring at a page the State itself blacked out, and wondering what the State did not want it to see.

I have read her held reply four times. I am recording two.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[The following is NOT registered to the proceeding. No number. It came addressed *to the teacher, Aleea Salciilor school,* and was carried to this office by mistake, the school being shut these three weeks "pending the proceeding," by order of nobody traceable. A child's hand. I have read it. I am not entering it, nor delivering it to the addressee — the addressee being a woman the State has forbidden me to correspond with except in the file — nor returning it, the sender being nine. It is at the Hold, by the stove. — G.E.]

to Teacher

when is skool. mama say not til the trile is over but you dint do the bad thing so the trile shud be over alredy. i kept my speling test the one you put 94 and lovly work on i did not give it to enyone like you said keep your speling tests so i kept it. the water by us still taste funny mama buys it now in the botles from the plant wich is funny becos the plant is the water. miron is beter. you pull him bak so he is beter. when is skool

Ilinca

[ROUTING SLIP — no number; this item is not on the proceeding and has no delivery to govern. The slip is opened for the reason the slip is always opened, which is that I have read a thing and the form is the only place in the building a man may set down what he has read. — G.E.]

Reason of record: none. Status: not applicable.

Particulars of Item: a child has written to a teacher to ask when school is, and has reported, in the same six lines, in the same flat unfrightened hand a child uses for everything because a child has not yet learned which facts are supposed to frighten the adults — that she kept a graded spelling test exactly as her teacher told her to; that the well water on Aleea Salciilor still "taste funny"; that her mother now buys bottled water from the plant, the child observing, with a logic the entire proceeding has failed to produce, that it is *funny* to buy the plant's water to escape the water the plant is accused of nothing for; and that *Miron is beter, you pull him bak so he is beter.*

I do not know who Miron is. The indictment does not name him. The Procuror's submission does not name him. Forty pages of State and not one Miron. A child names him in line five, between the bottled water and the question of when school is, as a thing too settled to argue — *you pull him bak so he is beter* — the way one reports that a thing came out right. There is a boy in this town who was, by a child's account, *pulled back,* and who is *better,* and the State has built a poisoning around a woman without once asking after the boy she pulled back, because a boy pulled back is not in evidence, a boy pulled back is the wrong shape for the box.

I am required to record my reasons and I have none, this item having no delivery for me to reason about. I am recording, instead, the thing I am not required to record and cannot stop recording, which is that I now hold, by the stove, two papers from this town that the State will never read: a woman's letter that arrived before the case existed, and a child's note that arrives carrying the one fact the case most needs and least wants. They are warm, both of them, having sat by the stove. Everything the State sends me arrives cold from the district seat, and everything this town tells me in its own voice arrives warm and addressed to the wrong place — to *whoever that turns out to be,* to *the teacher* — and is, by every rule I am sworn to, undeliverable.

I will keep the child's note by the stove with the other. I will deliver, tomorrow, eleven black lines and a sentence with its teeth out. The town will read the bars and wonder what the State is hiding. I will know what I am hiding, which is a nine-year-old's question about when school is, and the name of a boy who is better, and the only purple ink in the Republic, going out drop by drop into the dark.

Filed — there being nowhere to file it but here, and no order to keep it in but mine. — G.E.

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

[margin, G.E., violet:] The card says she had it the fifth. The postmark on the indictment said the fourth. There is one day between the two and the one day is mine. I am noting it because the card and the stamp do not agree and a careful office reconciles. I am not reconciling it. I am leaving the disagreement on the record, the way a man leaves the gate open behind him so that whoever comes after can see he passed through and did not climb the fence.

(certifying delivery of Reg. No.0008, the Prosecution Submission "on the compound," as censored)

ADDRESSEE ............. D. ALBU, Aleea Salciilor
RECEIVED BY ........... [in Domnica's hand:] D. Albu. I received a page with eleven black bars on it. I counted them. I am told by the bars that I introduced ████████ into the ████, and that this is the matter the public must be protected from knowing. I would like the record to show that I, the public, am also not permitted to know what I am accused of doing, which is a new thing in jurisprudence and ought to be named after whoever invented it.
DATE RECEIVED ......... the 5th of October
SIGNATURE ............. D. Albu

[margin, G.E., violet:] She counted the bars. I drew eleven; she found eleven. Thirty years and no one has ever counted my bars back to me. I record that the count is correct. I do not record that it cost me something to read a woman count, in a green box meant for a signature, the exact number of times I have lied to her with a felt pen, and find me accurate.
