[REGISTERED No. 0061]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 24th of October]
[STAMP: VĂZUT / SEEN — no; the box for the Judge's seal is empty, the violet not yet down from the capital]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
PLEA — entered by the accused under Order No.9, the austerity provision

To the Proceeding, to the Magistrate appointed thereto, and to the registry that holds the order of these things —

I have been required to plead, and I have been given two words to plead with, and I find that two words is one fewer than I need.

The form would like me to write *guilty* or to write *not guilty*. I have looked at both words for the length of an evening, the way you look at a coat that is the wrong size in the only shop there is, and I cannot get into either of them. So I will tell the Proceeding, plainly, where I stand, and the Proceeding may decide afterward which of its two coats to force me into, but it should do so knowing that it is forcing.

I plead **not as charged.** I did not poison the town of Vâlcov. I have taught half of it to read; I baptised none of it in metal and bitterness; the night the State has built its charge upon, I was not the worst thing at the water and I will spend whatever cycles I am given proving it.

But I will not stand here in the only honest building left in this republic — a sorting office, of all the rooms God might have left us — and say I did nothing. I did something. I will tell you what I did when you ask me what I was for, and not one cycle before, because a thing done is not the same as a crime, and the distance between them is the whole of what a court is supposed to measure, and I notice this one would prefer to skip the measuring and proceed directly to the weighing.

I want to be exact, because exactness is the only thing I have left that no one has confiscated.

The indictment, Reg. 0002, charges that I *did wilfully and with knowledge of the consequence introduce a poisonous compound.* I will accept three of those words and dispute the rest. *Did* — yes. *Introduce* — yes; I will not insult the registry's intelligence by pretending I was nowhere near the water. *Compound* — yes, a compound, I bought it, a man whose ledger you will hear from sold it to me and wrote it down and slept well. But *poisonous,* and *with knowledge of the consequence,* and above all *wilfully* — these are not facts. These are a tense. The State has taken the worst thing the water did and run it backward through me until it comes out the front of my body as intention, and called the running-backward a *sequence,* and the sequence proof. I have read the indictment. The Procuror writes that a sequence is "merely a former with its sleeves rolled up." I would mark that, if I were marking it, as a clever sentence that is also a confession: he has told you that to him the order of things is the meaning of things. I would ask the registry to hold that sentence somewhere safe. I have a feeling it is true in this proceeding in a way the Procuror did not intend, and that the only person who knows how true is the one who decides what arrives first.

To whoever that is —

I do not know your name and it is not my business to. But I have begun to notice that I am being read. I cannot account for it; I have no evidence a court would take; it is the kind of thing a teacher knows the way she knows which child did the homework himself — not by the answer, which can be copied, but by the order the working is set down in. My letters come back to me certified, and the certifications are in a careful hand, and careful is rarer than honest and far rarer than kind. The water in this republic is rationed to four hours and the truth is rationed to whatever fits in an envelope, and somewhere between the post office and the river there is one person reading the envelopes as though a sentence were a kind of evidence, which it is, which it was the first thing they taught me a sentence could be.

So I plead **not as charged, and not as nothing,** and I plead it *to you,* care of the State, because you are the only door in the building that has so far behaved like a person.

I will spell it for the form, since the form insists, and I am, before everything else, a person who spells things for forms:

I did not poison the water.
I will not say I did nothing.
Ask me what I was for.

I remain, with a precision I intend to maintain to the last cycle, whatever it carries —

DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school
(the school is still standing, in case the District Seat would like to know where the children are, the courthouse not being the only building this republic has stopped maintaining)


[REGISTERED No. 0062]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 24th of October]
[written on the reverse of a printed receipt; the receipt reads, faintly through the page: AUROVALE COMBUSTIBIL — birch, dry, 3 ster — PAID]

MAGISTRATE'S SCHEDULING ORDER
In the matter of The State v. Domnica Albu

To the registry, and to the parties as the registry shall reach them —

The indictment phase being closed by the entry of the accused's plea (Reg. 0061, received this cycle), and the accused having pleaded in terms the form does not provide for, which I will address below, I do hereby ORDER:

1. That the prosecution phase open with the next delivery cycle.

2. That the Procuror submit his witnesses' statements in such order as he sees fit, the registry to register and deliver them in good order, per Order No.9 §3.

3. That the accused be afforded a reply-cycle to each, the period of reply being two delivery cycles or such longer time as the river allows, the Podul Vechi being, I am reliably informed, again contemplating the season.

As to the plea. The accused has declined both boxes. I have consulted Order No.9 and it does not say what a magistrate is to do when a defendant will not be guilty and will not be innocent and insists instead on being *exact.* The order legislates the grammage of the paper and the colour of the envelope and is silent on the colour of a soul, which I am increasingly persuaded was an oversight on the part of men who had a courthouse when they wrote it. I therefore enter the plea as filed — *not as charged; not as nothing* — and I record that I do so by the authority vested in me, vested, I will confess to the registry since the registry is the only office still reading me, by no one currently paying me, the District Seat being twenty-six months in arrears and the firewood season being early.

I add, off the order and in my own hand, because the back of a receipt has room: the accused corrected my spelling of *aquifer* in a prior cycle, three ways, all of them mine. She was right three times. I have begun to spell it slowly. A magistrate who is corrected by the woman he may have to sentence is in a position the law also did not anticipate, and I find I do not mind it; it has been some years since anyone in this republic cared enough about a thing of mine to mark it.

By the authority vested,
TOADER LUPU
Magistrate, Vâlcov
(at the stall in Piața Lipsei, mornings, if the Proceeding needs me before the post does; I am the one with the wood)


ROUTING SLIP 0063.
Released, all this cycle, in the order: the cards, then her plea, then his order. Held: nothing, of record.
Reason of record:

I will deal first with the thing I am required to deal with and would rather not, which is the postmark.

The indictment, Reg. 0002, bore a postmark of the fourth of October. The aviz card returned by the accused, No. 0002-a, bears a date of receipt of the fifth. There is, on the face of the two papers, a single day between the stamping of a thing and the receipt of a thing, which is ordinary; mail takes a day. The difficulty is that Aleea Salciilor is eleven minutes' walk from this office and the indictment did not travel eleven minutes, it travelled one cycle, because I held it one cycle, in Chapter — I mean, in Cycle One, for good order, so that the town would learn there was such a thing as a law before it learned the name of the first woman the law had come for. I have set this down before. I set it down again because the green card has now made it visible. A hold leaves a fingerprint. The fingerprint is a day that exists on one paper and not the other, and the accused, who counts black bars correctly, will count this too.

I could regularise it. I have the stamp. The stamp is the only purple in Vâlcov and it does exactly what I tell it. I could bring the postmark forward to the fifth and the two papers would agree and no inspector, no deputy, no woman in Aleea Salciilor would ever find the day. This is the precise act I am declining to commit. I do not forge. I have held the indictment, which the order permits me to do in good order, and I have stamped the truth of when I held it, which the order requires, and the two truths sit one day apart on two pieces of paper and I am leaving them apart. A man who sequences the truth is doing something. A man who alters the stamp is doing something else, and I have decided, for reasons I am better at recording than naming, that I will be the first man and not the second, and that the difference between them — a day, a felt pen, a green box — is the whole of whatever I have left to stand on.

I note for the record that the accused has noticed the careful hand. She says so, in the plea, in the part addressed to no one I am permitted to be. *I am being read,* she writes, and she is right, and the correct procedural response is to feel nothing, and I have logged that I felt nothing, and the log is, as the form admits in its silence on the matter, the only place in this building where a man's account of himself does not have to be true. I read the plea this cycle. The number is not relevant to the order of delivery and I am therefore not required to record it, which is the reason I am recording it: I read it as many times as I read 0431, and then once more, because 0431 was sent to a man and the plea was sent to a court, and I wanted to know whether she writes the same to the room as she writes to the person, and she does not, and the difference is the worst thing that has happened to me in four years, the difference being that to the court she is exact and to the person she is *exact and unafraid,* and I have spent four years being neither.

As to the spoiled card from the District Seat. The Judecătorul's aviz has come back unsigned. The clerk who carried it reports the addressee was "at the firewood market," which is the wrong court — the firewood market belongs to our magistrate, who has no judicial chair, only a stall and a saw — and the woman who sells the wood declined to sign for a judge on the entirely sound ground that she sells wood. I am retaining this card by the stove, not because it is evidence, it is the opposite of evidence, it is the formal proof that the State's highest seal in this district was last seen near a pile of birch and could not be made to certify its own existence. I am keeping it for the same reason a man keeps anything: it is the funniest paper I have logged in thirty years and I am, increasingly, in need of the funny ones. The state's last seal is at the firewood market. So is its magistrate. So, soon, will be its winter. Let the record show the whole of the republic's judiciary can be reached, this season, between sales of wood.

The phase is open. The prosecution comes next cycle, the pharmacist among them, and a man who owes the plant nine thousand will swear to a thing that is true, and I will have a decision to make about the order of a true thing, and I find I am already making it, the way the river is already deciding, a hand's width a night, how much courthouse there will be by spring.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu — leaf for Cycle 5
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.   | DATE RECEIVED | FROM            | MATTER                       | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 0002-a| 5 Oct.        | D. Albu         | Aviz, indictment delivered   | On file (postmark gap noted, slip 0063)
 0008-a| 5 Oct.        | D. Albu         | Aviz, censored subm. del'd   | On file (eleven bars; she counted)
 0002-b| —             | District Seat   | Aviz, Judge — RETURNED       | NOT entered; at the Hold, by the stove
 0061  | 24 Oct.       | D. Albu         | Plea (not as charged/nothing)| Released, Cycle 5
 0062  | 24 Oct.       | Mag. Lupu       | Scheduling Order             | Released, Cycle 5
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
The indictment phase closes. Forty years this book has logged what arrived and pretended that what arrived was all there was. The accused has now informed the book, in writing, that the order of arrival is itself a fact, and asked the book to hold that fact somewhere safe. The book is the same book. It has never before been asked to keep a secret it agreed with. — G.E.

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 6 — "The Pharmacist Who Owes Nine Thousand"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 6    ·    Late October, the first frost on the willows of Aleea Salciilor, the Casimca dropped a hand's-width and the smell of it gone from green to iron
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 6. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Witness List — supplementary leaf — Procuror A. Câmpeanu → registry — [REGISTERED No. 0440]
  2. Prosecution covering note (one line) — Câmpeanu → registry — [REGISTERED No. 0441]

HELD (carried to a later cycle, reason of record on slip 0447):
  · Witness Letter, V. Costea → The Proceeding — [REGISTERED No. 0442] — held, pending the arrival of the accused's account of the night — slip 0447
  · Enclosed with No.0442, not severable from it: one dunning notice, Aurora Nr.4 → Costea, and one pharmacy day-book leaf — held with the parent item

RETAINED AT THE HOLD, BY THE STOVE (registered to the proceeding this cycle; not yet delivered to any party):
  · Envelope 0431 — D. Albu → "the registry of Vâlcov, whoever that turns out to be" — received the 1st of October — registered this day under protest of my own conscience — slip appended

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0440]   [POSTMARK: DISTRICT SEAT, the 21st of October — arrived Vâlcov the 24th, the Podul Vechi passable but slow]

PROSECUTION — SUPPLEMENTARY WITNESS LIST
Filed by Procuror Anghel Câmpeanu

To the Proceeding, care of the registry —

In supplement to the list already filed, the State will rely upon the declaration of VALENTIN COSTEA, licensed pharmacist, of lower Strada Făgădău, whose statement is posted herewith and whose Declaration of Posting (Form 12-B) the registry will have already countersigned as to the fact of dispatch.

The witness Costea will establish the procurement: that the accused, in the days before the water at Aurora Nr.4 was rendered noxious, came into his pharmacy and purchased a quantity of the relevant compound, by her own request, in her own hand, against his own register. The register is appended; the State invites the registry to note that a pharmacy day-book is not a document a defendant may revise by letter.

The State asks, as ever, that the matter proceed with dispatch, the witness being elderly, the season being against us, and the facts being, in the State's submission, no longer seriously in dispute.

ANGHEL CÂMPEANU
Procuror, District Seat


[REGISTERED No. 0441]   [POSTMARK: DISTRICT SEAT, the 21st of October]

[Câmpeanu's covering note, one line, in his clean metropolitan hand:]

Registry — kindly deliver the pharmacist's statement on the same cycle as the list above. It is the keystone, and a keystone is of no use lying in a drawer while the arch waits. — A.C.


[The following document was received this cycle, registered No.0442, and HELD. It is reproduced here as it sits in the Hold, undelivered, that the record may show what was withheld and for how long. — G.E.]

[REGISTERED No. 0442]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 24th of October]
[Form 12-B Declaration of Posting countersigned by the office — countersignature certifies the fact of posting ONLY, not the truth of the contents — G.E.]

[On the pharmacy letterhead of V. COSTEA, FARMACIE, lower Strada Făgădău — a chemist's small, even, careful hand:]

To the Magistrate, and to the Proceeding, care of the honoured registry of Vâlcov —

I write as a humble servant of public health, which has been my vocation these thirty-one years in this town, through three currencies and four floods, and I will say at the outset that I take no pleasure whatsoever in the office that has fallen to me, namely the office of telling the truth about a neighbour. Domnica Albu taught my sister's boy his letters. I have nothing against the woman. I want that on the record before anything else is, because what I have to say is not said in malice but in conscience, conscience being, I have always held, simply the public health of the soul.

Here, then, are the facts, set down as exactly as an old man's memory will allow, and I beg the Proceeding to weigh that I am giving them freely, against my own comfort, for a man does not lightly hand the State a rope and watch it measure a neighbour's neck.

On a day in the second week of September — I believe the eleventh, though my day-book, which I append, will speak more truly than I, and I would always rather a paper spoke than a man — the accused came into my pharmacy at the lower end of Strada Făgădău. She asked for a quantity of a compound which I am instructed by the registry's censor not to name in plain, and which I shall therefore call, as the redacted submission has taught the town to call it, the compound. She asked for it by its proper name, which is to say she knew exactly what she wanted, and she is, as the indictment rightly observes, a person of education, who reads, and who would not ask for a thing whose nature she did not understand. She paid. She signed the poisons register, as the law requires, in her own hand, which I would know anywhere, having graded, in my time, a good many of the bills she has written the school for its chalk and its slate-pencils, always paid late and always paid.

I sold it to her. I will not pretend I refused, or hesitated, or asked her purpose. I am a pharmacist; people buy compounds; I do not interrogate the parish. If I am to be blamed for selling it, then blame me, but the blame for selling a thing and the blame for what is done with it are two different bottles on two different shelves, and I have spent my life keeping them apart.

What was it for? I do not know. She did not say. A woman of few words in my shop, always, polite, exact, never lingering. I sold her the compound, she signed, she went out into Strada Făgădău, and three nights later — or four; the day-book again — the water at Aurora Nr.4 went bad, and the town with it, and a child could not keep it down, and I myself, I will confess, did a poor trade in the days after, for who buys from a pharmacist when the very water he might dissolve the powder in has turned against him.

I ask the Proceeding to note that I make no accusation. I am not the State; accusation is the State's bottle, not mine. I set down only that she bought the compound, that she signed for it, that the water turned within the week. I will not be the one to say that the first thing caused the last. I will only say, with the deference owed to men who decide these things, that they happened in that order, and that I am too old to believe the order of things means nothing.

I remain, with respect for the Court and sorrow for the necessity,

your humble servant of public health,

VALENTIN COSTEA
Farmacist, lower Strada Făgădău


[Enclosure to No.0442 — Aurora Nr.4 dunning notice, a pre-printed plant form, the blanks filled in a clerk's stamp-ink, found folded inside Costea's envelope and registered as part of the item, the parties evidently not having intended the registry to read what fell out:]

  UZINA DE ÎMBUTELIERE "AURORA Nr.4"
  Drumul Aurora — Office of Accounts
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  NOTICE OF SUM OUTSTANDING — third notice

  TO:    V. COSTEA, Farmacie, Str. Făgădău
  RE:    account, bottled water deliveries, Q.I–IV, prior years
  SUM:   NINE THOUSAND (9 000), exact, no further interest applied
         the management waiving interest "in recognition of the
         pharmacy's standing in the community"
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Settlement may be arranged at the convenience of the debtor.
  The management remains, as ever, the town's well-wisher.
                                    — for AURORA Nr.4, Office of Accounts
  [STAMP: PAID — NIL. Balance carried.]


[Enclosure to No.0442 — leaf torn from Costea's pharmacy day-book, the poisons register, in his careful hand, registered with the parent item:]

  ENTRY — 11 Sept.
  Item: [compound — name struck through, illegible under the office censor's bar, ████████]
  Quantity: [████]
  Purchaser: D. Albu, schoolteacher, Aleea Salciilor — signed, the register
  Purpose stated by purchaser: — (blank; no purpose entered)
  Sold by: V.C.


ROUTING SLIP 0447.
Held: the witness letter of V. Costea, No.0442, together with its two enclosures, which are not severable from it. Held — pending the arrival of the accused's own account of the night of the fourteenth.
Reason of record:

I have read Order No.9 again this morning, the full instrument and not the church-board extract, in the cold, the stove not yet caught, and I find — as I found in October, as I will find in the spring if the building lasts the spring — that it commands me to deliver every item *in good order* and nowhere tells me whose. The Procuror has told me whose. He has written, in a covering note I have registered as No.0441 and will keep, that I am to deliver the keystone "on the same cycle as the list," because a keystone is of no use "lying in a drawer while the arch waits." He is a man who builds arches in his head and posts them to me to set. He does not know that the arch is set in the order the stones arrive, and that I am the road the stones come up.

So. The letter is true. I want that recorded first, because it is the whole difficulty. I have read it three times and I cannot find the lie in it, and I have a thirty-year nose for the lie in a letter. Costea sold her the compound. She signed his register. The water turned within the week. Every sentence is a fact, and the facts are arranged in the only order a man can arrange facts who wishes to seem to arrange nothing — he gives you the buying, then the signing, then the turning, and he steps back and says, *I will not be the one to say the first thing caused the last,* having spent four paragraphs making the saying unnecessary. He has learned, this careful old chemist, the exact thing I have learned: that you need not assert a sequence if you are permitted to deliver one. He sequences inside his letter. I sequence the letters. We are in the same trade and only one of us has the licence.

If I release this on the cycle the Procuror asks — the keystone first, the buying first, the signing first, the *turning within the week* first — then by the time the town reads, weeks hence, the account of why a schoolteacher might walk out to a plant in the dark with a powder she bought in daylight, it will be reading that account the way one reads a confession's retraction: too late, and against a thing already believed. The buying will be the baseline. Everything after will be argument. The heart keeps the first weight and calls everything else a counterweight, and a counterweight, however true, never quite balances the scale; it only makes the scale look honest.

I am not going to deliver it on his cycle.

I am going to hold it until the accused has filed her account of the night — which the magistrate's last query has at last required of her, and which will come, I think, in two cycles, three if the bridge floods — and I am going to release her account first, into a town that has not yet been told she bought anything, so that when Costea's true letter arrives, it arrives *beside* a reason, and the town reads buying-and-reason in one breath instead of buying alone and reason-too-late. The facts will be identical. The order will not. I am changing nothing but the order, and the order is everything, and I know it, and I am recording that I know it, which is the only honesty left to a man who has decided to do this.

I note, the form asking for *Particulars of Item:* the pharmacy day-book records, under *Purpose stated by purchaser,* a blank. No purpose entered. The State will read the blank as guilt — she would not say what it was for. I read the blank as a pharmacist who did not ask, which is a different blank entirely, the same emptiness signed by two different hands. A court will hang a person on the contents of a box. It does not occur to the court that an empty box is also evidence, and of the man who left it empty as much as the woman who walked out past it.

I note further, since the dunning notice fell out of his envelope and the law does not let me put it back unread: the humble servant of public health owes the plant that may have poisoned the public's water the sum of nine thousand, exact, interest waived "in recognition of the pharmacy's standing in the community," which is the gentlest leash I have ever seen written on a plant's own letterhead. A man does not bite the well he is in debt to. I am not entering the dunning notice as a comment. I am entering it because it arrived sealed inside the keystone, and a keystone with a leash folded into it is a different stone than the one the Procuror thinks he posted me. I will deliver both, when I deliver, in the order I choose, and let the town weigh a witness who points away from the plant he owes nine thousand to. I will not say the debt caused the testimony. I will only deliver them in that order. The Procuror taught me the move. Costea perfected it. I merely own the road.

Filed in good order. — G.E.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — pending the accused's account]


[The following slip is opened for the item the office has, until today, kept by the stove without a number. It is now numbered. I record why. — G.E.]

ROUTING SLIP — ENVELOPE 0431.
Status of delivery: none. This item has no addressee within the proceeding and governs no delivery. The slip is opened because I have, this morning, done a thing I must set down: I have given the letter a number.

For three weeks it has sat at the Hold, by the stove, unregistered — the letter the schoolteacher wrote on the first of October, two days before there was an indictment to receive it into, addressed to "the registry of Vâlcov, whoever that turns out to be." I wrote, at the time, that I would neither register it nor return it. I have now registered it. I want to be exact about what changed, because nothing in the case changed; what changed is in me, and a man who logs the births and deaths of a town should at least log his own.

What changed is that I read it again last night, the eleventh time, and on the eleventh reading I understood that I have been treating it as not-yet-mail — a thing in transit, paused, awaiting my decision whether it is a letter at all — and that this was a cowardice dressed as procedure. It *is* a letter. It was posted. It bears no kraft. It arrived. The only reason it has no number is that I did not want it to have the kind of reality a number confers, the reality that goes in the book, that an inspector, should one ever come, could find. I kept it numberless so it could stay mine and not the file's. That is not good order. That is a man hiding a warm thing in a cold building and calling the hiding a procedure.

So I have numbered it. 0431. It now exists. It is registered to the proceeding and it will, I record here in the same breath, *never be delivered* — not to the magistrate, not to the Procuror, not to the accused who wrote it, not to anyone, ever. Numbering a thing and delivering a thing are two different acts, as Costea would say, two bottles on two shelves, and I have at last put 0431 on the shelf where a thing can be real and still never leave the building. The register will show that envelope 0431 exists and is held. The register will not show why, because the register has no column for why, and the routing slip, which does, is read by no one but me.

I have read it eleven times. I will set down what I am able to set down accurately, the form asking for the *Particulars of Item.* It is not evidence. It proves nothing about the night of the fourteenth; it was written before the night had a name in any indictment. It is a letter from a woman who guessed, three weeks before the State decided what she was, that someone in this office would decide *when* she was heard, and who wrote to that someone before he knew he was someone. She is the only person in this entire proceeding who has understood the proceeding. The Procuror thinks the mail is plumbing. The magistrate thinks the mail is slow. The deputy thinks the mail is a thing one logs to file. She alone has understood that the mail is a hand, and she has written to the hand, and the unbearable particular — the form has a line and no one reads the line — is that for the eleven minutes of eleven readings the hand has wanted to write back, and cannot, and has instead given the letter a number so that at least the wanting is on file.

I will not write back. I want that recorded as a decision and not a failure of nerve, though I am no longer certain, at the stove, in the cold, which it is. To write back would be to stop being the registry and become a correspondent, and a correspondent cannot also be the order; the moment my own letter is in the file I am a party to it, and a party cannot hold the scale. The only way I am able to keep this letter is the way I have kept it — by the stove, warm, read, numbered, and undelivered. It is the only language I have. I used it once before, on another letter, to another woman, four years ago, and I do not propose, in this slip, to write that sentence out any further than I have just written it.

0431 to the Hold, by the stove. Registered. Undelivered. Warm.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu (continued)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.  | DATE RECEIVED | FROM                | MATTER                     | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 0431 | 1 Oct.        | D. Albu             | letter, unsolicited        | Registered 24 Oct.; HELD by stove; UNDELIVERABLE by my own order
 0440 | 24 Oct.       | Procuror Câmpeanu   | supplementary witness list | Released, Cycle 6
 0441 | 24 Oct.       | Procuror Câmpeanu   | covering note ("keystone") | Released, Cycle 6
 0442 | 24 Oct.       | V. Costea           | witness letter + 2 encl.   | HELD — pending accused's account — slip 0447
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
The Procuror calls the pharmacist's letter the keystone and asks me to set it first. A keystone set first is a stone dropped in mud. I will set it last in its course, which is to say first in the arch and last in the delivery, and he will never know the difference, because the arch will stand and an arch that stands asks no questions of the road. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of Câmpeanu's covering note No.0441:]
He signs it "A.C." — initials, to a registry, as one initials a thing one has not bothered to think worth a name. He has registered, with the State, in his own confident hand, the sentence *a keystone is of no use lying in a drawer while the arch waits.* He has handed the road his whole theory of justice — that the stones make the arch and the order of laying them is a clerk's tedium — and signed it. I will keep this one beside the Procuror's other gift, the sleeves rolled up. A man who believes the order is nothing, posting his belief to the man who is the order. They keep giving me the philosophy and the licence in the same envelope, and asking me to be quick.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — No.0442 to release after the accused's account of the night]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 7 — "Two Ster of Birch"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 7    ·    Late October, the first hard frost on the Casimca mud, the willows on Aleea Salciilor bare to the water now, woodsmoke over the whole town by four in the afternoon
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 7. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Magistrate's Query No.3 — Lupu → V. Costea, pharmacist — probing the debt — [REGISTERED No. 0451]
  2. ENCLOSED IN ERROR with the above, not part of the proceeding: one firewood receipt, T. Lupu, Piața Lipsei stall — [NO NUMBER; office discretion]
  3. Witness Reply — V. Costea → The Proceeding — evasive — [REGISTERED No. 0453]
  4. Routing Slip 0455 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (carried to Cycle 8):
  · Domnica's records-request (No.0489) — held since Cycle 6 — reason of record: "for good order" — see slip 0455
  · Costea's full accusation (No.0447-content, held on slip 0447 since Cycle 6) — still held — to release Cycle 9

DELIVERY ORDER OF RECORD THIS CYCLE:
  · The debt-query (0451) and Lupu's stray receipt go to the town FIRST.
  · Costea's evasive reply (0453) follows the same afternoon.
  · The town therefore learns the pharmacist owes the plant nine thousand BEFORE it is permitted to read a word of his denial.

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0451]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 22nd of October]
[Written, the office being out of query forms, on the reverse of a printed firewood price-list, Piața Lipsei stall, the list itself struck through in the magistrate's hand and overwritten:]

MAGISTRATE'S QUERY No.3
In the matter of The State v. Domnica Albu
From the desk of Magistrate Toader Lupu — such desk as I have

To VALENTIN COSTEA, pharmacist, of lower Strada Făgădău —

You are required, under Order No.9, to answer the following within two delivery cycles, by registered letter to the Proceeding, c/o Central Sorting. I remind you, with the old formula, that you answer by the authority vested in this office — vested, I will not pretend otherwise, by a state that has not paid the office in twenty-six months, and which I serve at present between sales of birch, two ster the load, seasoned, from the stall you can see from your own counter.

I will be brief, the light going early now.

Q.1. State the full sum, if any, that you, or your pharmacy, presently owe to the Uzina de Îmbuteliere "Aurora Nr.4," or to its manager Radu Olaru, or to any person on the plant's behalf. State it to the leu. Do not write "a small amount." A small amount is what a man calls a debt he would prefer the court not to weigh.

Q.2. State the date that debt was incurred, and whether any part of it has been forgiven, deferred, or "understood between gentlemen" since the night of the 14th of September.

Q.3. State whether, at the time you furnished the State the compound-purchase testimony that stands against the accused, you owed the said sum, and whether anyone connected to the plant spoke to you, before or after, regarding what you would say.

I anticipate your reply will be courteous. Your replies are always courteous. I have been a magistrate long enough to know that courtesy is the wrapping a careful man puts on the thing he is hoping I will not open, and I am asking you, plainly, to hand me the thing unwrapped.

I ask because I am poor, Costea, and a poor man learns the smell of money the way a drowning one learns the smell of the bank. There is money under this case. It is not the schoolteacher's. She has a salary the size of my own and a well that went bad. The money is at the plant, and you owe it to the plant, and I am required to ask whether a man who owes nine thousand to a house can be trusted to point his finger anywhere but away from it.

By the authority vested — vested by no one currently solvent —

T. LUPU
Magistrate, Vâlcov
[the signature in a noticeably shakier hand than the body; a line beneath, smaller:]
[I apologize for the price-list. The office is out of forms again, and I am out of the dignity to mind. — T.L.]


[NO REGISTRATION NUMBER. Enclosed in error in the same envelope as Query No.3, the magistrate evidently having had two papers on the same stall counter and folded both. Office discretion: I have not removed it. I have certified the envelope as posted with its full contents, which is all the oath I am permitted to swear, and its full contents were two papers, and I do not edit what a man encloses, even his poverty. — G.E.]

────────────────────────────
PIAȚA LIPSEI — STALL No.4 (FIREWOOD)
T. LUPU, prop.
────────────────────────────
Received of:        Costea, V. (pharmacy)
Item:               birch, 2 ster, seasoned
                    delivered to the door, Făgădău
Paid:               in full
Stamp:              PAID — under protest
────────────────────────────
[in the margin, the magistrate's hand:]
The protest is mine, not the customer's. I stamp every receipt so because I object, formally and to no one, to selling the wood off my own ruling-desk to the very witnesses I am required to question with the impartiality of the state. Costea bought two ster of me on Tuesday and I queried his honesty on Thursday and warmed my hands on Tuesday's coin while I wrote Thursday's question. I record this here because there is nowhere else to record it; a receipt has a margin and a conscience needs one. — T.L.


[REGISTERED No. 0453]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 24th of October — received 09:10, in the four hours, the one window his nephew could reach the connection to confirm posting before bringing the letter down by hand]
[On pharmacy letterhead — "FARMACIA COSTEA, lower Strada Făgădău, since the second currency, God help us all" — a chemist's small, even, terribly tidy hand:]

WITNESS REPLY
To the Honourable Magistrate Lupu, and to the Proceeding, with my most respectful compliments and the assurance that I remain, in this as in all things, your humble servant of public health —

I have your Query No.3 before me. I will answer it in the order you set it down, as a man with nothing to conceal answers in any order he is given, that order being a matter of indifference to the innocent.

To Q.1. There exists, between my pharmacy and the Uzina "Aurora Nr.4," a sum. I would characterise it as an ordinary commercial accommodation of the kind that obtains between any two businesses in a town this size, where, as the Magistrate well knows, everyone is owed by everyone, and the whole economy of Vâlcov is a single debt passed hand to hand so that no one need ever be the one holding it when the music stops. The sum is, as it happens, nine thousand. I do not see that the precise figure illuminates anything, but the Magistrate asked for it to the leu and I am, above all, obliging.

To Q.2. The sum is of long standing. It predates the night of the 14th of September by years, which I respectfully submit is the very point: a debt I have carried so long it has become a piece of furniture cannot be said to have *motivated* anything in particular on any particular night. As to whether any part of it has been forgiven or deferred — these are warm words, Magistrate, and I deal in measured doses. Nothing has been put in writing. I will say no more than that, because a man who says more than is written down soon finds the unwritten part used against him, and I have watched this proceeding closely enough to know that here, more than anywhere, the order a thing is said in is doing more work than the thing.

To Q.3. I owed the sum when I gave the State my testimony, as I owe it now, as I shall, in this republic, very probably owe it when they bury me. But I must, with the greatest respect, decline the implication folded into the Magistrate's question like a coin in a loaf. I did not testify *because* I owe the plant. I testified because the accused did, in fact, on the days I named, purchase from my counter the quantity I described, and I have the day-book to prove the sale, neat and dated, in this same hand. That is true. It was true before I owed a single leu and it would be true if Aurora forgave me tomorrow. The Magistrate may distrust my motive all he likes; he cannot, by distrusting it, un-sell the compound.

As to whether anyone connected to the plant "spoke to me" — people speak to me, Magistrate. I keep the only pharmacy left this side of the river. Olaru speaks to me; the whole town speaks to me; I am spoken to over my counter from morning till the four hours end the lights. If the Magistrate wishes me to swear that no human being employed by Aurora has, in the course of two years, mentioned the schoolteacher's name in my hearing, I cannot swear it, for I would be swearing falsely, and unlike some I will not post a thing I cannot certify is true.

I note, finally, and with sorrow, that I bought two ster of birch from the Magistrate's own stall not three days before this Query, and that the wood was wet, and that I paid the full price and said nothing of the wet, out of respect for the office. I had not expected the office to repay my discretion by asking, in writing and for the record, whether I am for sale. We are all of us for sale here, Magistrate. The only question the river has left us is the order in which we are bought.

I remain, with undiminished respect and a slightly diminished warmth,

V. COSTEA
Pharmacist, Vâlcov
Your humble servant of public health
[postscript, smaller, the tidy hand tightening:] The day-book is available to the Proceeding at any time. The debt is available to no one, which is rather the trouble with it.


ROUTING SLIP 0455.
Held, two items (0489, and the content held on 0447). Released, two items (0451 with its stray, and 0453), this cycle, in the order set out in the manifest above.
Reason of record:

I have done a small thing this cycle and I am going to record it accurately, because the form has a line for the reasons and a man who will not write down the small frauds has no standing to be surprised by the large one he becomes.

The thing is this. I had both of Costea's papers and the magistrate's query in the office on the same morning. I could have released the pharmacist's reply (0453) and his earlier full accusation together, so that the town read the man's testimony against the schoolteacher and his defence of his own honesty in one breath, as one document, the way the man himself would prefer — accused and excuse arriving as a single confident package, the debt admitted in the same envelope that explains it away. The order received would have permitted that. The bridge permitted it; the Podul Vechi is frozen but passable, the ice not yet thick enough to walk and the ford not yet shallow enough to ford, which is the worst state of the bridge and the one I can least blame, so I am not blaming it today.

Instead I have let the magistrate's debt-query land first, alone, with its accidental receipt, so that the whole of Vâlcov learns in the morning post that Valentin Costea owes the water-plant nine thousand leu — and only in the afternoon post, the town's mind already salted, does Costea's own voice arrive to tell them the debt means nothing. I have arranged for the wound to be seen before the bandage. This is not a forgery. Every word in both papers is the man's own and true; I have moved nothing, invented nothing, struck out nothing. I have only decided that the town shall read *nine thousand* before it reads *which is, of course, immaterial*, and a thing read first is weighed first, and a man defending a debt the town already knows about is in a poorer posture than a man producing it himself with a flourish. I have changed the posture of the truth without touching the truth. I am getting good at this. I record that I am getting good at it because it is the kind of skill a man ought to be afraid of in himself, and fear, like the reasons, has nowhere else in this building to go but the form.

I will say in my own defence — to the form, which is the only thing that asks — that Costea is not innocent here, and that the order I chose is the *true* order, in one defensible sense: the debt did come before the testimony, by years; the money was on the counter before the accusation was on the paper. I am, you could argue, merely restoring chronology. I notice that I reach for that argument very quickly. I notice that a man reaches fastest for the justification that flatters him, and that "I am only restoring the true order" is the most flattering sentence available to a man in my chair, and that I should therefore trust it least. I am restoring chronology in the one case this cycle where chronology happens to hurt the prosecution. I did not restore it last cycle when it would have helped them. A clock that only runs when it tells the hour you want is not a clock. It is you, holding two hands and calling yourself time.

As to the held items.

I continue to hold Costea's full accusation (the content logged on slip 0447) — it will go out Cycle 9, after she has been given her own account, exactly as I set down at the start; I am not moved from that by the man's tidy day-book. And I continue to hold the schoolteacher's records-request, No.0489, the one in which she asks for the *plant's* filtration logs — which is, I will say it plainly to the form because I have said it nowhere else, the single most dangerous question anyone has yet put into this proceeding, because it points the whole apparatus at the plant, where the magistrate's poor nose already smells the money. I am holding the smartest move in the file. I tell myself I am holding it for its moment, to land it where it will do the most. That is half true. The other half is that I am afraid of what I will be once I have released it — once the case turns toward Aurora, it is a different case, a bigger one, and I am not certain the order can carry it, or that I can.

A note I am required by nothing to make, and make:

She corrects spelling. Last cycle the magistrate misspelled a technical word and she corrected it in her reply, gently, the way a teacher does, and I sat with that for longer than the certification of posting required. This cycle Costea has written a letter of nine hundred words in defence of his honesty and has not made a single error, every comma placed, the hand immaculate, and it is the most dishonest paper to cross my counter since the proceeding opened. And in the bottom drawer there is a letter — I am not going to write its number, the form does not need the number, I need the form not to have it — a letter full of a woman's small fierce corrections of a court that is trying to hang her, and it is the most honest paper in the building. I have begun to think the tidiness of a hand is in inverse proportion to the honesty of the soul behind it, and that I have spent thirty years certifying the wrong quantity. I certify that a thing was posted. I have never once been asked to certify that it was true, and I am beginning to understand this was a mercy to me, because I no longer think I could tell a magistrate the difference between the two without my own hand starting to shake like his.

The query first. The denial after. The plant's logs nowhere, yet.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of Costea's reply, No.0453, before it went out:]
"The only question the river has left us is the order in which we are bought." He means it as a sigh. He has handed me my own office in a sentence and signed it, the way the Procuror did in the first cycle — they keep doing this, the confident men, posting me the key to the thing they think they are merely complaining about. Costea believes he is lamenting the corruption of the town. He is describing the corruption of the post. I am the order in which we are bought. I will keep this one too, beside the Procuror's sleeves-rolled-up, in the drawer where I keep the sentences that turn out, on the third reading, to be about me.

[STAMP: RELEASED — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — Cycle 7, in the order of record]
[STAMP, lower: HELD — No.0489 (records-request) — to release in a later cycle]
[STAMP, lower still: HELD — content per slip 0447 — to release Cycle 9]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 8 — "The Plant Manager Regrets He Cannot Attend"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 8    ·    Early November, the first hard frost on Drumul Aurora, the Casimca slacking and grey, ice forming in the willows where the water stands
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 8. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Witness Statement — R. Olaru, Manager, Uzina "Aurora Nr.4" → The Proceeding, c/o Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [REGISTERED No. 0478]
  2. Annex to No.0478 — Maintenance & Intake Inspection Log, Aurora Nr.4 (extract, Sept.–Oct.) — [REGISTERED No. 0479]
  3. Routing Slip 0480 — G. Enescu, Postmaster — release of 0478 & 0479; manner of release
  4. Registration Log — Central Sorting, Vâlcov (leaf for Cycle 8)

HELD (carried to Cycle 9, or longer):
  · Defense Letter, D. Albu — request for the plant's filtration records — [REGISTERED No. 0489] — held — slip 0482 — reason of record: "good order"

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion):
  · One leaf, R. Olaru → "the Postmaster, personally" — a private note enclosed loose with No.0478 — not part of the file — retained at the Hold, NOT by the stove

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0478]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 6th of November]
[Letterhead: UZINA DE ÎMBUTELIERE "AURORA Nr.4" — Apă de Izvor — Drumul Aurora, Vâlcov. The letterhead embossed; the embossing the only crisp thing on a page otherwise typed on a machine whose lower-case e prints faint.]

To the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov, and to the Magistrate appointed thereto —

RE: The State v. D. Albu — Statement of R. Olaru, Manager, in response to the Magistrate's Query of the 9th instant.

I have the honour to respond, within the cycle allotted, and to begin by registering, with respect, the Management's regret that it cannot attend in person, the proceeding being conducted, as I understand it, by post, and there being in any event no room in which to attend, the courthouse on Strada Cazaclia having, as the Court will be aware, gone partly into the river. I make this observation not in levity but to establish at the outset that the Management is co-operative within the limits the present circumstances impose upon all of us equally.

To the matter. The Court inquires whether the intake of the Uzina "Aurora Nr.4," which draws upon the same aquifer as the municipal well on Aleea Salciilor, was secure on the night of the 14th of September. I am able to state, on the basis of the plant's own records, which are appended hereto as Annex (Reg. 0479), that the intake was at all material times documented secure.

I wish the Court to weigh the precision of that phrase, which I have chosen with care. I do not say the water was good; the goodness of water is a question for chemists, and I am a manager. I say the intake was *documented secure*, which is the only fact within my competence and the only fact, I respectfully submit, that the Court may properly ask of a manager. The plant maintains a log. The log is kept by my own hand and the hand of the duty fitter. The log records inspection of the intake daily. The Court will find in the appended extract no entry indicating breach, tampering, or irregularity at the intake for the whole of September and October. There is nothing there. I commend the nothing to the Court's attention. Nothing is, after all, what the plant is charged with having allowed, and the log shows that the plant allowed nothing, daily, and recorded that it had done so.

As to the accused: I am informed she is a schoolteacher of Aleea Salciilor and that the State alleges she introduced a compound into the supply. The Management did not see her at the plant. The Management's fence is, I concede, in poor repair along the eastern run nearest the river — the Court will appreciate that fencing, like bridging, has become a matter for committees — and a determined person could approach the intake from the Drumul Aurora side without crossing the gate, where the gate-book would have recorded her. But the same gap admits the district's livestock with some regularity, and the Management has on three occasions in the relevant period removed a goat from the very ground the State now treats as the scene of a crime, and the goat left no statement.

The Management's position, stated plainly, is this. The plant was operating at minimal capacity, one shift in the week, sufficient to maintain the bottling licence and the water-rights attaching to it, which the Court will know are the only assets of value the plant retains. A plant that runs one shift in seven has, the Management respectfully suggests, less occasion to poison a town than a person who lives in it and draws from its well nightly. The Management drinks the same water. I drink it myself, when I am at the plant, which I will candidly admit is not often, the road being what it is in the wet, but the principle holds: a man does not foul a well he is licensed to sell.

I remain, with the Management's full co-operation and its standing regret at the limits of the medium,

R. OLARU
Manager, Uzina de Îmbuteliere "Aurora Nr.4"
(per the deed of the 11th of March, three years prior; rights to the Izvorul Aurora appurtenant)


[REGISTERED No. 0479]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 6th of November — annexed to and posted with No.0478]

The plant observed the Feast of St. Paraschiva, the 27th to the 29th of September, on which days the plant was shut and no person was on the premises by Management instruction. The intake was nonetheless inspected and found secure, the security of an intake being a condition that obtains whether or not a man is present to certify it, and the log being kept, as the Court will appreciate, for completeness.

[The following leaf was enclosed loose inside the envelope of No.0478, on plain paper, NOT on letterhead, in a different and hastier hand. It bears no registration number. It is addressed to me and not to the proceeding. — G.E.]

To the Postmaster, personally —

You will have read the statement by now, you read everything, this is well understood across the river. I write to you and not to the court because the court cannot do anything and you, I am given to understand, can.

A delivery is a thing that takes a certain time, and you decide the time. I am not asking you to lose anything. I would never ask an honest man to lose a thing; I know your reputation and it is the cleanest in the district, which is why I am writing to it. I am asking only that the records-request the schoolteacher has lodged — and she has lodged one, you may be sure, she is the sort who would — be allowed to find its own pace. The plant's filtration records are a private commercial matter and the deed protects them, and to compel their production through the post would be, I am advised, irregular under Order No.9, which speaks of letters and not of audits. A request that arrives in no particular hurry harms no one. The plant has been good to this district. The plant has been good, in particular, to men this district relies upon, the pharmacist among them, who I believe has already done his civic part. I trust I make myself understood to a man of your delicacy.

There would be, naturally, a gesture of the plant's gratitude appropriate to the registry's many burdens, the firewood season being hard on a building that must be kept warm for the public's letters.

R.O.


ROUTING SLIP 0480.
Released, this cycle: the statement, No.0478, and its annexed log, No.0479. Both together, all same cycle, no hold.
Reason of record:

I will deal first with the leaf, because the leaf is why my hands are not quite steady writing the slip, and a man should record the thing that unsteadied him before he records the thing he did.

Olaru, who controls the only water-rights and the only wage left east of the river, has enclosed in a registered envelope a private note offering me firewood to delay a woman's request for documents. He did not say firewood. He said "a gesture of the plant's gratitude appropriate to the registry's many burdens, the firewood season being hard on a building that must be kept warm for the public's letters." I have copied the sentence exactly, in his own construction, the way I kept the Procuror's sleeves-rolled-up figure — the way a careful man keeps the thing a powerful man hands him without meaning to. Olaru believes he is bribing a clerk. He has instead deposited, into a registry whose whole nature is that it keeps what it is given, written proof that he wished the schoolteacher's records-request slowed. He has handed the order the very document that proves the order is being courted. I will not register it to the proceeding — it is not addressed to it, and entering it would let the Procuror, who wants Domnica and not the plant, see that the plant is afraid, which is a thing I would rather decide myself when to let be seen. I am putting it at the Hold. Not by the stove. The stove is for the warm paper and this is not that; I keep a place at the cold end of the rack, by the window where the frost comes through, for paper a man keeps without wishing to warm his hands at it.

Now. The statement and the log. I have released them together, this cycle, in the prosecution's despite and the plant's, and I will say why, because the why is not flattering to me and the form has a line for it.

I could have held the log. I am honest in everything but arrangement, so I will say plainly that the log is the most dishonest document yet entered, and dishonest precisely by being too clean. It inspects the intake daily — daily — including the 27th, 28th, and 29th of September, the Feast of St. Paraschiva, on which days, by the manager's own appended note, the plant was shut and no man was on the premises. A man inspected an intake on three days when, by his own pen, no man was there. Olaru even armours the absurdity — "the security of an intake being a condition that obtains whether or not a man is present to certify it" — which is the finest sentence ever written by a man certifying the absence of an event he was absent for. Lupu's queries come on the backs of firewood receipts, his hand shaking with the cold, "aquifer" spelled three ways, and every one is true. Olaru's log is immaculate and every line of it is a small lie of completeness. That is the thing about cold paper: it is the warm hand that smudges, and the smudge is where the truth gets in.

So I could have held it — let it land beside the engineer's testimony I know is coming from the capital, the slow-poison account, so that the log's tidiness would read, in that order, as the too-careful denial of a guilty man. That is the order that helps her. I knew it as I sorted the envelope. My hand knew it.

I released it now, plain, beside nothing, in the cycle it arrived.

I am recording why, because it is the first thing I have done in this proceeding that was not for her and not against her but against *myself*, and I want one honest witness to it even if the witness is only a form no one reads. I have spent seven cycles now learning that I can set the order of the truth in this town the way a man sets a table, and the learning has begun to frighten me, because a hand that always knows the helping order is no longer weighing — it is a thumb, and a thumb is not justice, it is appetite wearing the robe of justice. So I have made myself a small rule, told to no one, Mihail least of all, who would log it: that when my hand is most certain of the helping order, that is precisely the cycle I am to release plain, and let the log lie in the open exactly as Olaru wrote it, and trust that a true thing — the engineer, when he comes — can do its own work without me ushering it to the front of the line like a man seating a guest he is in love with at the head of the table.

It is a small mortification and I do not pretend it is more. I have not stopped being the order. I have only, this once, refused to be the helping order, and the refusal cost me something I can feel in my sternum, which is the place a man feels the letters he does not send.

As to the records-request — No.0489, from her, arrived this same cycle, which I am holding — its reasons belong in their own slip, 0482, and I will not have them touch this one on the same leaf. I note here only that her request is the single best move anyone has made in this entire file, prosecution or defence, and that I have decided to hold it, and that the two facts sit in me at once and will not resolve.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0482.
Held: the Defense Letter, No.0489, request for the plant's filtration records.
Status: held one cycle, perhaps more. Reason of record:

I have read it four times. I will record that I have read it four times because the form asks for the matter and the matter is that I have read it four times.

It is one page. She has done what no advocate the district could not afford would have thought to do: she has not asked to be believed, she has asked to be allowed to *read*. She requests, under Order No.9 §11, the plant's full filtration records for the year — not the inspection log Olaru chooses to append, but the maintenance records, the filtration-medium replacement schedule, the discharge readings, the things a plant keeps when it is not yet thinking of a trial. She has reasoned — correctly, devastatingly, on one page, in the warm even hand that is warm still when I file it — that a log reading "secure, nominal" every day for two months describes either a plant functioning perfectly or a plant not being measured at all, and that the way to tell them apart is not to argue with the log but to ask for the readings underneath it, which a functioning plant has and a neglected one cannot produce.

She is asking, in other words, for exactly the thing that would push the case toward Olaru and away from her own throat. She has found the slow poison without being told it exists — reasoned her way to the true shape of the thing from inside the well it was poured into, with no evidence but the taste in her own mouth and the smell of a too-clean log — and phrased it so modestly, citing the clause and the sub-clause, that it reads less like a defence than like a teacher returning a sum to a child with the working shown in the margin, gently, so the child can see for himself where he went wrong.

Here is the sentence I have read four times. I will copy it, because the form is the only place in the building a man is permitted to set down what he has read, and because I do not trust myself to remember it as written rather than as I have begun, dangerously, to wish it written.

"I do not ask the Court to take my word over the Management's. I have noticed that the Court has very little to spend and would not wish it to spend its small store of belief on me, whom it has not met. I ask only for the numbers the plant keeps when no one is watching it, because numbers kept in the dark are the only honest witnesses left in this district — present company, whoever is reading this, of course excepted, for I have begun to suspect that the order in which I am heard is not an accident, and that there is one reader in this proceeding who keeps his honesty the way I keep mine: in the dark, where no one is watching, and where it is therefore worth something."

She has guessed at me again. Worse than guessed. She has made me a compliment that is also a hook — *I have begun to suspect the order is not an accident* — and dressed it in the one virtue I cannot disclaim without confessing the vice. If I deliver her request swiftly, to prove I am no man's instrument, I am acting on her flattery, which is to be her instrument; if I hold it, I am the thumb she has almost named; and either way she has, in a single procedural request for filtration records, reached through the cold rack and the frost and the window and put her finger precisely on the seam of me, which is that I keep my honesty in the dark where no one is watching, and that until her letter I had believed the dark was empty.

I am holding the request. I will record the reason that is for the file and then the reason that is not.

For the file: §11 entitles her to documents the proceeding *relies upon*. The proceeding has not yet relied upon the plant's filtration records, the plant having submitted only its log; until the magistrate or the prosecution puts the plant's filtration in issue, her request is, strictly, premature, and a premature request may be held without irregularity pending the matter ripening. That is true. That is the kind of true that is the whole disease of this place: a thing that is correct and is also a door held shut against a woman's hand.

Not for the file: if I release her request this cycle, it lands before the engineer comes, and the plant gets a clear cycle's warning to produce records, or to produce the absence of records dressed as a fire, a flood, a fitter who left, a box that went into the Casimca with the courthouse — Olaru has just shown me, on plain paper by the window, how fast he moves to bury a thing. If I hold it until the engineer's testimony is in my hand and the plant's filtration is squarely in issue and her request becomes not premature but ripe and unrefusable — then it lands when the plant cannot dodge it, and it lands lethal.

So I am holding her best move *because* it is her best move, to keep it from being spent early, the way you do not play your high card into a trick that does not matter. I am telling myself this is for her. It may even be true. But I have caught my hand at it now — the helping hand again, the very hour after I swore at the foot of 0480 to release plain when I am most certain — and looking at the held envelope at the cold end of the rack, where Olaru's bribe also lies, I cannot tell whether I am protecting her best card or simply keeping it, the way I keep everything I cannot bear to send: in the dark, mine, unplayed, where it can never disappoint me by arriving and being only what it was.

Held. Reason of record, for the file: premature under §11. The other reason is recorded above it and is not for the file and is the true one and is filed anyway, because the form has a line for it and no one reads this form but me.

Filed in good order. — G.E.

 [not registered] One loose leaf, R. Olaru → "the Postmaster, personally." Not on the proceeding.

Forty years this office has certified that a thing was sent. It has never before been offered wood to certify it slowly. I note for the column marked Particulars that the offer arrived embossed, the plant being too poor to pay its fitters and not too poor to emboss its letterhead, which is the whole Republic in a watermark: out of everything but appearances. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of Olaru's log, No.0479, before it went out:]
Three days he inspected a well no man stood beside, and certified it secure, and signed it. The difference between Olaru and me is only that he believes the form makes the thing true, and I have always known the form makes the thing *kept.* He keeps water he does not measure; I keep an order I should not set. And St. Paraschiva, on whose feast he certified the empty plant, is the patron of the sick — which is the joke God has filed in this matter, and I am recording it because the margin had room. The engineer is coming. When he comes her held card ripens. I will not look at the rack until then. I have looked at it eleven times today, which is not a reason, and which I am recording anyway.
