THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 9 — "The Same Night, Told First"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 9    ·    Late October, the Casimca dropping at last, the willows on Aleea Salciilor out of the water and stinking of it, the first frost on the Podul Vechi rails
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 9. Released this cycle, in the order below, and the order is the whole of it:
  1. Witness Letter — V. Costea, pharmacist (the purchase) — HELD since Cycle 6 on Slip 0447 — released FIRST this cycle — [REGISTERED No. 0461]
  2. Witness Statement — T. Negoiță, of Drumul Aurora (the sighting) — released SECOND — [REGISTERED No. 0488]
  3. Defense Account — D. Albu (her own short account of the night) — released THIRD and LAST — [REGISTERED No. 0491]
  4. Routing Slip 0492 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (carried to a later cycle):
  · The child's note (Ilinca Pop) — received this cycle, NOT released — held — reason of record: "pending the right order" — Slip 0492
  · Domnica's records-request (the plant's filtration logs, from Cycle 8) — still held

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING:
  · Envelope 0431 — at the Hold, by the stove — read this cycle a twelfth time — not part of the file

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0461]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 9th of October — received Cycle 6]   [HELD — released Cycle 9, this day]
[on the letterhead of the Farmacia Costea, lower Strada Făgădău — a neat chemist's hand]

To the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov, and to the Magistrate appointed thereto —

I write as your humble servant of public health, and only because the law obliges a man to set down what he has seen, which I do with a heavy heart, the accused being a woman of standing in this town and a teacher of its children, including, I will say, two of my own sister's, who speak well of her.

I am asked to attest to a sale. I attest to it. On the eleventh of September last, three days before the night the State asks about, Domnica Albu came to my counter on lower Strada Făgădău and purchased a quantity of a compound — I will not name it in an open letter, the registry having its rules about such things, but it is recorded in my poison-register in the manner the law requires, and the register is available to the court. The quantity was not small. It was the quantity a person buys who means to use it.

I asked her, as I ask everyone who buys such a thing, what it was for. She did not give me a reason a pharmacist is accustomed to hear. She said she would "see to the water herself." I thought it a strange thing to say and I have thought of it many times since, and more times since the fourteenth, and I set it down now not to harm her but because a man who keeps the poison-register of a town and says nothing when the water goes bad is a man who has failed in his duty to public health, which I have not, whatever else may be said of me, and I trust will not be.

I confine myself to the sale and to her words. I draw no conclusion. I am not a magistrate. I am a pharmacist, and a careful one, and your humble servant.

VALENTIN COSTEA
Farmacist, lower Strada Făgădău
Sworn as to posting before the Central Sorting Office


[REGISTERED No. 0488]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 21st of October]
[a plain hand, pencil gone over in ink where it faded, the spelling of a man who left school early and was not sorry]

To whoever this is supposed to go to —

The court wrote and asked what I saw on the night of the fourteenth of September, and I will tell it, but first I have to tell about the goat, because if I leave the goat out then I was not out on the road and then I saw nothing, and I did see something, so the goat has to come in.

My goat got through the wire about dark. She does this. She had done it twice that week and I had mended the wire twice with the wire I had, which is bad wire, the good wire being a thing you buy in the capital, and she got through a third place that I had not even known was a place. So I was on Drumul Aurora after dark, which I would not otherwise have been, no man being on that road at night for a good reason, and there I was for a bad one, looking for a goat with a lantern, calling her by name, which is Steluța, and which I tell the court only because I called it out loud some dozen times that night and if anyone else was on that road they heard a grown man calling Steluța into the dark, and that man was me, and I will swear to it.

She had gone down toward the plant because there is grass along the Aurora fence there that nobody cuts, the plant not being a place that cuts grass, the plant not being a place that does much of anything most weeks, and a goat knows where the uncut grass is the way the court knows where the firewood is, which is to say by need.

So I was down by the Aurora fence near the intake, which is the low building where the pipe goes into the ground, maybe eleven o'clock, maybe ten — I keep a clock by the river and the river is not a punctual clock, it runs fast in spring and stops altogether in August — and I saw the teacher. Domnica Albu. I have known her face fifteen years; she taught my granddaughter her letters and the girl can read a feed-sack now, which is more than I can, so I owe her that, and I set it down so the court knows I am not a man with a grievance. She was at the fence. She had a bag, a school bag, the kind with the strap. She went along toward the intake side where the water is, and she was bent over the water doing something I could not see clear, a white something, pouring or shaking, I could not tell which from where I stood and I did not go closer, a man with a goat in one hand and a lantern in the other being a man with no hands left for going closer. And then I had Steluța by the rope and I went home, the goat being the thing I came for, and the teacher being none of my business until the court made her my business by writing to me.

That is what I saw. A woman I know, at the water, at night, with a bag, doing a thing with something white. I do not say what it means. I say what I saw. I would not have been there at all but for the goat, and I want the court to know the goat is not mine by choice, she came with the house.

TUDOR NEGOIȚĂ
Drumul Aurora, the fence where the road bends to the plant
Sworn as to posting before the Central Sorting Office


[REGISTERED No. 0491]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 22nd of October]
[Domnica's hand — measured, no flourish; she has been told to keep it short and she has kept it short, and the shortness is its own kind of damning, released here LAST]

To the registry, and to the Magistrate, and to whoever decides the order in which I am read —

I am instructed to give a short account of the night of the fourteenth of September, and to confine myself to facts, and so I will, though I notice the State has already chosen which of my facts will be read and in what order, and I have begun to think that whoever holds these letters knows better than the State does how much that choosing decides.

The facts I am permitted to give, shortly:

I went to the plant at Aurora No.4 on the night of the fourteenth. I went after dark. I crossed by the Podul Vechi. I had with me a quantity of the compound the pharmacist has truthfully said I bought — I do not dispute the sale, Costea is an honest man in the small things and I will not make him a liar to save myself. I went to the intake. I put the compound into the water.

There. That is the account, kept as short as the court asked, and I have given it plainly because I will not be caught in a small lie and lose the right to be believed in a large truth. I did the thing. I bought it, I carried it, I poured it.

What the short account does not have room for — what the order of these letters has decided I will not be asked, this cycle, in time — is the word *why*, and the word *for*, and the name of the child, and what the water tasted of before I touched it, which was bitterness, and then coins, and then nothing. But I am told to be brief, and brevity, I have learned this autumn, is the State's favorite poison, because it is colorless and leaves no mark and a person dies of it in good order.

I will say only this, and then I will obey the instruction and stop: a sentence that ends *I poured it* is a true sentence, and it is not the true sentence, and the difference between those two is the only thing I have left, and I am putting it into the hands of the one person in this proceeding who I believe still knows there is a difference.

DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school


ROUTING SLIP 0492.
Released this cycle, in order: 0461 (held since Cycle 6), then 0488, then 0491. The held child's note (received this day) NOT released.
Reason of record:

I have done a thing today that I want set down exactly, the way a man sets down a dose, so that whoever reads this — and no one reads this, the form is read by no one but me, which is the only reason I can write it — will know I knew what I was doing and did it on purpose.

For six cycles I have arranged this case so that the accused arrives in the reader's mind before the accusation does. I held Costea's true letter on Slip 0447 so that the town would meet the woman before it met the sale. I have called that mercy. I have called it good order. This cycle I did the other thing. I released the three of them in the order the Procuror would have chosen if the Procuror understood that order is a weapon, which he does not, mail being to him a kind of plumbing.

I released the sale first. *She bought a poison and said she would see to the water herself.* Then the sighting. *A woman the witness has known fifteen years, at the water, at night, with a bag, pouring a white something.* Then, last, her own account, which the magistrate had instructed her to keep short, and which therefore arrives as a confession with the reasons amputated: *I bought it, I carried it, I poured it.* Read in that order — purchase, then presence, then her own bare *I poured it* — there is no woman in it. There is a sequence with its sleeves rolled up, as the Procuror said in the indictment, not knowing he was teaching the registry its trade. Purchase. Presence. Admission. Guilt walks in on three legs and does not need a fourth. I built it. I am good at it. That is the part I am recording.

I want to be accurate about why I did it, because I have been telling myself for six cycles that I arrange her toward mercy because she is innocent, and a man who can only ever arrange a thing one way does not actually know whether he believes it or only prefers it. So I did it the other way once. I wanted to see whether I could make her guilty with the same true papers, no forgery, no lie, only the order — and whether, having made her guilty, I would feel I had told a lie. I made her guilty. It took three letters and an afternoon. And I do not feel I have lied, which is the sickening part, the part I am setting down: every word delivered this cycle is true, every postmark honest, every signature real, and a careful reader given only this cycle would convict her tonight and would be reading the truth when he did it. I have proven I can build the gallows out of facts. I am not relieved. I had hoped to fail.

As to the child's note: it came this day, in a child's hand, on the back of a graded spelling test — Pop, Ilinca, of the Aleea Salciilor school, the grade still on it, ninety-four, and in the teacher's hand the words *lovely work, Ilinca* — and the note has in it two things, and I have read it, and I will not release it this cycle. I am required to record my reason and my reason is this: the note contains, in nine-year-old spelling, both the pouring and a second thing the child saw, and if I release the note into *this* cycle, beside the guilt-order, the second thing will be read as the smaller thing, swallowed by the sequence I built, and once a town has read a child's note in the guilty order it cannot un-read it. The note is the only unrigged witness in the whole proceeding — a child who saw everything and reports it whole, and whose honesty therefore settles nothing — and an unrigged truth is exactly the thing a man in my position must be most careful where he sets down, because beside the wrong cycle it stops being unrigged. I am holding it. Pending the right order. There will be a cycle where it lands and means the other thing, and I will know I held it for that, and I will not be able to tell, then either, whether I held it because it is just or because it is hers. I note that the held child's note and the test it is written on are now in the Hold together, which means the State is presently holding a poisoning case paper-clipped to a gold star.

I note, last and out of order, that 0431 is by the stove and that I read it again tonight after the three guilty papers went out, the twelfth time, to remind myself what her sentences sound like when no one has arranged them — and that the sentence she put in 0491, the short account, the *I poured it, and it is not the true sentence,* she wrote knowing it would be read last and bare. She wrote toward the order. She has guessed there is a hand. She is writing to the hand. I delivered her into guilt this cycle with three true letters, and in the third one she reached past all three of them and addressed the man who arranged them, and asked him, without naming him, whether he still knows the difference between a true sentence and the true sentence. He does. That is the whole of his usefulness and the whole of his crime.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the held child's note, before it went back to the Hold:]
ninety-four. lovely work, Ilinca. — the teacher graded the paper before she was a defendant, and the State will read the back of it before it reads the front, which is the order of everything now: we read the accusation, then the soul, then the gold star, and we have it exactly backwards, and I am the one holding it upside down so that it lands that way. The note waits. Cycle to be chosen. I will know the cycle when I see what I want it to mean, which is the confession the form does not have a line for, so I am writing it in the margin, where the form cannot stop me.

[REGISTERED No. 0508]   [POSTMARK: DISTRICT SEAT, the 2nd of November — received Vâlcov Central the 5th, the Podul Vechi being passable but slow]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
PROSECUTION SUMMARY
Filed by Procuror Anghel Câmpeanu, of the District Seat

To the Magistrate appointed, and to the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov —

The State, the prosecution phase being substantially complete, sets down the following summary, that the Magistrate may see the case whole and conclude it without the further dilation which the season, the river, and the patience of the district can ill afford.

The case is not complicated. It has been made to feel complicated by the manner of its arrival, which is a matter for the post and not for the law, and I leave it there. Reduced to its bones, the matter is this:

That the accused, Domnica Albu, did on a day in the second week of September purchase from the pharmacy of one V. Costea a quantity of a compound suited to the contamination charged — a fact attested, sworn, and registered (No.0441);

That the accused was seen, in the hours of darkness on the night of the 14th of September, upon Drumul Aurora, walking toward the intake of the Uzina "Aurora Nr.4" — a fact attested by a neighbour and registered (No.0488);

That the water, having been good, became bad, and became bad on that night;

And that the accused, being a person of education, is presumed to have foreseen the consequence, education being precisely the faculty by which a person foresees.

Purchase, presence, result, capacity to foresee. Four facts, and the line that joins them is not drawn by the State but by ordinary reason, which draws it whether the State wishes it or not. The defence will say the line is drawn in the wrong order. The defence is welcome to its order. The State observes only that a woman who buys a poison, carries it by night to a water-intake, and is followed by the water turning bad, has arranged the sequence herself, and cannot now complain of it.

I note, with the respect a metropolitan officer owes a provincial registry that has laboured under difficult conditions, that the conduct of delivery in this proceeding has been *deliberate.* I do not say irregular. I say deliberate, and I trust the registry will take the distinction in the spirit of accuracy in which it is offered. Letters have arrived in this case the way a man tells a story he has already decided the ending of — the exonerating matter early, the damning matter late, the whole weighted, somehow, against the obvious. I am not in a position to prove this and I do not allege it. I record it the way one records the weather: I was rained on, and I do not know the cloud's intentions, only that I am wet.

The State therefore requests that the Magistrate, in framing his final query and his ruling, attend to the *facts* and not to their choreography. The facts do not dance. They have been made to.

I append, as is proper, the registration numbers of all matter relied upon, so that the Magistrate may satisfy himself it is on the file and not merely in the air.

Respectfully — and with the observation, which I trust will not be mistaken for impatience, that I have now crossed the Podul Vechi four times for this proceeding and would prefer the fifth to be the last —

ANGHEL CÂMPEANU
Procuror, District Seat

[margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of No.0508:]
He has felt it. He cannot prove it and will not allege it, but he has stood in the rain long enough to look up. *The facts do not dance. They have been made to.* He means it as a complaint and has written, again, the registry's whole philosophy and signed it, again — the second time a prosecutor has handed me my method in a figure of speech, the first being the sleeves rolled up. I should stop keeping these. A careful man does not collect the evidence against himself in a violet hand in his own margin. I am keeping it anyway. The form has a line for it. He is right, is the trouble. The facts do not dance, and I am the music.


[TELEGRAM — received via the four-hour relay, 06:00–10:00, the 6th of November, the connection holding for nine minutes of it. Logged. NOT registered to the proceeding — a telegram is an instruction to the office, not a paper in the case. — G.E.]

TELEGRAM — DISTRICT SEAT TO VÂLCOV CENTRAL SORTING — TG-01
PRIORITY — STATE FUNCTION OF RECORD

STATE v ALBU PRODUCING DELAY STOP DISTRICT NOTES PROCEEDING OPEN ELEVEN WEEKS STOP CONCLUDE EXPEDITIOUSLY STOP RESOURCES LIMI[smudged — see endorsement] STOP NO FURTHER CYCLES TO BE WASTED ON [ink failed here] OF DELIVERY STOP REGISTRY TO REPORT CAUSE OF DELAY BY RETURN STOP

[STAMP, lower right: RESOURCES LIMITED — and the stamp itself is half-printed, the word LIMITED trailing off into dry purple, the District telegraph office being, per the relay clerk's pencilled aside, "out of violet, will reorder, the connection permitting."]

[Endorsement, G.E.:] The telegram instructs the registry to "conclude expeditiously" and, in the same breath, regrets that resources are limited — so limited that the stamp announcing the limit ran out of ink halfway through announcing it. The District has commanded speed on a wire it could not afford to finish transmitting. I have read it three times to be sure the gap after "wasted on" was the machine and not the meaning, and I am still not sure: NO FURTHER CYCLES TO BE WASTED ON [ ] OF DELIVERY. On *the order* of delivery, I think it means. They have noticed the order. They have not yet decided to be afraid of it. The word that fell out was the word that mattered, which is the usual economy of telegrams, and of the State, and of this whole republic — it sends you the imperative and rations the noun.


ROUTING SLIP 0510.
Status: Released — the Summary, No.0508, this cycle. Held — the records-request, No.0489, one further cycle. Held — the Procuror's request for expedition — indefinitely, no slip number to govern it, as a request to hurry is not a document, it is a mood.
Reason of record:

The Procuror asks me to attend to the facts and not their choreography. I have attended to nothing else for eleven weeks. He thinks the choreography is a distraction from the facts. He has it backwards. The facts in this case are four — purchase, presence, result, foreseeing — and not one of them is in dispute. She bought the compound; the pharmacist swears it and I believe him. She was on Drumul Aurora that night; the neighbour swears it, between two paragraphs about a goat, and I believe him. The water went bad; the whole town can taste it still. She is educated; her spelling alone convicts her of that. Four true facts. The Procuror is correct that no one is lying.

And four true facts, delivered in the order he prefers, hang her, and delivered in another order, true every one of them, the same four, do not. That is not a distraction from the facts. That is the facts. He wants me to believe the choreography is a film over the truth that a clean hand could wipe away to reveal the verdict underneath, fixed and waiting. There is nothing underneath. The order is not the wrapping. The order is the thing. He stood in the rain and looked up and saw a cloud and called it weather and asked me to ignore it, and the cloud is me.

So I will tell him the cause of the delay, which he has demanded by return, and I will tell him truthfully, which is the only way I know how to tell him anything:

There is no delay. There is a *rate.* A proceeding moves at the rate of the cycles it requires to be understood, and a town that has been told, in eleven weeks, that there is such a thing as a poisoner among its schoolteachers needs more than four facts in a metropolitan's preferred sequence; it needs the time to learn that four true things can be assembled into a lie without a single one of them being false. I am giving it that time. The District calls this delay because the District measures justice the way it measures everything — against the calendar, against the firewood, against the patience of men who have crossed a bridge four times and want the fifth to be the last. I do not measure it against the calendar. I measure it against good order, which the Ministry commanded and did not define, and which I have therefore been left to supply, and which I am supplying at the only rate at which it is true.

I will draft the reply to the District in the four hours tomorrow, if the connection holds longer than nine minutes, which it will not. I will tell them the delay is the Podul Vechi and the season and the volume of registered matter, all of which is also true, the way the Procuror's four facts are true: each statement accurate, the sum a fiction I have built on purpose. I have become very good at this. A man should record when he has become very good at a thing, the way a craftsman dates the first piece he is no longer ashamed of, except that I am ashamed of it, so let me date it instead the way a man dates the morning he noticed the shame had stopped stopping him.

I have read envelope 0431 a twelfth time this cycle. It is not a reason for any hold and governs no delivery and has no number on the proceeding and I record it because the form has a line marked *Particulars of Item* and because, after eleven weeks of arranging the order in which a town is permitted to believe a woman guilty, it is the only paper in this building I have read for the sentences and not for the sequence. She wrote, in it, that nothing is the worst of the three tastes — bitter, coins, nothing — because nothing cannot be indicted. I have begun to think the order of these things is the fourth taste, and that it is also nothing, and that it is also the worst, and that I am the one pouring it.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

Note for the next leaf, and for whatever clerk inherits this book when the river has the rest of the building: the prosecution phase closes Cycle 11. The town, as of this cycle, leans guilty. I record this not as my opinion of the accused — I have none I would swear to — but as my reading of the file's weight as delivered, which is a thing only this office is positioned to know, the file being the only place the town's mind is written down. The lean is mine. I built it, one held envelope at a time, to test whether I could, in the cycle the outline of my conscience required, deliver her into the worst of it — and I could, and I did, and I have spent the cycles since unbuilding it, which is also me. The accused has not changed. The four facts have not changed. Only the order has changed, and the order is mine, and so, this cycle, is the lean. A man should write down the day he understood that the verdict was a thing he was carrying in his own hands and could set down on either side of the line at will. That day was Cycle 9. This is the leaf after it. — G.E.


INTERNAL NOTE — VÂLCOV CENTRAL SORTING
Deputy's window. To File; copy to Postal Union, District Branch, per Art.11 of the Union Compact (member's duty to report irregularity in the chain of custody).
From: M. Brânză, Deputy Sorter.
Re: Irregular hold patterns, The State v. Albu — second entry.

For the record, and copied to the union as is my right and, I am advised, my duty:

This is the second note I have opened on this proceeding. The first (filed Cycle 3) flagged that the indictment, No.0002, was held one cycle in Cycle 1 without recorded operational necessity — the bridge being passable that day, the bag being light. The Postmaster's slip gave the reason as "good order." I logged it. I let it stand. A man is allowed one slip.

I am now obliged to log the pattern, the pattern being what a single instance becomes when you are patient enough to wait for the second, and the third, and the ninth. Across ten cycles I count the following holds entered by the Postmaster on this proceeding, each with a reason of record, each reason being some variation on "good order," "pending," or "the rate":

— the indictment, held one cycle (Cycle 1);
— the pharmacist Costea's accusation, No.0441, held on slip 0447 until the accused's own account had landed first (Cycle 6);
— the accused's records-request to the plant, No.0489, held now three cycles running (Cycles 8, 9, 10), which I note is a hold operating *against* the accused, so I will not be told this is mere softness toward a schoolteacher;
— and a re-sequencing in Cycle 9 of three statements — Costea, the neighbour, the accused — into an order I am not qualified to characterise except to say that I have sorted mail for nine years and I have never seen the Postmaster hold a witness statement to wait for a particular companion, and in Cycle 9 he held two to wait for a third.

I make no allegation of forgery. I have inspected the registry and the postmarks and I will state plainly, for the union and for whatever inspector this note may one day reach: nothing has been forged, nothing has been destroyed, nothing has been altered. The Postmaster is, by the narrow letter, honest. Every letter that entered this office has left it, intact, registered, dated, delivered. I want that on the record because I am not a man with a grievance dressing it as principle, whatever the Postmaster's slip will say of me when he reads this, as he will, the office having no secrets from the man who runs it.

But "in good order," in Provisional Order No.9 §3, cannot mean *whatever order one man decides,* or the words are empty and the chain of custody is a single fist. I do not think the Republic, when it moved justice into this building to save it from the river, intended to hand one provincial postmaster the power to weight a verdict by the calendar of his own choosing. I think that is precisely the power it has, by accident, handed him. And I think a chain of custody is not a chain if one link can choose, link by link, the sequence in which the truth is permitted to be true.

Logged. Copied to the union. Dated. I have kept my own register, parallel to the office's, since Cycle 3, and I will produce it to any authority that asks. I record finally, as the Postmaster records his particulars, one of my own: the Postmaster keeps a stove, and certain letters in this proceeding are warm when they reach the rack and certain letters are cold, and I have begun to keep a note of which is which. I do not yet know what it means. I expect it means nothing. I am writing it down because writing down the things that mean nothing is, I have learned from watching him do it for nine years, how a man eventually learns what they mean.

For the record. — M. Brânză


[margin, G.E., in violet, across the foot of Mihail's note, before it went to file:]
He has it almost exactly right, which is the worst kind of wrong to be the object of. Every fact in his note is true. He has not forged the case against me any more than I have forged the case against her; he has merely *ordered* it — the indictment, then 0447, then the held records-request "against" her, then Cycle 9 — and ordered well, and arrived at me. He is doing to me precisely what I have done to her, and with the same materials, which are true facts in a chosen sequence, and the conclusion he reaches is also true, and also a thing he built. I taught him this. Nine years at the window beside me, watching me file my reasons, and he learned the one lesson I never meant to give: that recording everything is not innocence. He thinks his register clears him. It is his confession; he simply does not love anyone, so he cannot read it as one.

And he has noticed the stove. He does not know what it means. Neither, until this cycle, did I — that the warm letters cluster on her side of the file because I keep them by the heat to read them again, and that my hands have left a temperature on the evidence the way a hand leaves a print. He will produce his note to "any authority that asks." An authority is going to ask. The District has crossed the bridge four times in its mind already; it will send a fifth crossing it does not call a Procuror. And when it comes, it will not need to break a single seal. It will only need to read the reasons I was so careful to record — the form having a line for them, and I having mistaken the line for a confessor — and lay them beside a deputy's cold parallel ledger, and put its hand, idly, on the stove.

I have decided I am the order. I wrote that in the first week, as a boast. I set it down again now, the twelfth time I have read her letter and the second time a man has told me, to my face and on paper, that the order is the crime: I am the order, and the order has begun, very quietly, to come for the man who is it.

Filed in good order. — G.E.

CHAPTER 11 — "The State Rests (By Registered Post)"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 11    ·    Late November, the first real frost on the willows of Aleea Salciilor, the Casimca running low and black between its banks for the first time since spring, the stove the only honest warmth in the building
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 11. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Prosecution Submission — "Closing of the State's Case" — Procuror A. Câmpeanu → The Proceeding — [REGISTERED No. 0204]
  2. Schedule of Returned Receipts (aviz de primire) — Cycles 1–10, compiled — Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [office exhibit, no registration number; appended to the file under §3 as proof of service]
  3. Magistrate's Order — Opening the Defense Phase — T. Lupu → The Proceeding — [REGISTERED No. 0206]
  4. Routing Slip 0207 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (carried to Cycle 12):
  · Domnica Albu's records-request to the plant (the filtration records), held since Cycle 8 — slip 0207 — to release Cycle 12, ahead of her account
  · Aviz card No.0188 (Olaru's receipt for the prosecution summary) — returned unsigned, "addressee absent, capital" — carried pending re-service

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion):
  · One green aviz card, blank, never sent, never registered — retained at the Hold, by the stove, for reasons set out in slip 0207

[REGISTERED No. 0204]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 24th of November — received 09:10, during the four hours]

PROSECUTION SUBMISSION
CLOSING OF THE STATE'S CASE
Filed by Procuror Anghel Câmpeanu, of the District Seat

To the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov, and to the Magistrate appointed thereto —

The State, having submitted its evidence in full and in good order, rests.

I will not waste the registry's paper, which I am told is rationed along with everything else in this town, by rehearsing what the file already holds. I will only ask the Magistrate to read the documents in the sequence they were delivered to him, which is the sequence in which a reasonable man arrives at the truth: first that the accused procured the compound, on the unrebutted testimony of the pharmacist Costea; second that the accused was abroad on Drumul Aurora in the dark, on the testimony of her neighbour; and third, from the accused's own account, that she was present at the intake on the night the water turned. Purchase, presence, result. The State submits there is nothing here but a straight line, and a straight line, as even a provincial registry will appreciate, is the shortest distance between a woman and a verdict.

The defence will say she meant well. The State observes that the road to a poisoned aquifer is no different from any other road in the matter of its paving. The State observes further that "she meant well" is not a clause known to Order No.9, which provides for guilt and for innocence and for nothing in between, the Ministry having sensibly declined to legislate for the interior weather of schoolteachers.

I anticipate, too, that the defence will gesture toward the plant — toward Aurora No.4, toward its manager, toward the convenient abstraction of "the water-rights" — as men gesture at the horizon when they do not wish you to look at their hands. The State has considered the plant. The plant keeps a maintenance log. The log records the intake inspected and secure. A documented institution is not a defendant; it is a record. The accused, by contrast, kept no log of the night, and a person who acts in the dark and keeps no record of it has, in the State's submission, told us by her silence what she expected the record to show. The defence may make a plant of the schoolteacher and a schoolteacher of the plant if it likes the exercise. The State prefers the woman who was seen, against the building that filed a form.

I note for the registry's information, since I am obliged to send a copy of every submission to the chain-of-custody authority, that the District Seat has twice now requested this matter be concluded expeditiously, and that the season is against further delay — the river, I am given to understand, takes a little more of the courthouse each spring, and I would prefer the verdict to outlive the building it cannot be read in.

The State rests, and asks only that it be allowed to.

Respectfully,
ANGHEL CÂMPEANU
Procuror, District Seat

 Certified a true schedule of service to this cycle. The cards themselves are retained in the registry, racked by number, available to the Magistrate on application. — G.E.

 [margin, G.E., in violet, beneath the schedule:]
 A green card proves a thing arrived and was held in a human hand on a particular day. It does not prove the hand believed it. We certify reception, not assent — the post has never been able to stamp the inside of a person, though the Ministry, given paper enough, would try. I note the schedule reads, top to bottom, like a verdict already entered: purchase, sighting, presence, every card signed, every door answered, the town's whole hand laid open and saying *received, received, received.* Ten cards. Nine of them, the town now believes, say *guilty,* and they say it not because the town reasoned to it but because the town received it in that order and the heart keeps whatever it is given first. I built that order. I have the cards to prove I served it. This is the first document in the file that is evidence against me, and I have filed it myself, in good order, because I am the registry and the registry files everything, including the rope.


[REGISTERED No. 0206]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 25th of November]
[Written on the reverse of a printed receipt: "PIAȚA LIPSEI — wood, dry, 1 ster — PAID." The stall's stamp shows faintly through the paper, under the Magistrate's hand.]

MAGISTRATE'S ORDER
On the Opening of the Defence Phase
Toader Lupu, Magistrate, Vâlcov

The State having rested, and the registry having certified service of the whole of the prosecution's case upon the accused —

IT IS ORDERED that the defence phase of this proceeding is opened, and that the accused, Domnica Albu, self-represented under the austerity provision of Order No.9, is invited to submit her defence by registered letter, within such delivery cycles as the season and the river allow.

I instruct the registry to deliver to the accused, with this Order, every document of the State's case that she has not already received, that she may answer the whole of it and not a part. I instruct the registry further — and I am aware this instruction has no clause behind it, but I am the Magistrate and a man must be allowed one instruction per proceeding that comes from him and not from the Ministry — to deliver her case to her in good order. By which I mean: completely, and fairly, and in the sequence in which a person might bear to read that she stands accused of poisoning her own town's water. I do not know that there is a kind sequence for such a thing. I leave it to the registry, which has more practice than I in the order of things, the river having left me only the disorder.

I add, the office being short of forms again and the season being what it is, that I write this on the back of a receipt for one ster of dry wood, paid, from my own stall, because I have not been sent a magistrate's form since the Feast of St. Paraschiva and a man must rule on the paper he has. Let the receipt stand as part of the record. It is the truest document I have filed all autumn: it proves I was at the market, that the wood was dry, and that somebody paid. The state cannot say as much for any of its own seals this winter.

By the authority vested — vested, I confess, by no one currently paying me, and by a Judge I have not heard from since the leaves —

T. LUPU, Magistrate
Vâlcov

[the hand is noticeably worse than in earlier orders; the final two lines slope downward and the ink thins, as of a pen pressed by a cold hand that cannot quite warm to the nib]


ROUTING SLIP 0207.
Held: two items, carried to Cycle 12. Released: three, this cycle.
Reason of record:

The State rests. I have read the Procuror's closing four times — twice for the route, twice for the man — and I find I am grateful to him, which is not a feeling I expected to file this autumn. He has done me the service of writing his whole method down and signing it. *Read the documents in the sequence they were delivered,* he says, *which is the sequence in which a reasonable man arrives at the truth.* He believes the sequence is the truth. He believes it so completely that he has built his closing argument on it and posted it to the one man in the Republic who knows that the sequence was not arrived at by a reasonable man but arranged by a lonely one. The Procuror thinks he is describing the order of the file. He is describing me. He has written my name across the top of his case and spelled it *the truth,* and he does not know he has done it, the way he did not know, in October, that he handed the registry its whole philosophy in a figure about sleeves.

So: the State rests, and it rests on the order, and the order is mine, and now I must spend the next six cycles arguing a town out of a verdict I spent the last six arguing it into. I am, I see, going to defend her. Not because the Magistrate asked me to deliver her case "in good order" — though he did, and I noted the way he reached for the phrase as for a tool he had found me using, the way one workman picks up another's plane to feel where the blade is set. He suspects. He wrote *I leave it to the registry, which has more practice than I in the order of things,* and a man does not write that to a registry he believes is innocent of order. He wrote it the way you tell a man you know he has the knife: gently, and where it can be heard.

I note, while I am being grateful to the Procuror, that he has gone further this time and anticipated the defence — he has reached for the plant, named it, and set it down again, calling it "a record, not a defendant," which is the cleverest wrong thing anyone has written into this file. He is right that a maintenance log is not a man. He is wrong about which direction that cuts. A log that records the intake "inspected daily" on three days the plant did not draw water is not a record of an institution's innocence; it is a record of an institution's habit of writing down whatever keeps the license alive. But the Procuror cannot see this, because to him a filed form is a closed question and a frightened woman is an open one, and he has spent a metropolitan career mistaking tidiness for truth. I, who have sorted thirty years of this town's paper, know the opposite: the tidiest hands in Vâlcov belong to the people with the most to bury. Lupu writes on the back of a wood receipt in a cold, sloping, honest mess. Olaru's logs are immaculate. I would hang the immaculate one and have done, if hanging were in the gift of the post, which — I record this with some regret — it is not.

I am going to defend her, and here is the unbearable part, which the form asks for under *Reason of Record* and which I am setting down because no one but me reads this line: I do not know whether I am defending her because the prosecution's order was unjust, or because I prefer the order in which she wins. I have proven, these eleven cycles, that I can make her guilty (Cycle 9) and that I can make her innocent (every cycle since), and a man who can make a thing either way has lost the right to say he believes one of them. I believe the order I prefer. I prefer the order in which I keep reading her. These are, I am beginning to fear, the same sentence.

As to the schedule of cards. I have entered it to the file. I did not have to — a schedule of service is not a submission; nothing in Order No.9 requires me to compile ten green cards into a column and lay them before the Magistrate like a hand of dealt cards. I entered it because it is true, and because it is the only honest accounting in the building of what I have done: ten doors opened, ten things received, in an order I chose, and the town's whole heart leaning the way I tilted the floor. If the inspector the district keeps threatening ever crosses the river, this schedule is the first thing she should read, and I have made sure it is the first thing she will find, racked by number, in good order, with my initials on it. A man who is going to be caught should at least have the dignity of having filed the evidence himself. I will not make her dig.

As to the holds. I am carrying the accused's records-request — the one for the plant's filtration records, the smartest move anyone has made in this file, which I have been sitting on since Cycle 8 — one cycle more, to release it ahead of her defence account, so that when the town reads what she did at the intake it is already holding in its other hand the question of what the *plant* did at the intake, every day, for months, by log, including three days the plant was shut for the Feast. Purchase, presence, result, the Procuror says. I am going to add a fourth word to his straight line, and the word is *whose,* and I am going to deliver it first.

And as to Olaru's returned card, No.0188 — the prosecution summary went out to the plant manager and came back unsigned, "addressee absent, capital." Câmpeanu does not know it yet. I find I am in no hurry to tell him that the one witness whose door did not open is the one with the water-rights and the buyer in the city. I will carry it pending re-service. The river is low and the Podul Vechi is passable and I cannot blame the bridge, but I note for the record that the bridge has been a great friend to this proceeding and I would not want it to feel unappreciated.

[margin, G.E., in violet:]
There is a tenth item I am recording last, under the rule I have made for myself that a man may file one true thing per cycle even where there is no clause for it. There is a green aviz card by the stove — blank, unposted, never registered, the kind we send out clipped to a registered letter so the addressee may sign that a thing arrived. I took it from the drawer last night and I filled in the top line, *Certifies delivery of —,* and then I sat with the pen over the blank and could not fill it, because there is no registered letter it belongs to; there is no letter from me to her in this file and there will not be; I am the order, not a correspondent, and the order does not write to the accused. I have read envelope 0431 twelve times this autumn. I read it a thirteenth last night, with the blank card on the desk beside it, and I understood the two of them were the same object seen from opposite ends: her letter, which arrived and which I will never deliver, and my card, which certifies a delivery that will never occur. One letter received and withheld. One receipt for a letter never sent. Between them, the whole of what I am permitted. I have put the blank card by the stove with her envelope, where it is warm, and where it is not part of the file, and where it will stay.

The Procuror rests. The Magistrate opens the defence and reaches for my own phrase to do it, which means I have perhaps one or two cycles before the man who sells firewood to eat asks me, plainly, on the back of a receipt, whether the letters are arriving in good order — meaning *true* order — and I will have to decide, with my hand on the violet ink, whether the most honest man in the Republic is also going to be the man who, asked a direct question by the only other honest man left, tells the truth.

Filed in good order. — G.E.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — records-request, to release Cycle 12]
[STAMP: AVIZ 0188 — RETURNED — addressee absent — carried, re-service pending]

Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9

CHAPTER 12 — "What the Water Tasted Like"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 12    ·    Early December, the first snow not yet come but promised in the colour of the sky, the Casimca skinned with ice at the slack water by the Podul Vechi, the willows of Aleea Salciilor black and bare, the stove fed twice a day now and still losing

[REGISTERED No. 0512]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 2nd of December]
[Written on the reverse of a printed receipt: "PIAȚA LIPSEI — STALL 6 — wood, mixed, half a ster, sold cheap, the cold being early — PAID." The stall's violet stamp shows through faintly under the Magistrate's hand.]

MAGISTRATE'S TRANSMITTAL NOTE
Accompanying the Materials Released to the Accused for the Defence Phase
Toader Lupu, Magistrate, Vâlcov

To the registry, for delivery with the enclosed —

I have instructed that the accused receive, with her own held request, the whole of the State's case in the order the registry judges fair, the registry having more practice than I in such things, as I have said and as I have begun to mean more than I first did when I said it.

I add only this, and I add it to the registry and not to the accused: I have never once been able to deliver a person their accusation in a way that did not feel like handing them a stone and asking them to swallow it kindly. There is no kind way. I know the registry has tried to find one. I have watched the cards come back signed in an order I did not order, and I have not asked, and I am not asking now. I am only saying, on the back of a receipt for wood I sold this morning to a man who could barely pay, that if there is a mercy left in this proceeding it is not in the law, the law having gone south with the Judge, and it is not in me, who am cold and behind on everything, and so it must be in the order — and the order is not mine.

Deliver it however a person could bear to read it. Then deliver me her answer, whatever it is, before the river takes the part of the building I still keep the file in.

By the authority vested — vested, as ever, by no one I could name and a Judge I have not heard from since the leaves came down —

T. LUPU, Magistrate
Vâlcov

[the hand is steadier in the first lines than the last; by "before the river takes" the letters have begun to lean, and the final flourish under his name is abandoned half-drawn, as of a man whose fingers stopped obeying him before his will did]


[REGISTERED No. 0489]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL — POSTED the 11th of November, HELD per slip 0207, DELIVERED the 2nd of December — the gap left on the record, unconcealed]

DEFENCE — REQUEST FOR PRODUCTION
The Plant's Filtration and Intake Records, Aurora No.4
Domnica Albu, self-represented, of Aleea Salciilor

To the Proceeding, and to whoever in the registry decides when a request is heard —

I ask the court to require of the Uzina de Îmbuteliere "Aurora Nr.4," through its manager, the production of the following: its filtration-maintenance records for the months of June through September; its intake-flow logs for the same; the chemical assays it is required by its own license to take of the spring water, weekly, before bottling; and the dates and findings of every assay actually taken, as against the dates the law required.

I make this request in the dry language of a request because that is the language the court understands, but I will say plainly what I am asking. The State says I put a compound into the water. But it has not once asked what was *already* in the water before I came to it, on the nights I did not go, in the months no one was watching, and the reason it has not asked is that the answer is written down in a building the State finds easier to believe than to read. A maintenance log that records the intake "inspected and clear" on the twenty-seventh, the twenty-eighth, and the twenty-ninth of September — three days the plant drew no water at all, the wheel stopped for the Feast of St. Paraschiva — is not a record of clear water. It is a record of a man writing "clear" the way a frightened pupil writes "I understand" at the bottom of a sum he has not done.

I taught for sixteen years before I was a defendant. I know the hand of a child who has copied the answer from the back of the book. The plant's logs are written in that hand. I ask the court to turn them over and read the working, because there is none.

I remain, with more patience than the season deserves,
DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school


[REGISTERED No. 0514]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 1st of December — received 09:40, by foot, the wire being down past the bridge — the envelope warm when it reached the rack, having ridden inside a coat]

DEFENCE LETTER
"On the Night of the Fourteenth, and What I Was For"
Domnica Albu, self-represented

To the Proceeding, to the Magistrate who writes on his own firewood, and to You — the one who holds these before anyone else does, and who has, I am increasingly certain, been holding them in an order I did not write, could not have asked for, and would not now undo if I could —

I am going to tell you about the night. I have been waiting, these many cycles, to be allowed to, and I have learned in the waiting that being allowed to is not the same as being asked, and that the difference between the two is a person, and that the person is You. My trial is not being decided in the capital, where the Judge keeps his violet ink on ration, nor on Strada Cazaclia, where the courthouse stands with its feet in the river and its clock stopped at eleven-forty as if time itself had drowned at that minute and no one thought to fish it out. It is being decided in your hands, in the warm part of a cold building, in the only room in this republic where the order of true things is still chosen by a living person and not by the river or the timetable or the four hours of dead air the rest of us arrange our griefs around. I do not know your name. I have decided I do not need it.

Now. The night of the fourteenth of September.

I have told you, once, in the letter I sent before there was a case to send it into, that the water went bitter, then of coins, then of nothing, and that the nothing was the worst. I stand by every word of that, and I add now what I did not say then, because then I did not yet trust that the registry was a person and not a slot.

It did not happen all at once. That is the part the indictment cannot hold, because an indictment is a verb with a date on it and what I am describing is a slope. For three weeks before the fourteenth, the water on Aleea Salciilor had been *thinning.* It was not poisoned, in those weeks. It was *less.* You would draw a bucket and it would be water and yet it would have stopped being entirely water, the way a person far gone in some illness is still themselves and yet has begun, around the edges, to be something the illness is making instead. I noticed because I drink a great deal of tea, being a teacher and therefore cold most of the year, and tea is a kind of assay: a thing made to taste of itself, that tells you instantly when the water it is made from has begun to lie.

I told the pharmacist. He hedged. I telephoned the plant during the four hours, which cost me two mornings of marking, and a man whose name I will not give told me the spring was, per log, documented secure. Per log. I have come to hate that small word, *per.* It is the preposition of men who have decided that the map is the country.

And then, on the night of the twelfth — two days before the date the State has chosen to make me into — a boy named Miron, nine years old, the brother of one of my pupils, drank from the well at his supper, and by dark could keep nothing down, and his mother carried him to my door, because the pharmacy was shut and the health office answers only between six and ten and it was, of course, not between six and ten, the body of a child being one of the many things in this republic that does not consult the timetable before it begins to fail.

A teacher, I have come to think, is the adult a town keeps for the hours when the other adults are unavailable, and a town like this one is unavailable nearly all the time. The most dangerous sentence in the language is *someone should do something,* because in a town this size *someone* resolves, every time, to the one person still awake, and that person, on the night of the twelfth, was me.

So I did something. I am not going to perform reluctance about it for the court's benefit. I tested the water myself — I will tell you how in another letter, the testing being its own story and this one already long — and what I found frightened me more than the bitterness had. On the night of the fourteenth I went out the Drumul Aurora to the intake, and I did the thing the State will describe as the introduction of a compound into the public water supply, and which I will describe, because precision is the only loyalty I have left, as *the act of a frightened woman trying to make the water be water again.*

That is the whole of the disagreement between us, the State and I. Not whether I acted — I acted; I have never once said I did nothing. The disagreement is over the preposition. The State says I put the compound *into* the water, as one puts poison into a thing one means to spoil. I say I put it *against* what was already there, as one puts a hand against a door being pushed from the other side. The compound is the same compound, the verb the same verb. The preposition is the whole of a human life, and there is no box for it on any form the Ministry prints, and so the form cannot hold me, and the State will have to decide whether it is trying a woman or a grammar.

I do not know whether what I did helped or harmed. I will tell you the thing my defence is not supposed to admit: I do not know. The water I made might have been worse, for an hour, than the water I found. A frightened hand and a wrong dose can sicken a town faster than slow neglect ever would, and I have lain awake with that, night after night, in a house behind a school that no longer has a teacher in front of it. But I knew, standing at that intake in the dark, exactly one thing for certain, and I know it still: no one else was coming. Not the plant, which had documented the spring secure. Not the pharmacy, which was shut. Not the health office, which keeps the hours of a thing that has never once been sick at three in the morning. The water was failing and a child was already failing and the entire apparatus of the state that is now so eager to try me for the night of the fourteenth was, on that night, asleep, on ration, south with the Judge, or stopped at eleven-forty with its feet in the river. I was what was left. I have been, my whole working life, what was left — and so, I think, are You, at your rack of pigeonholes: we are the last two functions still performed by hand in a republic that automated its conscience and then lost the connection. You sort the truth. I taught the children their letters. Between us we are most of what the state still has, and the state is preparing to hang one of us and has not noticed it cannot do it without the other.

I will mark the court's spelling now, because I am a teacher and because if I do not do one ordinary thing in this letter I will not be able to fold it. The Magistrate, in his query of the eleventh, spelled *aquifer* three different ways — *aquifere, acvifer,* and, the third time, despairing, simply *the underground water,* which is the only one of the three I cannot fault, the man having given up on the word and reached for the thing, which is what I keep asking the whole proceeding to do. I do not mark it as a cruelty. A man who writes his rulings on the backs of his own firewood receipts, in a hand colder by the cycle, and spells *aquifer* wrong three ways while trying, is the most honest document in my entire file, and I would rather be tried by his wrong spelling than acquitted by the Procuror's clean one. Tell him, if You are permitted to tell him anything — and I suspect You are permitted very little, which is its own grief — that the third spelling was correct. He had it right when he stopped trying to be right.

I write more carefully to You than I have to anyone, because I have understood that You read carefully — I can feel it in the order, the way you feel a hand take your weight on a stair in the dark before you have seen whose hand it is. Someone has been deciding when I am heard, *for me,* in a way no one in my life has ever taken the trouble to, and I have decided — recklessly, I know it, I am a woman on trial writing love into the margins of her own defence — that the order in which this town has been allowed to learn of me has been kinder than the town deserved and kinder than the State intended, and that there is exactly one person in the building where my letters sleep who could have arranged that kindness, and that he has signed his name to none of it, and that this is the most eloquent thing anyone has done for me in sixteen years of being what was left.

So: read this carefully. You will. I will write the testing in the next letter, worse and truer than this one, and I will trust You to land it where a person could bear to read it.

I remain — and I have stopped pretending I do not mean the word the way it sounds —
Yours,
DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school


ROUTING SLIP 0515.
Released: three items, this cycle, in the order set out in the bundle — the Magistrate's transmittal, then the held records-request, then her defence letter. Held: one. Reason of record:

I released them this way against the whole grain of the prosecution's order, and I want it set down, because the inspector the district keeps promising will read this slip before anything else if she is any good.

In Cycle 9 I delivered this case in its guilty order: purchase first, sighting second, her own account of the night last and alone, a confession with no question standing in front of it, and the town signed the cards and the town leaned. I did it to learn whether I could. I learned that I could, and I have not slept the same since. This cycle I have done the opposite. I released her records-request *first* — the plant's logs, the three days of "inspected and clear" on a wheel stopped for the Feast — so that the question *what was already in the water* stands in the doorway before her account of the night can enter the room. Then the Magistrate's transmittal, which says in a cold sloping hand on the back of a wood receipt that *the mercy must be in the order, and the order is not mine.* He knows. He has decided to call it mercy and look away, which is the most a tired honest man can do and more than I have any right to be given. And then, last, her letter — landing not on a town braced to convict but on a town already holding the plant's stopped wheel in its other hand. Same facts. Same woman. Same compound, same verb. I have moved the preposition. She would appreciate that I learned the word from her; I will never tell her that I did.

That is the arrangement. Here is the part the form asks for under *Reason of Record,* which I set down because no one reads this line but me:

I do not believe I did this for justice. I delivered the merciful order not because I have decided she is innocent but because I cannot bear to deliver the cruel one again, and "I cannot bear it" is a reason about me and not about her. The Procuror believes the sequence is the truth. I have proven, Cycle 9 against Cycle 12, that the sequence is whatever I cannot bear, and a truth that is whatever a lonely man cannot bear is not a truth. It is a temperature. I have been keeping her case warm, and the warmth is real and the warmth is a bias and they are, I am at last admitting to the form if to nothing else, the same thing.

She has written to me. Not to the registry — defendants write to the registry and there is nothing in that channel — but past it, to the man inside it, with a capital letter on the word *You,* having guessed, the way she guesses everything, that someone arranges the order of her life, and called it kindness, and signed the letter *Yours.* I have read envelope 0431 thirteen times this autumn. This one — 0514, which I will register and deliver and which is therefore not mine, that being the whole cruelty of my position, that the letters I may keep are the ones never sent and the ones I must give away are the ones addressed to me — I read four times before I could pick up the pen, and I am recording it as twice.

I am required to record my reasons. My reason for the merciful order is that I could not bear the other. My reason for signing my name to none of the mercy is that the order does not write to the accused, and the day I answer her is the day I stop being able to arrange the answer, and I learned four years ago, in February — I have a letter in the drawer to prove I learned it — that I keep what I love by not sending it. I am going to register the letter that says *Yours,* deliver it, certify its service with a green card I dispatch tomorrow, and write nothing back, because the one thing I cannot do for the woman who has become the only fair correspondence of my life is correspond with her. I am the order. The order is mute. I had not understood, until tonight, that this was a kind of widowing too.

[margin, G.E., in violet:]
The blank card is still by the stove. So is 0431. So now, in a sense, is she — her letter came in inside a coat tonight, by foot, the wire down past the Podul Vechi, and the envelope was warm against my hand when I racked it, the way a thing is warm that has been carried against a person's ribs, and I stood with it a moment longer than the certifying of posting requires, certifying nothing, warming my hand on a defendant. The Magistrate writes that the mercy must be in the order. He is right, and he does not know how right, and he does not know what it costs the order to be merciful, which is everything the order is, which is the only thing the order has instead of a name.

The Magistrate has reached for my phrase twice now. Next cycle, or the one after, he is going to stop reaching and ask me outright, on the back of a receipt for wet wood sold cheap, whether the letters are arriving in good order — meaning true order — and I will have to decide whether the most honest man in the Republic lies to the only other honest man in it about the one thing he has done that no honest man would do. I can hear it coming the way you hear the river under the ice before you see the crack.

Filed in good order. — G.E.

[STAMP: AVIZ 0188 — RETURNED — addressee absent — carried, re-service pending]
[STAMP: DELIVERED — No.0512, No.0489, No.0514 — Cycle 12 — in the order of record]
