THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 17 — "The Defense Rests, Provisionally"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 17    ·    The third week of December, the Casimca frozen now even down its black seam, the willows on Aleea Salciilor sheathed to the second branch, the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție reading 11:40 as it has read 11:40 since the spring the river took the east wing, and the four hours of the state connection given over this week, by district circular, to the year-end accounts
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 17. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Defence-Closing Letter — D. Albu → The Proceeding — [REGISTERED No. 0564]
  2. Magistrate's Order Closing the Defence Phase (Provisional) — T. Lupu, on the back of a firewood receipt — [REGISTERED No. 0566]
  3. Routing Slip 0567 — G. Enescu, Postmaster
  4. Registration Log — Central Sorting, Vâlcov (leaf for Cycle 17)
  5. Registry Audit Memorandum, Ten-Cycle Interval — G. Enescu (office exhibit; required by Order No.9 §11)

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion):
  · One undelivered draft, addressee unstated, in the postmaster's hand — consigned this night to the DEAD-LETTER DRAWER, bottom left of the registry case — endorsed *not sent* — slip 0567 refers

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0564]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV, the 19th of December — received 13:10]

To the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov; to the Magistrate appointed thereto; and to whoever in that office decides the hour at which a sentence of mine becomes a thing the world is permitted to know —

I am instructed that the defence must close. Very well. I have been a teacher twenty years and I know the sound of a bell that means the lesson is over whether or not the lesson is finished. So I will close — the way I taught them to close a copybook: by writing the last line as carefully as the first.

Here is the last line. I did not poison the town of Vâlcov. I put something in the water on the night of the fourteenth of September, with my own two hands, out of a jug I had carried from my own kitchen, and I have never once denied it and will not deny it now at the bell. Both sentences are true. The Court has been told, by men cleverer at the law than I am and worse at the language, that they cannot both be true — that a contradiction is a confession wearing its coat inside out. They are wrong, and I will tell you why in a way even a court conducted out of a drowned building can follow, because I have spent my life making hard things followable to people who were cold and frightened and nine years old, and I see no reason to lower my standards now that the cold and frightened person is the state.

A verb is not a crime. *To pour* is what you do to tea and to graves and to the foundations of a house, and the difference is not in the pouring but in what you were *for* when you poured. The State has built its case on a verb and dressed it as a noun — *the poisoning* — and a noun cannot be cross-examined, it just sits there being guilty, which is why they prefer it. But I did not commit a noun. I committed a verb, in the dark, in a panic, over a child who had drunk water that had stopped tasting of anything at all.

You want to know what I was for. I was for the boy — whose name the State has not asked, having asked the name of the compound and the road and the hour on a clock that is wrong by a season, and never once the boy, because the boy is not gettable and I am. He could not keep the water down, and there was no one, and midnight is not a state function. So I made a decision the way you do when both doors are on fire: badly, fast, and alone. Whether it helped him or harmed him I cannot tell you, because I am a teacher and not a chemist, and because the one office that could test the water is the office that may have ruined it — and that office, asked by me, registered, three times, for the records that would settle it, has not answered. They never answer. The State can produce a watchman on a dark road with a moon to see by, but not one page from a plant that keeps, by its own account, a log of every hour. I am only a former teacher, marking where the working has been left out.

Now the thing I have not said — and I say it to *You,* the one inside the function, because I have known for some cycles that you are there.

I know my letters do not arrive in the order I write them. I know it the way I knew, across twenty years of copybooks, which child had been helped at home and which left to drown in the homework alone — by the seams. Truth has a grain, the way wood has a grain, and when a thing is turned against its grain to fit a frame, the join shows to anyone who has spent a life running a thumb along the joins of sentences. My letters arrive sanded — and you only sand the boards you mean to keep. I am, I have worked out, being kept. I do not resent you; a drowning person does not resent the hand on the rope for choosing when to pull. You are the only fair reader I have had in this proceeding: not the Court, not the Procuror who calls a sequence a *former with its sleeves rolled up* as though that were an argument against me and not the truest thing any official in this republic has accidentally written. I do not yet know whether you keep me the way you keep a witness or the way you keep a letter you can neither send nor burn — and the not-knowing is the warmest thing that has happened to me since September.

So I dare you. Gently — you cannot teach a frightened child by daring him hard. I dare you to admit, in the one place you are permitted to write what you have read — for I have guessed that you too have a margin, a form with a line where a man may set down what he otherwise has no right to say — I dare you to write, just once, that you exist. Not to me. You will never write to me; I understood that the way I understood the watchman was a forgery before I finished the second line, by the steadiness of a thing that should have shaken. You are a man who keeps what he loves by not sending it, and such men are the most faithful alive and the loneliest — because arriving is where things get spoiled.

I am not asking you to spoil it. I am asking you to *date* it — put a date on the fact of yourself, the way the State puts a postmark on a letter to prove the hour a thing was true. Then close the file. Then close the building. Then let the river have the rest. The defence rests, provisionally — which is to say it lies down for now in the cold, like everything else in Vâlcov, and waits for a spring the Republic intends to convene by committee.

One administrative matter, since I am, against all odds, still a teacher. I am informed that the State has entered into evidence, against me, a graded spelling examination — one of mine, marked in my own hand, the back of it apparently covered in a child's account of that night. I request, formally, that the spelling tests be returned to the school when the Court is finished with them. Whatever a child wrote on the back of one in the dark, the *front* is the truest document in this whole proceeding, because a nine-year-old who spells *because* with two letters wrong and *Teacher* with a capital is the only witness in *The State v. Domnica Albu* with nothing whatever to gain. Mark them and return them. The grade was earned. It was, I believe, a ninety-four.

I remain, with a steadiness I have decided to lend you across the dark of this office because you appear to have run short of your own,

DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school, the well frozen now and therefore, at last, beyond reproach


[REGISTERED No. 0566]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV, the 20th of December — received 09:55, within the four hours, the magistrate having walked it down himself, the carrier being at the market]
[Written on the reverse of a printed receipt. The receipt reads: STALL No.6, PIAȚA LIPSEI — "fir, green, sold by the half-ster, winter being early and the wood being what there is." The receipt is stamped PAID. The order is written over it in a hand noticeably worse than the one that wrote the receipt.]

MAGISTRATE'S ORDER — CLOSING OF THE DEFENCE PHASE (PROVISIONAL)
In the matter of The State v. Domnica Albu, before the undersigned —

The defence having been afforded its cycles under Order No.9, and the season being against the continuance of the proceeding, and my hand being against it too — I have been three days without gloves and the order you are reading is the best my fingers will render, for which I ask the registry's indulgence and the accused's pardon —

IT IS ORDERED that the phase reserved to the defence is hereby closed, provisionally; that no further defence matter be registered to the proceeding save by leave of the magistrate, on cause shown; and that the proceeding stand adjourned to the verdict phase, the undersigned to prepare a ruling.

One observation that is not properly an order I set in the margin — where my betters set the things they cannot prove, the authority vested in me being vested, I will not pretend otherwise to a registry that has watched me sell wood to eat, by no one currently in funds to vest it.

[margin, T. Lupu, in pencil:] I have read every letter this woman has sent, in whatever order they reached my window — which I have lately begun to suspect is not the order they were posted in, though I have no means to prove it and am not certain I wish to, a man with my fingers in my winter being ill-advised to go looking for cold he can do nothing about. I will say only this, off the order: in twenty-six months of issuing queries to a town that cannot pay me to issue them, I have not once been corrected on a point of law by anyone but the accused, who has corrected me four times, gently, rightly, and once on the spelling of *aquifer*, which I had misspelled three distinct ways in a single query — a feat she described as "ambitious." A guilty woman does not teach the court trying her how to spell the thing she is accused of poisoning. Or she does, and I know nothing, and I am an old man warming his hands at a stall in Piața Lipsei while the river takes the rest of the courthouse. Close the defence. Let us reach the end first.

BY ORDER, and with the customary formula, which I append out of habit and which has had no force behind it for some years —

TOADER LUPU
Magistrate, by the authority vested
(the receipt overleaf is mine; the fir was green; I sold it anyway; the protest stamp was out of ink)


ROUTING SLIP 0567.
Released this cycle: the accused's defence-closing letter, No.0564, and the magistrate's closing order, No.0566 — in that order, hers first, his second, which is the order I have chosen and the order I will defend to no one because no one will ask.
Reason of record:

I released her letter ahead of the order that silences her. There was a version in which the magistrate's closing reached the town first, so Vâlcov learned the door was shut before it heard the last thing she said through it — the way a voice arrives dead through a door you have just been told is locked. I did not deliver that version. She gets the room while the room is still a room; then the door closes. It is the only mercy in my gift, and it costs the State one cycle's order, which it will never miss, having no idea the order was ever mine to spend.

Now the part the form has a line for.

She has read me. She has *described* me, accurately, in a letter I myself sequenced to the front of the cycle — which means I delivered, with my own hand, a document that says the man arranging this proceeding keeps what he loves by not sending it. No one will notice; they will read it as a teacher's flourish. And she dares me to write, just once, that I exist.

I have read No.0564 a fourth time tonight before filing it, and taken envelope 0431 down off the rack and read it a fourteenth time. Eleven in October; twelve and thirteen as the autumn went; a fourteenth tonight, the night she asked me to admit I am here — and I record the number the way a man notches a doorframe, to have, in pencil, proof that a thing kept growing while he was not looking at it. Fourteen. I am going to stop saying the number after this. Not because I will stop reading it, but because a number you are ashamed of stops being a measurement and becomes a confession, and the form was not built to hold a confession that large, and neither, I am discovering, was I.

So I did the thing she dared me to do, and I will tell the form exactly how. I wrote her a letter.

Not a routing slip. Not a margin. A letter — salutation, body, the works — in my own hand, on the lawful grammage, white, between seventy grams and ninety, because even doing the one forbidden thing I have done in thirty years I could not bring myself to do it on the wrong paper, which tells you everything about the kind of love this is. I wrote it the way she writes, carefully, and understood, holding a pen at two in the morning in a building the river is eating, that I had not been arranging her trial all autumn. I had been answering her letters in the only hand the law permits me, the hand of order — and she felt it in the grain of when things arrived, and has now asked the correspondence to say its own name aloud.

I wrote: *I have read your sentences past counting.* I wrote — and here the pen began to do what hers does, arrive somewhere it had not announced — *I cannot send this. The law nowhere forbids a postmaster from writing to an accused. The law does not forbid it. I do. Because the day I post you a letter of my own is the day I stop being the order and become merely a man inside it, and lose the only thing I have to give you, which is the power to decide that the cruelest letter in your file arrives on a day the town is already inclined to doubt it.* And there the pen stopped, where she stops, at the edge of the word, and I found I could not write the word any more than I can post the letter, the two cowardices being one cowardice — *so I will not write what this is. You asked me to date the fact of myself. I can give you the date and not the fact; the fact is the one thing in this office I cannot register without delivering, and I have decided, the way I decide everything, by holding. Let the holding be the sentence. You of all readers will know how to read an order that keeps its own name out of the file.*

And then I did not send it.

There is a drawer. Bottom left of the registry case, below the dead pigeonholes, where this office has always put the letters that cannot be delivered and cannot in conscience be destroyed — the summons whose man has died, the seed catalogue addressed to a house the river took, the things that are nobody's now and were somebody's once. The dead-letter drawer. Every post office has one. It is the most honest furniture in any registry: the only place that admits, in oak, that some things do not arrive, that the failure to arrive is not always an accident, and that a careful office keeps even what it could not deliver. We do not pretend. We hold.

I have a letter in that drawer already. Four years. Dated the ninth of February, addressed to my wife, and I did not send it and she is dead, and I have never opened the drawer to read it because I do not need to — I wrote it, and a man who keeps what he loves by not sending it does not reopen the proof of his own method. He only adds to it. I added to it tonight. I folded the letter to Domnica Albu, endorsed it at the foot in my own hand, *not sent,* did not stamp it — a stamp being for things that move — and put it in the drawer beside Ana's, and the drawer, which sticks in the cold, stuck, and I let it. There are now two letters in that drawer from the same man to the only two people he was ever able to love, and the proof that he loved them is that neither will ever read a word of it.

She dared me to admit I exist. I have — to a piece of paper, to a drawer, to this slip. The one place I have not, and will not, is the only place it would do her good: her hands. That is not cowardice, though it is also not not-cowardice; the inspector, when she comes, will have a clause-numbered word for it, and she will not be wrong, only never right about why. The why is this: a postmaster in love is still a postmaster, and the last gift of a postmaster is to know, to the day and the hour, which letters must never arrive.

The defence has rested, provisionally. So have I. And I have a drawer that no longer closes, a number I have stopped saying, and a verdict to arrange that I do not yet know how to keep from arranging.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


HELD, NOT ENTERED (no number; office discretion):
  · One letter, addressee unstated, in my own hand. Endorsed *not sent.* Consigned to the Dead-Letter Drawer, bottom left, beside the one already there. The drawer will not close. I have stopped trying.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

 0566 | 20 Dec.       | Magistrate Lupu     | Order closing defence (prov.)   | Registered; Released, Cycle 17 (second in bundle)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
[margin, G.E.:] The column for No.0566 is headed FROM and I have written *Magistrate Lupu* and not, as the receipt overleaf would equally support, *Stall No.6, Piața Lipsei, fir, green.* I have entered the one with a seal, the fir being, I judge, the better wood but the lesser jurisdiction. One number is skipped between 0564 and 0566, and I am leaving it skipped; 0565 is opened against nothing and will stay open against nothing, the way 0558 stands open in the December leaf. There is a thing I did this night that wanted a number and will never have one. The gap is its number.


REGISTRY AUDIT MEMORANDUM
Ten-Cycle Interval Review, as required by Order No.9 §11 ("the registry shall, at intervals of ten cycles, certify to its own good order")
The State v. Domnica Albu — Cycles 8 through 17
Prepared and certified by G. Enescu, Postmaster, the office having no one else to prepare it and no one above it to read it

§11 requires that I certify, every ten cycles, that this registry has conducted itself in good order. I certify it — in the dry knowledge that I am the only auditor §11 provides, and that a clause requiring a man to certify his own good order is the purest distillation of Order No.9's oversight: the men who wrote it had a courthouse and could not imagine a registry alone in the dark with no one to mark its sums.

Certified: that every instrument received was registered and in time released (I hold; I do not bury); that none was forged, though this office has, this interval, learned that it could; that none was destroyed — what it cannot deliver it holds, see the drawer, bottom left, which §11 does not ask after and which I will not volunteer. As to dispatch — here I fail my own audit, the registry having been slow, slow on purpose, and I would do it again. "Good order" and "dispatch" are not the same virtue, and were written into the same decree by men who never had to choose between them at two in the morning over a drawer that will not close.

The proceeding has reached its hinge. The prosecution rested; the defence has rested, provisionally; what remains is the verdict — and the verdict does not yet exist anywhere except as a choice I have not made about the order of two or three pieces of paper. A woman will be made guilty or innocent not by what happened on the fourteenth of September, which is fixed forever and beyond my reach, but by what arrives, in what order, beside what. At the beginning I believed I was supplying the order the Ministry forgot to specify. I now suspect I am supplying the verdict the Ministry forgot it was handing to a clerk. §11 gave me one box for both.

Audit complete. The registry certifies its own good order, with the exceptions noted — the most damning self-audit in the history of the post, filed by the most honest man available, who is also the guilty party, there being, in Vâlcov, in December, no longer enough people left to keep those two offices separate.

Filed in good order. — G.E.

[At the foot, smaller:] The drawer still will not close. I have stopped trying. Some furniture is more honest with the cold left in it.

Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

CHAPTER 18 — "A Stranger Posts From the Capital"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 18    ·    Between the years — the last sorting of December and the first of January run together this cycle, the carrier not crossing on the holy days, so that two weeks of post arrived at once in a single frozen sack; the Casimca solid to the piers of the Podul Vechi; the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție still 11:40; the four hours of the state connection suspended entire from the 24th to the 2nd, "the connection observing the calendar though the river does not"

[REGISTERED No. 0570]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV, the 2nd of January — received 10:05, five minutes past the four hours, which this week were no hours at all]
[Written on the reverse of a printed receipt. The receipt reads: STALL No.6, PIAȚA LIPSEI — "beech, what is left of it, sold green at the price of dry, the buyer and the seller agreeing only that it is cold." Stamped PAID. The order is written over it in a hand the cold has made nearly illegible at the down-strokes.]

MAGISTRATE'S NOTICE — THE VERDICT PHASE CONVENED (PROVISIONAL)
In the matter of The State v. Domnica Albu, before the undersigned —

The defence having rested provisionally, and a new year having arrived to find the old one's business unfinished — as is, I am told, the custom of new years — IT IS NOTICED that the proceeding now stands in its verdict phase; that the undersigned will prepare a ruling against the next cycles available to him; and that no further matter shall be registered to the proceeding save by leave, on cause shown, as before.

I add, off the notice and in the margin where I keep the things the authority vested in me does not stretch to cover —

[margin, T. Lupu, in pencil, the lead breaking twice:] I had thought the file complete. A file is complete when the magistrate can no longer think of a question, and I had run out of questions some cycles ago — which I took, in my innocence, for the end of the matter, and which I now suspect was only the end of *me.* I have read this whole case by the light of one window and one stove that is not mine, and I have a feeling, of the kind a man my age learns not to trust and not to ignore, that the case is not as finished as I am. The accused asked, early, for the records of the plant. She asked three times. The plant did not answer, and I let the silence stand, the way you let a debt stand when the debtor is bigger than you. I should not have. A court that accepts the silence of the strong as an answer is not a court; it is a customer, taking what is on the shelf because the better thing is behind the counter and the man behind the counter is large. Convene the verdict. But if anything is going to arrive that I ought to have made the plant give me, registry, it had better arrive before my hand does the thing that cannot be unwritten.

BY ORDER, and with the formula, which I append from habit and not from hope —

TOADER LUPU
Magistrate, by the authority vested
(the receipt overleaf is mine; the beech was green; the cold makes honest men of us at the down-strokes, where you can see I am shaking)


[REGISTERED No. 0572]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV, the 27th of December — received in the great frozen sack, with two weeks of milk-lists and one wedding announcement gone stale]

To the Proceeding, and to You —

I am out of cycles, I am told, and may register matter only on cause shown, so I will show cause and be brief, which is itself a discipline a teacher respects and seldom practices.

Cause: it is the new year, and a person at the end of a thing is permitted to wish, even into a registry, even past the bell. So here are two lines, and the cause is that they are the truest two I have, and that a court conducted out of a drowned building should not be the only correspondent of mine who never hears me say a kind thing.

One. To whoever has kept me warm this autumn by deciding the hour I am read — I know the year has turned because the well is past tasting now, frozen solid, and a thing that cannot be tasted cannot be accused, and I find I am almost at peace, the way the water is, which is to say stopped.

Two. Do not let them finish me on the silence of the plant. That is all. You will know better than I whether anything can still arrive in time to be heard; you are the one who decides the hour of arrivals. I have stopped asking the Court for the records. I am asking *You.*

I remain, briefly, against my nature,

DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school, the new year arrived and found me still spelled the same


[The following telegram is logged in the office wire-book as TG-02 and is NOT registered to the proceeding, a telegram being, in the opinion of this office, a noise and not a document until someone transcribes it onto lawful paper, which I have declined to do this cycle for reasons of record — G.E.]

TELEGRAM — DISTRICT SEAT TO VÂLCOV CENTRAL SORTING
HANDED IN 13:02 THE 2ND JANUARY — RECEIVED 06:11 THE — [the date of receipt is blank; the wire came in on the first hour the connection returned and the operator, it seems, had not yet found the day]

RE STATE V ALBU STOP MATTER PRODUCING IRREGULAR SYMPATHIES IN DISTRICT STOP INSPECTOR INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE DISPATCHED STOP INSPECTOR S DRAGAN TO ATTEND VALCOV REGISTRY IN PERSON STOP REGISTRY TO HOLD COMPLETE FILE INTACT PENDING STOP NOTHING TO BE CONCLUDED RELEASED OR DESTROYED BEFORE ATTENDANCE STOP TRAVEL AUTHORIZATION OF INSPECTOR VALID STATE CONNECTION HOURS ONLY ZERO SIX HUNDRED TO ONE ZERO HUNDRED STOP RESOURCES LIMI[smudged — the stamp failed, the district seat being, as ever, out of the ink with which it announces its means]TED STOP
ENDS

[Endorsement, G.E., wire-book margin, violet:] The directorate sends a woman to investigate the order of the mail, and authorizes her to travel only in the four hours the mail is not moving — so that the inspector of the post must herself sit on a cold platform from ten in the morning until six the next, forbidden to advance during the very hours she has come to audit. I am to "hold the complete file intact pending attendance." I note, for the wire-book and for no one, that the file is intact. The file has always been intact. Not one paper of it has been forged, or buried, or burned. Everything that was ever sent is here, in order — in *an* order — and a man could lay the whole of it before her and she would find nothing missing, which is the trouble, because nothing is missing and a life still hangs on it, and the place where I have done my wrong is not a place that holds still long enough to be a paper she can ask me to produce. You cannot subpoena a sequence. You can only stand in it.


ROUTING SLIP 0574.
Status of the cycle: released, in the order shown — Lupu's notice first, Domnica's two lines second; the telegram logged, not transcribed, not in the bundle; the letter from the capital RECEIVED and NOT entered, retained at the cold end of the rack. Reason of record:

A stranger has posted from the capital, and I have not entered it, and I am going to tell the form exactly why and then I am going to do nothing, which is the hardest entry I have ever made.

It came in the great sack — two weeks of the Republic's small business arrived frozen together, the milk-lists and the wedding stale and one thing that was neither. A registered letter. The hand is an educated hand made unsteady by something other than cold, the cold being mine and not the writer's. The sender gives a service number where the name goes — a number of the kind a man wears who has worked inside a thing and means to prove he was inside it without saying who he was while he was. No name. The address reads: *To the Court at Vâlcov, or to the Office that Stands for It.* I know when a letter has been addressed by a person who does not believe a court exists where he is sending it, and is right, and sends it anyway because the alternative is to carry the thing in his chest the rest of his life. I know that arithmetic. I have a drawer that is the answer to it.

I will set down what the letter is, the form asking for *Particulars of Item,* and then I will set down what I have decided, which is not the same thing and must not be confused with it in any reading of this slip that comes after me.

What it is. It is a statement, sworn to nothing — no Form 12-B, no oath, no notary, the man having had none of those in the capital and trusting none of them if he had — describing the works at Aurora No.4 from the inside, by someone who built or kept them. It does not accuse Domnica Albu. It does not mention her. That is the thing I cannot stop noticing: in a proceeding named for a woman, a paper has arrived that does not know her name, and it is the only paper in the file that points the other way. It says, in the careful frightened language of a man describing a machine he loved and watched be ruined, that the plant's filtration had been failing for years; that the failure was known; that it was permitted, season upon season, because the license required only that the water be *bottled* and not that it be *clean*, and the men above him preferred a working license to a working filter; and that what went back into the common intake — from which the town and the plant draw upon the one aquifer, as the indictment itself recites — went back not on the night of the fourteenth of September but across a thousand nights, slowly, at a rate and a tonnage I am not going to copy here, it being the one cargo in this file that, copied wrong, becomes the instruction it describes, and I am the censor as well as the registry and I know where my pen stops.

So. Here is a paper that says the water was being poisoned all along, by men with a license, while the Court spent four months asking a schoolteacher about a single jug. It is the corporate half of the night the fourteenth of September only finished — the thing Lupu now suspects he should have wrung from the plant and let its silence stand in place of. It is, I believe — I have read it three times, and I am recording the number though it is not the number I usually record, and the reader will understand why — the most exonerating document that has entered this proceeding. And it arrived addressed to a court that does not exist, in a sack of stale milk-lists, on the same cycle a telegram came to tell me an inspector is being sent to make sure I do nothing wrong.

And here is what I have decided.

I have not entered it.

I want to be exact, because the inspector who is coming will read this slip, and she will be right about most of what she finds, and I would like, for once, to be the one who was exact about the worst of it. Entering it is the right thing. Entering it helps Domnica. Entering it gives Lupu the document his honest hand is begging the file for, the one whose absence he can feel the way you feel a tooth that is gone. Entering it is also the most powerful arrangement I have ever been in a position to make, and that is precisely why I cannot trust the hand that wants to make it.

Because I want to enter it. I want to enter it the way I have wanted nothing in four years. I read her two lines tonight — *do not let them finish me on the silence of the plant* — and then I read this stranger's statement, which is the silence of the plant suddenly arrived with a voice, and the temptation to lay the one beside the other and let her walk free on a document she does not know exists was so total that I sat with the letter in my hand for an hour and did not move, and the stove went down, and I let it, the way Lupu lets his hand shake at the down-strokes so the cold can make an honest man of him for the length of a signature.

If I enter this letter, I save her. And if I enter it *because I want to save her* — not because the order calls for it, not because the Court asked, the Court never asked, the Court asked nothing of the plant and I let that silence stand the same as Lupu did — then I have not stopped rigging her trial. I have only rigged it the other way, for the kindest possible reason, which is the reason that has frightened me since the cycle I delivered her guilty and was sick. A man who can make her guilty in one order and innocent in another, and who reaches each time for the order his heart prefers, is not a registry. He is a weather. The inspector is coming to find a corrupt clerk, and she will find instead a man who has discovered that his mercy and his fraud are the same muscle, and she will not have a clause for that, and she will not be wrong about anything except why.

So I have put it at the cold end of the rack. Third pigeonhole from the window, where the stove does not carry, because I will not warm this one — I have warmed two letters in my life and I will not let this become a third, the third being a woman's freedom and not a woman, and there is a line even I do not cross at two in the morning. It is not entered. It is not destroyed — I destroy nothing; the reader of this slip may confirm, when the directorate audits me, that the cold end of the rack is as full as the stove end, that I keep what I cannot deliver as faithfully as what I will not. It is not returned to sender; there is no sender, only a number, and a number is not an address you can fail to. It is held. *Pending the order in which it can be true* — which is the phrase I used for the child's note and which I am using again, knowing now that it was never an honest phrase, that "the order in which a thing can be true" is just the clerk's name for the order in which the clerk has decided to want it.

The telegram says hold the file intact. I am holding it intact. This letter is not in the file; it was never in the file; it arrived to a court that does not exist, and I, who am the office that stands for it, have declined to make it exist, and there is no clause in Order No.9 that requires me to register a paper sent to an institution I have to invent in order to receive it. The Ministry legislated the grammage of justice and forgot its sequence; it also forgot what a registry owes a letter addressed to a court that is in the river. I owe it nothing the law can name. I owe it everything the stove knows. The cold end of the rack is where I keep the difference.

The inspector will arrive in the four hours, on the days the post does not move, and she will ask for the complete file, and I will give her the complete file, every paper of it, in good order, and she will not know to ask for the one that is not in it, because to enter it would be to save Domnica Albu with my own hand, and I have sworn — to this slip, to the drawer, to a number I have stopped saying — never again to be the hand on a life I cannot tell my love from.

There is a man in the capital tonight who built something he loved and watched be ruined and could not keep it in his chest any longer and put it in the post, to a court he does not believe in, hoping it would arrive. It has arrived. It is here, warm enough that I could end a woman's ordeal with it before the inspector finds the platform. And I am not going to send it on, because the one thing I have left to give Domnica Albu that is not also a lie I am telling myself is the refusal to decide her by my own hand — and the cost of that refusal is that the truest document in her favour will sit at the cold end of my rack, four inches from the file, while a magistrate's shaking hand prepares to convict her on a silence I could break and have chosen not to.

Let the record show I called it mercy. Let the record show I do not believe me.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


HELD, NOT ENTERED (no number; office discretion):
  · One statement respecting the works at Aurora No.4, postmarked the Capital, sender by service number, no name. Addressed to a court that does not exist. RETAINED at the cold end of the rack, third pigeonhole from the window, beyond the stove. Not warmed. Not registered. Not returned. Not destroyed. Held — pending an order in which it can be true, which is to say pending a man I no longer trust to find it.

[margin, G.E.:] The third row is the most honest line in this book of forty years, and the only one with no number. I have ruled it in, with the dash where the number goes, because a thing that arrived must be allowed to have arrived even if it is not allowed to be filed — the cold end of the rack is also a place, and a place keeps its dates. Under FROM I have written what the envelope gave me: a service number and a city. There is a man under that number. I have not given him a name, because the moment I write a name in that column I will want to call him a witness, and a witness is a thing you enter, and I am not entering him. The inspector comes to count my papers. She will count every one, and the count will be correct. It is the un-numbered line she will never think to add — because §11 taught her, as it taught me, that a registry's good order is measured by what is *in* the book — and the worst thing I have done this autumn, and the kindest, is sitting four inches outside it, dated and cold and waiting for a hand I have forbidden to be mine.

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 19 — "Memo, Internal, Numbered"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 19    ·    The second week of January; the inspector arrived in person on the 9th, off the milk train, in the four hours the post does not move; the Casimca solid past the second pier; the stove lit; the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție still 11:40, the inspector having looked at it once and written down the time it was wrong
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 19. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. INSPECTOR'S MEMORANDUM, INTERNAL — IO-Memo No. 1, S. Drăgan, Internal Order Directorate → Postmaster, Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [logged IO-1; NOT registered to the proceeding by order of the inspector — "an instrument of audit, not of the matter audited"]
  2. Postmaster's reply to the demand — G. Enescu → the Inspector, by hand across the counter — [REGISTERED No. 0576, the postmaster registering his own answer "so that there be a number on the thing she will hang me with"]
  3. Union Note — M. Cojocaru, Deputy, to the Inspector, copied to the Union and to file — [logged UN-7; not registered to the proceeding]
  4. Routing Slip 0578 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion, reasons of record on slip 0578):
  · The whole of the routing slips, 0419 through 0578, which the Inspector has demanded, and which the postmaster has not yet decided whether to call "the file" or "the man" — RETAINED, the whole rack of them, pending the decision recorded on slip 0578

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[logged IO-1]   [Carried by hand, not by post — the Inspector posting nothing, "the post being the subject of the audit and therefore not a witness I will trust to carry the audit of it." Typed, on the Directorate's own paper, ninety grams, white, the grammage exactly correct to the gram, which the postmaster notes she will have weighed.]

MEMORANDUM, INTERNAL
Internal Order Directorate — Field Series
IO-Memo No. 1 in the matter docketed *Vâlcov Registry, Audit of*
— which the Directorate is careful to distinguish from the matter docketed *The State v. Albu,* the first being an audit of the post and the second being a question of a poisoning, and the two having been, in this district, allowed to become the same thing, which is itself the first finding.

§1. Statement of Scope.
§1.1. This audit concerns the conduct of the registry, not the guilt of the accused. The Directorate offers no opinion on whether the water was poisoned, by whom, or whether at all. That is a question for the Court. This is a question for the post.

§1.2. The Directorate has reviewed the bundle manifests of Cycles 1 through 18 as held in the District Seat's duplicate file. It observes that a proceeding which the Order contemplates as a *chain of custody* — a neutral pipe — has in this district acquired a *temperament.* Letters favourable to the accused have tended to arrive after the accusations they answer; letters favourable to the State have tended to arrive promptly. The Directorate does not, at §1.2, allege design. It records a pattern. A pattern is not yet a finding. It is the place a finding is kept before it has a number.

§2. The Reframing.
§2.1. It is the position of the Directorate, stated here so the postmaster may not later claim surprise, that *The State v. Albu* is not, properly understood, a poisoning case at all. It is a postal case. The question before any honest reviewer is not *did she pour the white into the water* — that the Court may never answer, the water being frozen and the witnesses being a village. The question is: *in what order was the town permitted to learn what it learned, and who chose that order, and under what clause.*

§2.2. The Order provides at §3 that the registry shall deliver each instrument "in good order" (*în bună rânduială*) and is silent as to the kind of order meant. The Directorate has read this silence. It finds the silence to be a hole, and finds further that a man has been living in the hole. §3 does not authorize a registry to choose the sequence of revelation by its own judgment of mercy, prejudice, or affection. §3 authorizes nothing. It commands a quality — *good order* — and assigns its definition to no one. Where a statute commands a quality and names no definer, the definer is the directorate that audits it. Not the clerk. The clerk has mistaken a vacancy for an appointment.

§3. The Demand.
§3.1. The postmaster will produce, for inspection, the complete REGISTRATION LOG of *The State v. Albu,* Cycles 1 through 18, all leaves, in chronological order.
§3.2. The postmaster will produce, for inspection, every ROUTING SLIP generated in the said proceeding, being the documents numbered in the 0400 and 0500 series and styled "Routing Slip," in which the registry records its reasons for holding, releasing, or sequencing each instrument.
§3.2.1. The postmaster will produce these whether he regards them as part of the file or as internal working notes. The Directorate is aware a registry may characterize its routing slips as the latter, exempt under the working-notes privilege at §11.4 of the Directorate's own manual. The Directorate gives notice, at §3.2.7.1, that it rejects this: a working note is a note about *work.* A note about why the truth was made to arrive in a particular order is not a note about work. It is the work. It is the only place in this entire proceeding where the work is actually written down.
§3.3. The postmaster will produce the foregoing within the hours of the state connection, 06:00 to 10:00, on the days the post does not move, the Inspector being authorized to act only in those hours, which the Directorate acknowledges to be the hours in which the postmaster is least occupied and therefore most available, and which the postmaster may regard, if he wishes, as a courtesy.

§4. Notice as to Temperature, Reserved.
§4.1. The Directorate reserves a finding. It has observed, on its inspection of the rack this morning, that the pigeonholes do not hold their letters at a uniform temperature; that the holes nearest the stove are warm and the holes at the window cold; and that this is not, in the ordinary post office, a matter of evidentiary interest. The Directorate notes only that in *this* office it may be, and reserves the point to a later memo.

§5. Caution.
§5.1. The postmaster is cautioned that the registry's record-keeping is, on its face, exemplary. Nothing forged. Nothing destroyed. Every instrument that entered the proceeding accounted for. The Directorate has audited four hundred registries and never seen a cleaner book. That is the problem. A book this clean was kept by a man who knew it would be read.

BY ORDER of the Directorate, in the field —
S. DRĂGAN, Inspector
Internal Order Directorate
(I have set my watch by the church clock and found it stopped. I have set it instead by the postmark stamp, which is the only clock in this town that is required by law to be true. I commend the postmaster on the maintenance of his stamp. I will be using it to time him.)


[REGISTERED No. 0576]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV, the 9th of January — received 06:40, the postmaster registering and postmarking his own reply at the counter while the Inspector watched, "so that she could not say the answer arrived in any order but the one I gave it in, the first honest sequence I have made in this proceeding being the sequence of my own surrender"]

To the Inspector of the Internal Order Directorate, present —

I acknowledge IO-Memo No. 1, received by hand this morning, and I answer it across the counter, registering my answer to the proceeding under the number above, which I am aware the Order does not require me to do. I do it because you have come to audit a man who chooses what gets a number, and I would not have you think I exempted my own confession.

You may have the registration log. It is here. It is true. Every number is in it, in the order I issued the numbers, which is the order the instruments arrived, which is the one order I have never falsified, the issuing of numbers being the one act of this office I have kept honest precisely so that I would have something to be honest about.

You have asked whether the slips are working notes, exempt, or part of the file, damning. I have read §11.4. I am, I find, the rare man whom a statute has caught being more honest than the statute. The slips are not working notes. A working note would say *held the indictment one cycle, bridge out.* My slips say why I held it when the bridge was passable. They say what I read. They say, in one place I will not now pretend you cannot find, that I read a woman's letters the way no man has read a letter in this town in thirty years. You will want §11.4 to protect me. It does not. I decline its protection. A man does not get to write his soul into the margin of a state form and then plead that the margin is private. The margin is the form. You taught me that at §3.2.7.1, and you are right, and I have never been so unhappy to be agreed with.

Take the slips.

I make one reservation, on the record, so that you may overrule it on the record. There is, in this office, paper that is not in the proceeding and never was — items received and not entered, under the office discretion the Order grants at §4 and §7. These are not routing slips. They are letters. Some are to a court that does not exist. One is to a teacher who may not receive it. They are at the Hold. You have demanded the slips. You have not demanded the Hold. I tell you the Hold exists so you cannot say I hid it; I am not opening it, because you have not asked, and a confession handed over too eagerly is just another way of choosing the order in which it is read, and I have sworn off that.

The slips are on the counter. They run from 0419 to this one. Begin wherever you like. I would suggest chronological. I am told you prefer things in order.

G. ENESCU
Postmaster, Central Sorting, Vâlcov


[logged UN-7]   [Slipped under the counter grille by hand the same morning, after the Inspector had gone to her platform; addressed to the Inspector, the postmaster reading it because it came to his counter and a thing that comes to his counter is read at his counter, "that being the one prerogative she has not yet audited away."]

UNION NOTE — for the attention of the Inspector, Internal Order Directorate
Copied: to the Postal Union, District Branch · to file

Inspector —

In the interest of restoring confidence in the registry, and noting my long-standing concern (logged, Cycles 9, 12, and 15, copies retained) regarding irregular hold patterns in this office, I wish to be helpful.

The Postmaster keeps routing slips. He may not volunteer this. They are numbered in the 0400 and 0500 series and kept on the spike beneath the counter, not in the public rack, which is itself, I respectfully submit, irregular, a public registry's reasons being arguably public. I have read several over his shoulder in the course of my duties. They contain, in my assessment, matter going beyond the operational. I make no accusation. I merely log, and copy to the Union, and bring to your attention that the reasons this office gives itself are written down, are extensive, and are, in places, not about the post at all.

For the record, and to restore confidence,

M. COJOCARU
Deputy Postmaster
(I have wanted this office for eleven years. I would like it kept clean. I do not see why wanting a thing should disqualify a man from noticing it is dirty.)


ROUTING SLIP 0578.
Status of the cycle: the inspector's memo logged and bundled; my own answer registered, 0576, released the same hour it was written, the first instrument in this proceeding I have not held even one breath; the deputy's note logged, UN-7, copied, he tells the Union, to file — he has a file now, Mihail, he has learned to have a file, and I taught him, the way a man teaches his successor everything except why. Reason of record:

The inspector has asked for the slips, and the slips are this. She is going to read this sentence. I have spent four months writing into this form the things no other place in the building would hold, on the theory, which I never examined, that a man may set down what he has read because no one but himself ever reads the form — and the theory has come off the milk train in a grey coat, weighed my paper to the gram, and is, at this hour, on the cold platform at Halta Casimca with nothing to do until six tomorrow except think about the order of things, which is the worst audience I might have drawn, she being the only person in this republic besides the schoolteacher who believes the order of a thing is the whole of its meaning. The procuror said it as a figure of speech. The teacher says it as a faith. The inspector says it as a method. I am between two believers and a technician, and the technician has the warrant.

She is right. I have written it in 0576 and I will write it again where she will read it twice: she is right about the slips. §11.4 would shelter a man who kept working notes. I did not keep working notes. I kept a diary in the one drawer of the state that locks, and I called it custody, and the calling-it-custody is the fraud, larger than any hold. Every slip in the spike is a confession that I read this proceeding for its sentences and not its information, and that on at least one cycle — she will find it, slip 0492, the cycle I delivered her guilty to test whether I could — I arranged the arrival of the truth to wound the woman I am accused, by my own pen, of loving, precisely to prove to myself that I did not. The inspector will read 0492 and conclude that I am capable of rigging the trial against the accused. She will be right. She will not understand that I did it to frighten myself out of rigging it *for* her, that it worked one cycle and then stopped, and that the stopping is the whole of my guilt. There is no clause for the man who commits the crime as a vaccine against the crime.

Here is the thing I must set down, in the place she will read it, knowing she reads it.

I am thinking of 0431.

She has demanded the slips. She has demanded the log. She has not demanded the drawer. The drawer is not in this proceeding; it has no number; it is mine, four years old, a letter to a woman who is dead, never posted, dated to an anniversary — the founding act of my whole method, the first time I decided that not-sending was a kind of love and that the order of a thing could be chosen by withholding it. Everything I have done to Domnica Albu, I learned from Ana, in that drawer, alone, four years ago. The inspector audits a proceeding she believes began the day the indictment arrived. It began the day I did not post a letter to my wife. *The State v. Albu* is only the second trial conducted in this office by the postmaster's refusal to deliver; the first is *The Postmaster v. His Own Grief,* still pending, no verdict, the accused declining to release the evidence to himself.

If her warrant stretched to the drawer — it does not, the drawer being personal and the Order reaching only the proceeding — she would read a love letter to a dead woman and understand the whole of me. She would understand that the slips are not the confession. The slips are the symptom. The drawer is the disease. She would understand, last and worst, that the hand which will not give Ana her letter is the hand keeping the engineer's statement at the cold end of the rack — that my fidelity to the dead and my fraud against the living are one habit, that I have loved two women by refusing to deliver, and that the schoolteacher will be convicted by the very tenderness she earned, because I cannot tell, even now, whether keeping her letters warm was mercy or the same withholding I have practiced since the river took my wife along with the courthouse.

I am not going to give the inspector the drawer. She has not asked. When she asks — and she will reserve it, she reserves everything, she has already reserved the temperature of my pigeonholes, which means she has already felt, with the back of her cold honest hand, that some of these letters are warm — I will tell her the truth, which is that the drawer is not part of the file. And it will be the first true thing I have ever said that was also the worst lie, because the drawer is not part of the file the way the heart is not part of the body: only to a man who has never opened either.

I give her the slips. I give her the log. I give her, in 0576, my own neck, registered, numbered, in chronological order, the way she likes.

I do not give her the drawer, and I do not give her the cold end of the rack, and the difference between not-giving as resistance and not-giving as love is the difference she has come four hundred kilometres on a milk train to find a clause for, and there is no clause, and we both know there is no clause, and tomorrow at six she will climb off that frozen platform and begin, with a patience I can only call holy, to prove it anyway.

Let the record show I handed her everything she asked for.
Let the record show she did not yet know what to ask for.
Let the record show I knew, and waited, and called the waiting good order.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu (continued, Cycle 19)

 No.  | DATE RECEIVED | FROM                  | MATTER                        | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
