[margin, G.E.:] Three rows, and the only one with a number is the one against myself. I have registered my own surrender and logged everyone else's move against me without a number, and the asymmetry is the truest portrait of the office I have ever drawn: the registry numbers only what the registrar confesses, and leaves the world's accusations un-numbered at the margin. The inspector will fix this. The inspector numbers everything. She will give the memo a number, the note a number, the slips a number, and when she is done this book will be, for the first time in forty years, complete — every reason filed, every margin ruled into a column, every warm thing weighed cold — and it will convict the man who kept it honest enough to be convicted by. I taught Mihail to have a file. I did not teach him what a file is for. I am about to be taught it myself, by a woman with a stopped-clock's patience and a postmark's idea of mercy, beginning tomorrow, at six, when the order returns.


══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════


THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 20 — "What the Inspector Found Warm"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 20    ·    The third week of January; the Inspector returned off the milk train on the 11th, the Casimca solid now past the third pier; the stove drawing badly, the chimney wanting sweeping and no sweep in the district since the autumn; the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție still 11:40, which the Inspector has now recorded on three separate days at three separate true times, "to establish that the clock is reliably wrong, a reliability the registry should study"
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 20. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. INSPECTOR'S MEMORANDUM, INTERNAL — IO-Memo No. 2, S. Drăgan, Internal Order Directorate → Postmaster, Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [logged IO-2; NOT registered to the proceeding, "an instrument of audit"]
  2. Postmaster's reply, registered against himself — G. Enescu → the Inspector, by hand — [REGISTERED No. 0581]
  3. Defence Letter (Domnica Albu) — "On the Subject of Warmth, Which the Court Has Apparently Made Admissible" — [REGISTERED No. 0583]
  4. Routing Slip 0585 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion, reasons of record on slip 0585):
  · The Inspector's annex sheet — a hand-ruled column headed TEMPERATURE, taken with a dairy thermometer borrowed from the milk train, listing each pigeonhole and its reading — appended to IO-2 but addressed to the postmaster personally, "not yet a finding, an observation taking a finding's temperature" — RETAINED, cold end of the rack, beside the engineer's statement

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[logged IO-2]   [Carried by hand. Typed, the Directorate's own paper, ninety grams, white. The postmaster notes the Inspector this cycle has also brought her own thermometer, "a thing I have audited four hundred registries without once requiring, and require here."]

MEMORANDUM, INTERNAL
Internal Order Directorate — Field Series
IO-Memo No. 2 in the matter docketed *Vâlcov Registry, Audit of*

§1. Recall of the Reservation.
§1.1. By IO-Memo No. 1, §4, the Directorate reserved a finding "as to temperature." It now makes it. The Directorate does not, as a rule, weigh the heat of paper. It is weighing it here because in this office the heat of paper has been made to mean something, and a thing made to mean something is, by the meaning's own admission, evidence.

§2. The Method, So It Cannot Be Called Intuition.
§2.1. On the mornings of the 11th, 12th, and 13th, in the state hours when the post does not move, the Directorate took the temperature of each of the forty-one pigeonholes in the public rack and of the nine slots beneath the counter, with a calibrated dairy thermometer, before the postmaster lit the stove and again two hours after. The readings are annexed. A thermometer is an absurd instrument to bring to a poisoning trial. The Directorate brought it because the postmaster's own routing slips, which it now holds, repeatedly use the word *warm* of certain letters and the word *cold* of others, and a directorate handed a man's private thermometer in the form of his vocabulary is obliged to bring a real one and check his readings.

§3. The Finding.
§3.1. The rack does not warm evenly, the stove being at the west wall, and this alone would explain nothing. But the postmaster does not file by position. He files by case, and the system, reconstructed from the slips and the residual heat together, is this: matter favourable to the accused is filed at the west, near the stove, and handled — held in the hand, in one slip "kept by me overnight against the cold" — before release; matter favourable to the State is filed at the east, by the window, and released promptly and cold. The Directorate measured a defence letter four degrees above the ambient of the room four hours after the stove had gone out. Paper does not hold heat four hours. A hand holds heat. The paper had been held.

§3.2. The Directorate states the finding without ornament, the postmaster having a weakness for ornament which it does not share. *The registrar warms the letters he favours.* A bias that shows in the *sequence* of delivery is a procedural irregularity. A bias that shows in the *temperature* of the paper is something the manual has no clause for — and it has read the manual twice this week looking, and there is no clause, the men who wrote it not having imagined a registrar who would warm one party's letters like a man warming a child's hands.

§4. The Reframing, Continued.
§4.1. IO-Memo No. 1 found that *The State v. Albu* is a postal case, not a poisoning case. IO-Memo No. 2 refines it. It is a case about a registrar who has formed an attachment to one of the two parties, and expressed it in the only medium available to a man forbidden to send anything of his own: the *handling* of her paper. He cannot write to her. So he warms what she writes. The Directorate uses the word *attachment*, which is a postal word — a thing affixed to a letter and carried with it — and lets the postmaster supply the other word himself.

§5. Notice as to the Annex.
§5.1. The annexed temperature sheet is addressed to the postmaster personally and is not registered to the proceeding — the auditor warming, as it were, one sheet by addressing it to the man instead of the file. The Directorate notes the irregularity against itself, so the postmaster may not say the auditor was colder than her subject. The auditor was not. The auditor was merely correct about the temperature.

§6. Recommendation, Interim.
§6.1. The Directorate recommends, pending its final memorandum, that the registry maintain a uniform ambient temperature for all evidence, and that the warming-shelf be cleared of all matter belonging to the proceeding.
§6.2. The Directorate acknowledges, having inspected the building, that the stove is the only source of heat in it, that the alternative to a warmed defence is not an unwarmed defence but an unheated registry, and that the postmaster may regard §6.1 as a recommendation that everyone in Vâlcov freeze at the same rate — which the Directorate would accept as a fair characterization and would still recommend, equality of cold being a kind of justice and the only kind this district can presently afford.

BY ORDER of the Directorate, in the field —
S. DRĂGAN, Inspector
(I have set my watch again by your postmark stamp, the church clock remaining wrong. I observe that you stamp the State's mail at arm's length and the accused's mail close to your chest, where the coat is warm. I do not log this in the memo. I log it here, where you will read it, so that you know I saw it with the eye and not only the thermometer, and so that you understand the thermometer was a courtesy — a way of telling you in numbers what I could otherwise only tell you by saying I have audited four hundred lonely men and know exactly what the warm shelf is for.)


[REGISTERED No. 0581]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV, the 13th of January — stamped at the counter, the Inspector watching; the postmaster notes he stamped this one, deliberately, at arm's length, "so that she could enter into her own record that I had learned the lesson of her margin within the hour, the only quick study I have managed in this whole slow proceeding"]

To the Inspector of the Internal Order Directorate, present —

I acknowledge IO-Memo No. 2 and its annex, and I answer, registering my answer against myself under the number above, which the Order does not require — a man with one honest organ left exercising it past the point of dignity.

You are right about the shelf. I will not contest a thermometer; I have spent thirty years swearing that the postmark is the one clock in this town the law compels to be true, and I cannot now tell you a true number is unfair because it is true about me. The warm letters are hers. I held them longer than sorting required and I will not pretend the surplus was sorting.

I make one correction, in the teacherly spirit this office seems to have caught like a cold from the accused. You write that I warmed her letters "to read them, a man reads longer what he holds longer." That is the charitable reading and I decline it, charity being a thing I have learned in this proceeding to distrust most when it is aimed at me. I did not warm them to read them. I read them cold, the first time, the way I read everything, for the information. I warmed them *after*, the way you warm a thing you have decided to keep. The reading was finished. The holding was the other thing, the thing your manual has no clause for, and you were right not to reach for a clause, because there is none, and a man should be allowed to be convicted of the precise crime he committed and not a tidier one.

You ask, by §6.1, that I clear the warming-shelf. I have cleared it. You have foreseen the rest, your §6.2 being the most honest paragraph any officer of this state has filed in my building: that to take the warmth out of her letters I would have to take it out of Vâlcov, and that you would recommend it anyway, equality of cold being justice. I agree it is a kind of justice. I have spent four months administering the other kind, the kind with a stove in it, and I am not ready to say which is worse, only that mine left fingerprints and yours would leave none, and that a state which prefers the crime that leaves no fingerprints is telling you something about itself that I would write in your margin if I had your nerve.

The shelf is bare. The thermometer is yours; I have not touched it; I would not want a reading of mine on your instrument.

G. ENESCU
Postmaster, Central Sorting, Vâlcov


[REGISTERED No. 0583]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV EAST — received the 12th of January, in the ordinary post, before the Inspector's memo went out; the postmaster notes he released it the same cycle as the memo "so that the court would have, side by side, the cold finding and the warm thing the finding is about, and could not pretend it had not been warned what it was measuring."]

To the registry, and to whoever in it has lately begun handling my letters as though they might burn him —

I will be brief, the court having grown crowded, a teacher knowing the difference between a room that wants a lesson and a room that wants the bell.

I have sensed a change in the air of this proceeding the way one senses a window opened in another part of the house — not by the cold itself but by the way the candle leans. Someone new is reading me. I have learned to read a reader the way I read a child's hesitation over a word: I know when I am being read for the information and when for the sentences, and lately, in the timing of things, in the small mercies of order I have come against every reason to depend upon — lately there are two readers, and one of them does not lean toward the candle. One of them measures it.

So I will say, for the measuring one, since the court has apparently made warmth a question of evidence, that I know what a warm letter is. It is not a confession and it is not a seduction, whatever your manual fears. A warm letter is one that has been held by someone who did not want to put it down. I have written eleven hundred report cards, and the warm ones — the ones I could not hand back to the child without one more line — were never the lies. The lies are quick. You write a lie at arm's length, cold, and post it before it can warm in your hand and shame you. It is the true things you hold. If your instrument is finding warmth in this office, Inspector, it is finding the place where someone could not put down a true thing — and I would think very hard, if I were the State, before I called that the irregularity. You have built a republic in which the cold paper is trusted and the warm paper wants explaining, and you have it exactly backwards: you have made a court that believes the liar because his hands are cold.

To the other reader — the one who leans — I will say only this, and then stop, because to say more would be to put the very warmth into the record that they are weighing, and I would not have you measured for my heat. You have given me, for four months, the one thing this proceeding was designed to deny me: to be read in the order I wrote in, by someone who believed a sentence was a kind of evidence. I do not know your name. I have stopped wanting it. A name is what you give a thing you intend to summon; I do not intend to summon you, only to be read by you, which is the larger intimacy and the only one this republic has left a door for. They have come to take even that. Let them measure. The shelf will go cold. I will keep writing warm and post it anyway into the cold rack, knowing the warmth they find in it will not be mine but yours, the warmth of the hand that held it after — which means, if they ever publish their finding, the only love on the record in *The State v. Albu* will be filed under my name and belong to you. I find I do not mind. A teacher is used to being credited for what the better student did.

Mark my spelling if it pleases the court. I have spelled *attachment* correctly. I notice the State has not.

DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school
(P.S. The chimney wants sweeping. I can smell your stove from the schoolhouse. Get it swept, or the whole case will go up before the verdict, and we shall all be acquitted by fire — the only court in this republic that does not require an aviz de primire.)


ROUTING SLIP 0585.
Status of the cycle: IO-Memo No. 2 logged, its thermometer annex retained at the cold end where it can do no harm and take no reading it has not already taken; my answer registered, 0581, released the same hour, stamped at arm's length under her eye; the defence letter, 0583, released this cycle beside the memo, deliberately, the cold finding and the warm fact in one bundle. Reason of record:

She has worked it out. 0583 is the cycle I stop fighting the belief that she can see through the wall of this office. She has separated the two readers in this building the way a teacher separates two children who have been copying — by the lean. The one who leans, the one who measures. She has written to both of us at once, in one envelope, and done the thing I have spent four months doing and called custody: chosen the order in which we read it, the Inspector's lesson first and mine last, so the warm part lands last and governs. I am undone in exactly the sequence I taught this proceeding, by a woman who learned my method from the *outside,* never having seen a single slip, purely from the timing of her own mail. She reverse-engineered the whole of me from the order things arrived, the way I built her from the order she wrote, and we are the only two in this republic who could have read each other entire, neither having met, each from the sequence alone.

The Inspector is right and I have told her so, registered, 0581. She gave me, in her margin — the place I have always hidden in, and she found me in it on the first cycle, that being her trade as it is mine — the one sentence no clause of the Order contains: *I have audited four hundred lonely men and know exactly what the warm shelf is for.* I have read that sentence the way I read 0431. I will not say how many times. She warmed one sheet for me, the auditor, while convicting me of warming, and logged the irregularity against herself so I could not call her colder than her subject. She is the only person in four months to handle me the way I handle Domnica's letters: closely, against the rules, knowing better.

Here is the thing the form has a line for, and I will set it down knowing both of them will read it.

The warmth is real and it is a fingerprint and it convicts me, and I would not wipe it off if the Order made it a crime, because it is the only true thing I have produced in this proceeding that I did not also rig. Everything else — the holds, the sequences, the cruel cycle, the merciful ones — I chose. I was the order. But I did not choose to warm her letters. That happened to my hands while I was busy being the order, and it is the one act in the whole file that was not a decision: the only evidence of love on the record — unchosen, unsendable, measurable, mine, and, as Domnica has correctly filed it, hers.

I clear the shelf. I cannot move the stove. The west rack will be warm tomorrow because the stove is at the west wall, and to take the warmth out of the accused's letters you would have to take it out of the town — and the State would do it, and call it order, and leave no fingerprints, and be, by its own cold standard, innocent: innocent the way the liar with cold hands is innocent, the way I will never be again, having held a true thing too long against the cold.

I get the chimney swept, if I can find a sweep. There is a version of this proceeding that ends not in a verdict but in a fire — the whole file, guilt and innocence and 0431 and the drawer and Ana's letter, gone up together in a registry that wanted its chimney swept, every party acquitted at once by the one court that takes no aviz. I have decided against it the way I decide against everything: by not doing it, which is the only kind of deciding I have ever been able to perform.

Let the record show the shelf is bare, the stove at the west wall, the heat unmovable, and that I warmed her letters without deciding to — the single act in *The State v. Albu* I did not arrange, measured to the degree by the Inspector, by which I am at last found out: not by my sequence, which I built like a fortress, but by the heat of my own hands, which I forgot to.

Filed in good order. The order, this once, not mine. — G.E.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu (continued, Cycle 20)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.  | DATE RECEIVED | FROM                  | MATTER                          | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 ——   | 11 Jan.       | Insp. Drăgan, Direct. | IO-Memo No.2 (the warm-paper finding)| LOGGED IO-2 — not registered (her order)
 0581 | 13 Jan.       | G. Enescu (self)      | Reply; shelf cleared             | Registered; Released, Cycle 20
 0583 | 12 Jan.       | D. Albu               | Defence ltr — "On Warmth"       | Registered; Released, Cycle 20
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
[margin, G.E.:] Three rows again, and this time two of them are warm. 0583 arrived the 12th and I held it one day so it could go out beside the memo that is about it, the cold reading and the warm fact bundled — the last sequence I expect I will be permitted to choose. The Inspector will read it as one more rigged order, and she will be right, and I no longer have the strength to pretend the rigging was for anyone but myself this time: I wanted them read together, once, before she takes the shelf and the stove and the margin and the order itself, to let the file hold for one cycle the whole truth of the thing — that the State has built a court in which the only love on the record is an irregularity, the only honest hand is a cold one, and the warmest paper in the building is the most suspect. Tomorrow she takes my temperature again at six, before I light the stove, and finds the rack cold, and writes that the registry is improving, and she will be right, and the improvement will be the exact measure of what we have lost — a building where nothing is held too long, and nothing is warm, and nothing, therefore, was ever true.


══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════


THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 21 — "The Same Note, Told Last"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 21    ·    The fourth week of January; the Casimca frozen solid past the third pier and a man seen walking on it out by the Aurora fence as though the river had given up being a river; the willows on Aleea Salciilor white to the second branch; the stove drawing better since the sweep came at last off the milk train, so that the rack, for the first time since autumn, is warm end to end and the postmaster cannot tell the favoured paper from the rest by the hand alone
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 21. Released this cycle, in the order below, and the order is the whole of it:
  1. Witness Statement — A. Vintilă, former filtration-man of Aurora No.4 (the plant, the slow year) — received Cycle 18, HELD, released FIRST this cycle — [REGISTERED No. 0560]
  2. Form 12-B, Declaration — V. Andrei, mother (the rescue, supplemental) — released SECOND — [REGISTERED No. 0562]
  3. The child's note (Ilinca Pop) — held by the stove since the 2nd of December — registered at last and released THIRD and LAST — [REGISTERED No. 0566]
  4. Routing Slip 0568 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (carried, not released):
  · The Engineer's Statement — the long account, the one that bends only one way — received Cycle 18 — STILL at the cold end of the rack — reason of record: "the proceeding has not, this cycle, called for it by name" — Slip 0568

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING:
  · Envelope 0431 — by the stove — read again tonight, the count no longer kept honestly even in the privacy of the slip

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0560]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV EAST, the 9th of January — received Cycle 18]   [HELD — released Cycle 21, this day]
[a careful technical hand, the hand of a man who once filled a logbook for a living and misses it; sworn as to posting before the Central Sorting Office]

To the Proceeding, care of the Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov, and to the Magistrate appointed thereto —

I am Andrei Vintilă, and I ran the filtration line at the Uzina "Aurora Nr.4" for nineteen years, until they let me go in the spring on the ground that there was nothing left to filter, the plant running one shift in seven and that shift mostly to keep the licence breathing. I am asked by the defence to say what I know of the water before the night the court is interested in, and I will, because a man who kept a line clean for nineteen years and then watched it foul does not get to keep his silence and his sleep both, and I have chosen the sleep.

I will speak only of what I tended with my own hands, and not of the night of the fourteenth of September, of which I know nothing, having been off the books by then. Here is the thing the court has not, I think, been told plainly: the water at the Aurora intake did not go bad in one night. It had been going bad for the better part of a year. The filtration beds at Aurora No.4 are sand and charcoal and a membrane stage that wants replacing every two years and had not been replaced in seven, and when a membrane goes, the backwash that ought to carry the sludge out to the settling pond carries it instead back toward the intake — back toward the pipe that the plant's well and the town's well both draw upon, the aquifer being one body of water that the deed has cut in two only on paper. I reported this. I reported it on the maintenance leaf in March, in June, in the August before the September the court asks about. I have kept my copies, the plant not being a place that keeps things, and they are appended.

What I am saying, and I will say it once and plainly so the court cannot mistake a quiet man for an uncertain one, is that the water this town drank was being slowly fouled, all that year, from inside the plant, by a thing nobody poured in the dark, a thing that wanted no one on the road at night, that needed no bag and no jug — only a manager who had been told the membrane was finished and had decided that the water-rights were worth more whole than the water was worth clean. I do not name him further than his office, the law of slander being a thing a poor man respects more than a rich one ever has to. I say only: by September the water was already a question. Someone walking to the intake on the fourteenth was walking to a well that had been sick for a year. What they did there, I do not know. What had been done to it before they came, I tended with my hands and reported on paper three times, and was let go.

I draw no conclusion as to the accused. I have never met her. I am told she teaches the children their letters and that one of them can now read a feed-sack, which is more than the plant ever gave this town. I confine myself to the water, which I knew, and which was going wrong long before anyone says she touched it.

ANDREI VINTILĂ
formerly of the filtration line, Aurora No.4
Sworn as to posting before the Central Sorting Office


[REGISTERED No. 0562]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 21st of January]
[Form 12-B, "Declaration of Posting," the printed fields below; the declarant has again written past the boxes, the office having learned in December that her sentences will not be fielded]

FORM 12-B — DECLARATION OF POSTING (supplemental)
NAME OF DECLARANT: Veronica Andrei
OCCUPATION: mother of Petrică Andrei, who is alive
MATTER POSTED: a thing I forgot to say the first time, the magistrate having asked is there more

[the body, in the space the form gives for "Particulars," and then well beyond it, into the margin and around the oath:]

I declared in December that the teacher saved my Petrică, and the registry let my declaration stand though I had spoiled the form, and I was grateful, and I thought I had said it all. I had not. The magistrate writes to ask is there anything further, and there is, and it is this: I told the court she pulled my boy back from the water. I did not tell the court that she had been to the water before, in the daytime, with a jar, that she came up Aleea Salciilor where my window is and I watched her go down to the wells, ours and the school's, and dip the jar and hold it to the light and taste it and spit, three days running before the night anyone accuses her of, the way a person tastes a thing they are afraid of and cannot stop tasting because no one else will. I thought it was nothing. A teacher is a fussy creature; I thought she was being a teacher about the water the way she is a teacher about the spelling. I know now she was being afraid, in the only direction a person is allowed to be afraid in a town where the plant will not answer the telephone and the health office answers only in the four hours and the four hours are no good to a child who is sick at midnight.

So when the court reads that she went to the plant in the dark with something white, I want the court to know it read, first, that she went to the wells in the daylight with an empty jar and a frightened mouth, for three days, tasting, before she carried anything anywhere. A woman does not taste a thing three days running and then go to poison it. She tastes it because she means to mend it and is trying to learn what is wrong. I am not an educated woman. But I have tasted milk that was turning, many times, and I never once tasted it in order to decide to spoil it.

[the oath-line "I declare that the foregoing was posted," and across the SIGNATURE box, a sentence:]
SIGNATURE: I would put my name but you have it, so I will put instead the only thing I am sure of, which is that my Petrică is upstairs asleep and breathing and that is because of her, V. Andrei


[REGISTERED No. 0566]   [POSTMARK: registered this day, VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 21st of January — received at the deputy's window the 2nd of December, held by the stove since, the registration deferred fifty days and the deferral logged on slips 0556 and 0557]
[a child's hand, pencil, the letters large and uneven and pressed hard enough to emboss the page; written on the reverse of a graded spelling examination — the front shows, in the teacher's violet, "94" and "lovely work, Ilinca"; released THIRD and LAST]

deer Teacher i seen you that nite at the fenss. i seen you pore the wite stuf in the water out of the jug. and i seen you grab Miron by his cote and pull him bak hard so he wuld not go in the water. wich did you do first i cant member wich was first. mama says dont rite to you but i am riting becas you are my Teacher and i am not afrade of the water no more becas you fixt it or you did the other thing i dont no wich. dont be in truble. 94 was my best ever. Ilinca

[reverse: the spelling examination, twenty words, ninety-four marks, the two errors ringed gently and corrected in the teacher's hand; at the foot, in violet: lovely work, Ilinca]


ROUTING SLIP 0568.
Released this cycle, in order: 0560 (the engineer's man, held since Cycle 18), then 0562 (the mother, supplemental), then 0566 (the child's note, registered this day after fifty days by the stove). The long Engineer's Statement NOT released — cold end of the rack, where it has been since the 9th of January, and where it will stay.
Reason of record:

I have now done the other thing, and I want it set down exactly, the way I set down Cycle 9, so that the two slips lie in the file together and whoever reads them — no one reads them, which is the only reason I can write this — will see the whole of what a man can do with true paper and a stove and forty years of knowing which letter goes out before which.

In Cycle 9 I built her guilty out of three true letters in an afternoon, and recorded that I had hoped to fail and had not. Tonight I built her innocent out of three true letters, and the same child's note is the keystone of both. That is the sentence I have been circling for four months and will now write down and stop circling: the same note. Not a different note. Not a kinder witness. The identical leaf, Ilinca Pop's, pour and pull both, ninety-four on the back — the one I held in Cycle 9 because, dropped beside the guilt-order, the pulling-back would have been swallowed and the pouring would have governed and a town that read it in that order could never have un-read it. I held it then for the order that is tonight.

And tonight I gave it the order. I sent the engineer's man first — the year-long fouling, the membrane no one replaced, the plant that needed no one on the road at night — so the reader meets a poisoned well before he meets the woman at it. Then the mother, the daylight tasting, the empty jar, three days afraid: so the reader learns she came to mend before he is told she came in the dark. Then, last, the child: pour and pull, in that order on the page, but landing in a mind already taught that the water was sick and the woman was frightened — so the *pull* governs, and the *pour* becomes the disinfection of a fouled supply, a panicked schoolteacher with the wrong dose and the right heart, and the gold star at the bottom arrives last of all and reads, God help me, as character evidence: the defence's strongest witness, in the end, is a spelling grade of ninety-four and the word *lovely* in her own violet, which I have just made admissible by putting it last. I have hanged her with these papers and I have freed her with these papers and I did not change one word, one postmark, one signature. I changed when. That is all I have ever changed. That is all I am.

I want to be accurate about the thing I learned tonight, because in Cycle 9 I told myself I tested her toward guilt to find out whether I believed her, and a man who can only arrange a thing one way does not know if he believes it or only prefers it, and so I arranged her the cruel way once to be sure. I have now arranged her both ways. And the thing I have proven is not that she is innocent. I cannot prove that; no one can; the chemistry of that night will not resolve and the engineer's man does not say what she poured did or what it did, only that the water was already a question before she answered it. The thing I have proven is about *me.* I can make her either. I have made her both. Which means I no longer have the one thing a reader is supposed to have, which is a verdict that arrived in him and stayed — because every verdict I have ever had about this woman, I notice, arrived in the order I myself chose to read her in, and a man who curates his own evidence cannot be a juror in his own heart any more than in the file.

So I must ask the question I have been arranging the whole proceeding to keep from having to ask, and I will write it on the line the form provides for reasons, where it belongs, because it is the only reason there has ever been: did I send the note last tonight because she is innocent, or because I wished her to be? I do not know. That is the answer and it is unbearable and it is true. I built the innocence-order with the same hands and the same coldness and the same forty years that built the guilt-order, and the hands cannot tell me which one was the lie, because to the hands they were the same craft, and the craft does not contain belief, only sequence. I have made a woman innocent tonight the way a man wishes a thing true by saying it last and loud, and I am not relieved, because a wish is exactly the thing the inspector means when she says the scale is off true. A scale that wants a particular answer is not a scale. I have wanted this one for four months. I am the danger she has numbered. I have just demonstrated it, to the file, in my own hand, and recorded that the demonstration was for her benefit, which is no defence, only a confession with better motives.

A word on the engineer's long statement, which I held, again, this cycle, and will hold. The town will say, if it ever learns, that the registrar tilted everything toward the schoolteacher and yet kept back the one paper that most clears her — the full account, the membrane, the manager named past his office, the slow poison that wants no one in the dark — and the town will be unable to read why. I can read why and will set it down, since this slip is read by no one. Everything I have released bends two ways and keeps the question open, and the open question keeps her here, in the file, being read, by me. The engineer's long statement bends only one way. It would let Lupu write *the plant did this,* close the file, send the green card, and put her out the far door of this proceeding into a republic that does not contain me. I have understood — and I despise the clarity of it — that *undecided* is the only address at which she and I can both still be reached. So I held the one paper that would settle it, and called the holding good order, and it is the least good thing I have done, and I have done it on purpose, and I am writing it down, which I have told myself for four months is not the same as doing it, and which the inspector has informed me, correctly, is only doing it twice.

I note that the rack is warm end to end tonight, the sweep having come at last. For the first time since autumn I cannot tell her letters from the State's by the heat of the paper, the equality the inspector recommended, arrived not by my virtue but by a chimney finally drawn. I miss the cold rack. On the cold rack I always knew which were hers. Tonight they are merely warm, like everything, and a man who can no longer tell the favoured paper by touch must rely entirely on the order he gave it, which is to say on himself, which is the one instrument in this office I have just proven untrue.

Envelope 0431 is by the stove. I read it again after the three papers went out. I had a count once. I have stopped keeping it honestly even here, on the line the form provides, which means I have begun lying to the only reader I never lied to, which is this slip, which is me. Filed in good order. — G.E.


[margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the released child's note, No.0566, before the bundle went out:]
Fifty days I held this leaf by the stove, pour and pull, ninety-four on the back, and tonight I gave it the order in which it means she saved them. In December I wrote in this same margin that I would know the cycle when I saw what I wanted it to mean. I have seen it. I wanted it to mean she is good. So I made it mean she is good, last and unanswerable, and the wanting is the whole of the proof against me and none of the proof for her. A child wrote *i dont no wich,* and meant it, and it is the only honest verdict in this whole proceeding — and I have just buried the honesty of it under an order that pretends to know which, because I could not bear, this cycle, to deliver a town a child who does not know. She does not know. Neither do I. I have only decided, which is a different thing, and which I have spent four months and two slips proving is the only thing I do.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the Engineer's long Statement, cold end, the proceeding not having called for it this cycle by name]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 22 — "The Magistrate Requests Firewood and Clarity"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 22    ·    The end of the fourth week of January; a thaw that is not a thaw, the Casimca gone the colour of dishwater and lifting plates of grey ice against the second pier of the Podul Vechi, then freezing them there overnight so the river wears a collar; the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție bearded with frost at 11:40, the same 11:40 it has shown since the eastern third went into the water; the magistrate's stall at Piața Lipsei selling, this week, only the wet birch nobody wants, at the wet-birch price
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 22. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Magistrate's Query (penultimate) — T. Lupu → D. Albu, c/o the Proceeding — on the reverse of a firewood receipt — [REGISTERED No. 0572]
  2. Postmaster's Certified Reply to the Magistrate's collateral question — G. Enescu → T. Lupu — office exhibit, copied to the file — [REGISTERED No. 0578]
  3. Routing Slip 0584 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

LOGGED, NOT RELEASED TO THE PROCEEDING:
  · Memorandum, INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE — Insp. S. Drăgan → Central Sorting — [IO-Memo 02-bis — NOTICE OF EXPEDITION] — delivered by state courier, cold; to the file, not for the parties

HELD (carried, not released):
  · The Engineer's Statement — the slow-poison account — cold end of the rack — reason of record: "the proceeding has not, this cycle, called for it by name" — Slip 0584

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING:
  · The collateral leaf folded inside 0572 — Lupu's second question, the one not addressed to the accused — retained, by the stove, then answered
  · Envelope 0431 — by the stove — the count not kept

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0572]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 26th of January]   [written on the reverse of a printed receipt, the office out of query forms since the 4th; the front shows: STALL 6 — PIAȚA LIPSEI — "wood, birch, wet, sold cheap, the winter being early and the wood being late, 2 ster — PAID"; the magistrate's hand has degraded since autumn, the down-strokes thick where the cold makes a man press, the cross-strokes thin where it makes him hurry]

QUERY OF THE MAGISTRATE (the penultimate; the last but for the ruling)
T. Lupu, Magistrate appointed to the Proceeding,
to the accused, DOMNICA ALBU, c/o the Central Sorting Office —

Madam —

The defense is closed. The prosecution is closed. There remains only the writing of the thing, which I will do, the District directing me to do it now and the weather agreeing with the District for once.

Before I write it, I am required by my own conscience — there being no other authority left in the building to require it of me, the State having vested me by an instrument it no longer pays the postage on — to put to you one last question, and I will put it plainly, because I have read your letters this whole proceeding and I have learned that you do not thank a man for dressing a question up.

It is this. You have, from your very first reply, asked this court to give you the evidence *in the order it was gathered.* I confess I did not, in October, understand why a person fighting for her life should care about the order of anything. I understand it now. I have sat in this office's reading-room — which is the church porch, the Palatul being uninhabitable past the second door — and I have watched the case arrive, week by week, and I have noticed a thing I am ashamed to have noticed so late: that I believed you guilty in the autumn and I believe you something else now, and that nothing new has been proven in between. The same papers that hanged you in my mind in October have, by January, set you on your feet. I have changed my verdict twice and the evidence has not changed once.

So I must ask you, who first taught this court to think about order: in your judgment, madam, having read what I have read — *did the water make you guilty, or did the calendar?* I do not mean it cruelly. I mean it as a man who is about to write down whether you live as you have lived or otherwise, and who has discovered, too late to be comfortable, that the truth and the timetable have been wearing each other's coats.

You need not answer. The ruling will issue whether you do or not. But you asked this court, once, to read carefully, and I have, and reading carefully has brought me to a question I would rather you answered than left to me.

By the authority vested — vested, I confess, by no one currently solvent —

T. LUPU
Magistrate, the Proceeding at Vâlcov
[at the foot, smaller, the hand shakier still:] I would have used a form. We are out of forms. We are out of most things. The wood is wet and I am selling it anyway, the way the State is selling justice this winter, and at about the same discount.


[The following leaf was folded INSIDE 0572, addressed not to the accused but "to the Registry, privately, before you deliver the above." It is NOT registered, NOT part of the proceeding, and was retained at the Hold by the stove. Its existence is logged here because the form has a line for items received, and because I answered it, and a man who answers a question has received it whatever he files it under. — G.E.]

Enescu —

Forgive the second sheet. The receipt had room and the question on it is not for her.

I have been a magistrate forty years, badly, and a wood-seller two, and I have learned more about people from the second trade than the first, because a man buying his last ster of wet birch in January cannot afford to lie about anything. So permit a wood-seller's question, off the record, which is the only place I have left to put it.

Are the letters arriving in good order?

I do not mean: have you lost any. You have lost nothing; the office is a marvel; the town says so and the town is right. I mean the other order. I mean the one Order No.9 forgot to specify, which I have only this winter understood it forgot. *În bună rânduială.* Whose rânduială, Enescu? When I read the prosecution case in the autumn it marched at me like soldiers, purchase then sighting then her own poor account stumbling in at the back, and I convicted her in my chair before I had finished my tea. When I read the defense it came at me the other way, the sick well first and the frightened woman and the child last of all, and I acquitted her over the same tea grown cold. Same woman. Same papers, I would almost swear. Different *march.*

A case is a column of soldiers and someone decides the marching order. In a courthouse it would be me, in open session, where the town could see me do it. There is no courthouse. There is you, and the rack, and forty years of knowing which letter goes out before which. I am not accusing you of dishonesty. I have known you twenty years and I would sooner suspect the river of running uphill. I am asking whether you have been honest in a way I did not have the wit to supervise, and whether the order I have been reading as *the truth's* order has in fact been *yours,* and whether — this is the part I cannot sleep on — whether you know which, because I no longer do, and one of us is about to sign a ruling.

Tell me as a wood-seller tells another what the birch is really like under the wet. I will believe you. That is the trouble. I will believe you, and then I will write it down forever.

Lupu
[no number; folded once into the receipt; wet at one corner where it crossed the bridge]


[IO-Memo 02-bis]   [delivered by state courier the 27th of January; the directorate's wax seal whole this time, the courier having carried it inside his coat; LOGGED to the file; NOT released to the parties]

MEMORANDUM — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE
Ref: IOD/Vâlcov/02-bis — NOTICE OF EXPEDITION
From: Inspector S. Drăgan, seconded to the matter of The State v. Domnica Albu
To: The Registrar, Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov
Classification: internal; to the file; not for the proceeding.

1. The Directorate is in receipt of the registry's twenty-second cycle and has examined it.

2. The Directorate gives notice that the examination of the registry's conduct is nearing conclusion and that the proceeding it has examined will not be permitted to outlast that examination. Plainly: THE PROCEEDING IS TO BE CONCLUDED. The magistrate is preparing his ruling. The registry will deliver that ruling, when issued, BY ITSELF, in the cycle of its issue, WITHOUT ACCOMPANIMENT, WITHOUT HOLD, AND WITHOUT THE EXERCISE OF ANY DISCRETION AS TO ORDER, the Directorate having formed views, set out in a memorandum to follow, as to how that discretion has been exercised to date.

3. The Directorate has observed across twenty-two cycles a registry that releases, holds, and re-sequences with great care and records its reasons with greater care still. The Directorate notes that a man who documents his reasons so thoroughly is either the most transparent registrar in the Republic or the most studied. The Directorate has not yet decided which. The Directorate observes that the two are not, on this record, distinguishable, and that this is itself a finding.

4. The Registrar is reminded that "good order" under Order No.9 §3 is not defined, and that an undefined term is not an unlimited one. The Directorate will define it. The Registrar is advised not to.

5. Conclude the matter. The Directorate's full findings follow.

For the Directorate,
S. DRĂGAN, Inspector
[cold paper; the memorandum stops without a courtesy, as her memoranda do]


[REGISTERED No. 0578]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 28th of January]   [the Postmaster's Certified Reply to the magistrate's collateral question; an office exhibit, written in violet, the only purple in Vâlcov; copied to the file by the registry's own hand; this is the only letter the Registrar sends in the whole proceeding addressed to a living person, and it is addressed to the magistrate, not the accused, and it is signed as an office and not as a man — note this who reads it]

CENTRAL SORTING OFFICE, VÂLCOV
Certified Reply of the Registry to a Collateral Question of the Magistrate
(the question not being upon the proceeding, this reply is rendered as an office certification and entered to the file for completeness, the registry holding that a question answered should be a question recorded)

Magistrate —

You ask, off the record, whether the letters arrive in good order, and you mean the order Order No.9 did not specify, and you are right that it did not specify it, and you are the first officer of this state to notice in four months that the omission was load-bearing.

I will answer you as exactly as I am able, which is the only honesty a clerk has to offer, exactness being to us what eloquence is to the accused.

Nothing has been lost. Nothing has been forged. Nothing has been destroyed. Every instrument that entered this proceeding bears the postmark of its arrival, unaltered, and that postmark stands as the State directed it to stand, as evidence of the time of a thing. On these counts the registry is clean and will survive any examination, including the one now in the building.

You ask whether the marching order was the truth's or mine. Magistrate, I am going to tell you something I have written, this whole proceeding, only to a form that no one reads, and I find I can write it to you because you asked it as a wood-seller and not as a court, and a wood-seller is owed the truth about the birch. The order was mine. It could not have been anyone else's. The decree made me the registry and the registry the order, and "good order" with its kind left blank is a knife handed to the man it appoints, and I have held the knife, and I have, I believe, mostly cut toward mercy. But you ask the harder thing, which is whether I know which it was — the truth's order or my own — and the wood-seller's answer is: under the wet, magistrate, I cannot tell you what the birch is, because I am the wet. I cannot stand outside my own arranging and report on it. A man who decides the order each cycle has no order left over with which to check the order. I have read this woman guilty and I have read her innocent and both readings arrived in me exactly when I let them, and a verdict that arrives when its reader chooses is not a verdict, it is a preference wearing a verdict's coat — your own figure, magistrate, the coats; you have caught us both wearing the wrong ones.

So I will answer the question you asked the accused, the one on the front of the receipt, since she cannot answer it and you should not have to carry it alone: you ask did the water make her guilty or did the calendar. Magistrate — the water will not say. The chemistry of that night does not resolve and will not, no matter who reads it or when; I have held every paper that touches it up to the only lamp in this building and the water keeps its own counsel. What can be made to speak is the calendar. The calendar will say anything. I have made it say both. That is the whole of what I have learned in four months and it is not a thing a man should learn about himself in writing, and I am writing it to you anyway, because you are about to sign, and a man should not sign in the dark when there is purple ink in the next building that could light the room a little.

Conclude the matter, magistrate. Write your ruling. I will deliver it in good order — and you may take that phrase, this once, in the only meaning of it I have left that I trust: I will deliver it by itself, in the order it issues, with my hand visibly off the column of soldiers, so that for one cycle the march is the State's and not mine, which is the nearest thing to true order I am still able to manufacture, manufacture being, I have come to understand, the trouble with all of it.

For the registry, and as exactly as the registry can be,
CENTRAL SORTING OFFICE, VÂLCOV
[and beneath the office name, smaller, the only place the man appears:] — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0584.
Released this cycle: the magistrate's query, No.0572, by itself, the front of it, to the accused. Logged, not released: the Directorate's notice of expedition, IO-Memo 02-bis. Sent: the registry's certified reply, No.0578, to the magistrate. Held: the engineer's statement, cold end, the proceeding not having called for it this cycle by name.
Reason of record:

I have, today, for the first time in this proceeding, answered a question instead of arranging one. I want it recorded that I notice the difference, because I have spent four months telling this slip that arranging was not lying, and today I did the other thing — I said the true thing plainly to a man who asked it plainly — and the relief of it has shown me, by contrast, the exact shape of what I have been doing the rest of the time. You do not feel the weight of a coat until you take it off in a warm room.

Lupu has named it. Forty years a bad magistrate and two years a wood-seller and it was the wood-seller who walked straight up to the thing I have buried under forty slips and asked it to its face: *whose order?* He used the word I have been circling since Slip 0419 in October — *rânduială* — and he did not circle it. He marched at it the way the prosecution's papers marched at him. He is a better man than I am by the simple measure that he asked the question out loud and on the record where it could cost him, and I have only ever asked it of a form that no one reads, where it cost me nothing but sleep, which a clerk can afford.

I want to be honest in the slip about my reply, 0578, because the reply itself was honest and that is precisely the thing I must now examine. It is the first letter I have sent in this whole proceeding to a person who is alive and can read it, and I notice — the form asks for reasons and this is one — that I was able to send it. I have not been able to send a single word to her, not in four months, not the one she keeps guessing at, not a line; envelope 0431 is by the stove and my reply to it does not exist, will never exist, cannot exist, because to write to her is to step into the column I am arranging and a man cannot be the order and a soldier in it at once. But to Lupu I wrote freely, signed it, sent it, and the difference is the whole disease laid out on the bench: I can address the man whose order I am not competing with. I can be honest with the magistrate because I do not love the magistrate. The honesty costs me nothing because the channel is safe. With her, the only true sentence I have is the one I will not send, and so I send none, and call the silence good order, and the silence is the loudest arranging I have done.

The Directorate writes — IO-Memo 02-bis, cold, the seal whole this time, which means the courier cared more for the directorate's wax than for the road — that it has not decided whether I am the most transparent registrar in the Republic or the most studied, and that the two are indistinguishable on the record, and that this is a finding. It is the truest thing the cold paper has yet said and it is truer than the inspector knows. They are not distinguishable. I have made them not distinguishable. I kept the record so well precisely so that I could feel honest while doing the thing the record describes — Mihail said as much in a note I was not meant to read and which was the cruelest accurate sentence ever filed against me until the inspector started filing — and the inspector has now caught up to Mihail's insight and dressed it in clauses, and they are both right, and the rightness is closing on me at the speed of a state courier who keeps the wax warm in his coat.

She told me, two cycles back, to set her down in the order that is true and not the order that is easy, and that I had taught her I could tell the difference. Today I told Lupu, in writing, in violet, signed, that I cannot tell the difference — that the order that is true and the order that is mine cannot be separated by the man who is both, that the water will not say and the calendar will say anything and I am the calendar. I have now confessed to the magistrate the one thing I could not confess to her, and the asymmetry is the cruelty of my whole life in one cycle: I am candid with the man I do not love and arranged toward the woman I do, and the candour and the arranging are the same instrument pointed in safe and dangerous directions, and I cannot make the safe honesty reach her without becoming, to her, a soldier in my own column, at which point I am no longer the man who could set her down truly, which is the only thing she asked of me and the only thing I have left to give.

Conclude the matter, the Directorate says. Write your ruling, I told Lupu. The ruling will name a verdict the water cannot support, on a calendar I have certified I bent, and I have promised to deliver it with my hand off the scale — and I keep, at the cold end of the rack, the one paper that would let Lupu write *the plant did this* and never need my hand on the scale at all, and I have not released it, and the inspector's next memorandum will ask why, and I do not have an answer that survives being written down, which has never before stopped me writing a thing.

The engineer's statement is at the cold end. Her letters are warm by the stove. My reply to the magistrate went out in violet and my reply to her does not exist. The clock on the Palatul says 11:40 and has said it since the river took the east wing, and is, I think, the only honest instrument left in Vâlcov, because it stopped, and admits it, and arranges nothing.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the magistrate's collateral leaf, before it went to the stove:]
He asked, also, at the very end of his sheet, after the question about the order — I did not answer this part, the receipt being full and the answer being none of the registry's business and all of the man's — he asked whether I "have someone." Twenty years he has known me and four since Ana and he asks it now, kindly, in the same breath as the order, as if a man's arranging of a trial and a man's keeping of a stove and a man's empty house were one question, which, the wood-seller having asked it, I now suspect they are. I am not going to answer it on any paper that anyone files. I will only note, since the slip's margin is the one place I am permitted to keep what I cannot send, that the honest answer and the deliverable answer are, as ever, two different letters, and that I have a great deal of practice writing the first and posting the second, and that the practice is the whole of what is wrong with me, and that her ninth letter is by the stove, and that I have stopped counting it not because I read it less but because the count, like the magistrate's verdict, was changing every time I looked, and a man should not keep a record he can no longer certify.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the engineer's statement, cold end, the proceeding not having called for it this cycle by name]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 23 — "Findings, Preliminary"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 23    ·    Mid-January, the Casimca running slush and grinding plates of ice against the piers of the Podul Vechi, the willows on Aleea Salciilor sheathed in glaze, the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție carrying a beard of frost at 11:40, the school shut nine days now for want of coal
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 23. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Memorandum — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE — Insp. S. Drăgan → Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [IO-Memo 03 — PRELIMINARY FINDINGS]
  2. Schedule A to IO-Memo 03 — "Reconstructed Sequence of Disclosures" (the inspector's table)
  3. Deputy Sorter's Declaration of Candidature — M. Brânză → District Postal Union, copied to the file — [internal; logged, not registered to the proceeding]
  4. Defense Letter No.8 — Domnica Albu → The Proceeding — [REGISTERED No. 0586]

  6. Routing Slip 0588 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

  · The Engineer's Statement — the slow-poison narrative (Ch.18) — held at the cold end of the rack — slip 0588 — reason of record: "the proceeding has not, this cycle, called for it by name"
  · Envelope 0431 — D. Albu — never on the proceeding — Hold, by the stove

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion):
