[IO-Memo 03]   [delivered by state courier the 13th of January; received cold, the wax of the directorate's seal cracked across by the cold of the road]

MEMORANDUM — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE
Ref: IOD/Vâlcov/03 — PRELIMINARY FINDINGS
From: Inspector S. Drăgan, seconded to the matter of The State v. Domnica Albu
To: The Registrar, Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov
Classification: internal; to the file; not for the proceeding.

1. This memorandum sets out the Directorate's preliminary findings upon examination of the registry's complete record in the above matter: the registration log, the routing slips to date, the censorship register under Order No.9 §7, and the postmark-and-delivery dockets. The examination is not concluded. The findings are preliminary. They are also, in the Directorate's assessment, sufficient.

2. PRELIMINARY FINDING OF FACT.

2.1. The registry's record-keeping is exemplary. The Directorate records this first, and without irony, because it is the foundation of everything that follows. In four months and twenty-two cycles the registry has not lost, mis-shelved, or failed to log a document, or failed to record its reasons for any hold. The chain of custody is unbroken; the hand legible throughout; the reasons stated in every instance.

2.2. It is by reason of that completeness, and by no other means, that the Directorate can reconstruct what the record was kept to conceal. A registry that recorded less could not have been caught. The registrar has documented his own irregularity to a standard the Directorate could not have achieved had it sat in this office the four months itself.

3. PRELIMINARY FINDING OF IRREGULARITY.

3.1. Order No.9 §3 requires that every instrument be delivered "in good order" (*în bună rânduială*). The order does not define the term. The registry has, throughout, supplied a definition by conduct.

3.2. The definition the registry has supplied is not *the order of receipt*, not *the order of the proceeding's logic*, and not *the chronological order of the events the documents describe*. The Directorate has tested all three and the record fits none. By way of illustration: the pharmacist Costea's statement, received Cycle 6, was held on slip 0447 and delivered Cycle 9, behind the accused's account though received before it. The accused's request for the plant's records was held from Cycle 7/8 to Cycle 12 and released to open the defense at its strongest cycle. The child's note was held from receipt and released Cycle 21.

3.3. The Directorate has therefore reconstructed the operative standard. It is: *each true document was delivered at the cycle at which it would be read most favourably to the accused* — save in one cycle, Cycle 9, where the same documents were delivered in the order most unfavourable to her, for reasons the registry's own slip 0492 records as a test "to prove I could." The Directorate reads this as the moment the registrar confirmed to himself the power he was exercising. A man does not test a lever he does not know he holds.

4. THE TWO HINGES.

4.1. The Directorate draws the Registrar's attention to two cycles, 9 and 21, in which *recognizably the same evidence* was delivered to the proceeding in two different sequences.

4.2. In Cycle 9, the purchase (Costea), the sighting (the neighbour), and the accused's account were delivered in that order. Read in that order, the accused is guilty: she bought the means, she was seen going toward the place, and her account arrives last, as the confession of a person already convicted by the two letters before it.

4.3. In Cycle 21, the engineer's account of the plant, the mother's account of the rescue, and the child's note were delivered in that order. The child's note contains both the pouring and the pulling-back. Delivered last, after the engineer and the mother, the pulling-back governs and the pouring reads as the disinfection of a fouled supply. Read in that order, the accused is a woman who saved a boy and tried to save a town.

4.4. The evidence in Cycle 21 is not new evidence. It is, in material part, the same evidence, re-sequenced. The Directorate states the finding plainly, the plainness being the point: *the registry has demonstrated, on its own record, that it can produce either verdict from the same documents by altering only the order of their delivery.* This is not an allegation of forgery. The Directorate has examined every instrument for the physical signs of forgery and found none; the registrar's hand is nowhere where it should not be; not one word has been added, altered, or destroyed. The irregularity is wholly in the sequence, and the sequence is wholly the registrar's, and the registry's own slips say so, in the registrar's own hand, in violet, on the line the form provides for reasons.

5. PRELIMINARY CONCLUSION.

5.1. The Directorate concludes, preliminarily, that the delivery order in The State v. Domnica Albu was not "good order" within any meaning the order can bear that does not reduce to *the order the registrar preferred*, and that the registrar has bent the reading of the proceeding by the only instrument available to him, which is the one the order placed in his sole keeping: time.

5.2. The Directorate does not, at this stage, find a motive. The record discloses the conduct and conceals the reason. The slips contain matter not pertaining to the proceeding — re-reads of an unregistered item logged by count, the ambient temperature at which certain letters were filed — which the Directorate addresses in the covering note and not here, and which, while irregular, is not yet material. The conduct is sufficient without the reason. A scale does not need to want anything to be off true.

6. The Directorate's recommendation will follow in a further memorandum, upon conclusion of the examination. The Registrar is advised that the recommendation will, in the ordinary course, address whether the Vâlcov registry should be continued as a chain-of-custody authority under Order No.9 or whether the proceedings of the district should be removed to the seat. The Registrar is invited to assist the conclusion of the matter by such means as remain proper to him.

For the Directorate,
S. DRĂGAN, Inspector
[no warmth in the closing; no closing courtesy; the memorandum simply stops]


[Schedule A to IO-Memo 03 — the inspector's reconstruction, set out as a table in her hand, columns ruled with a straightedge]

SCHEDULE A — RECONSTRUCTED SEQUENCE OF DISCLOSURES
(documents bearing on the night of the 14th of September, by cycle of RECEIPT and cycle of DELIVERY)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 ITEM                          | RECEIVED | DELIVERED | GAP (cycles) | EFFECT OF GAP
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 Costea — purchase             | 6        | 9         | +3           | true fact lands AFTER her account
 Domnica — account of night     | 9        | 9         | 0            | lands LAST in guilt-order (Cyc.9)
 Records-request (filtration)   | 7/8      | 12        | +4/+5        | opens defense at its strongest cycle
 Engineer — plant filtration    | 18       | held      | —            | NOT delivered; reason of record varies
 Mother — rescue (Form 12-B)    | 13       | 13        | 0            | —
 Child's note (pour + pull)     | (held)   | 21        | —            | governs as INNOCENCE in Cyc.21 order
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
NOTE (Drăgan): the single document received and never delivered (the engineer's statement, item 4) is, in the Directorate's preliminary assessment, the most eloquent entry in this table. The registry has delivered, in varied order, everything that can be read two ways. It has withheld, in only one order — silence — the one document that can be read only one way: against the plant. The Directorate does not yet know why a registrar who has bent the proceeding toward the accused would withhold the one paper that most exonerates her. The Directorate observes that this is the only finding in this Schedule that does not fit the pattern, and that a pattern's one exception is, in the Directorate's long experience, where the truth of the pattern is usually kept.


[The following is NOT registered to the proceeding. It arrived inside the directorate's packet, folded separately, marked in the inspector's hand "to the Registrar, personal." Retained at the Hold, cold end of the rack, not by the stove. — G.E.]

To the Registrar —

I will not put this in the memorandum, the memorandum being for the file, and the file outliving us both.

I have read your slips. All of them. I came to read a corrupted registry and spent eleven days reading the diary of a man who, having decided he was the order, recorded the deciding so carefully that I could follow him into it like a corridor with the lamps left on. You did not hide. You filed. I have investigated men who burned what I came for; you kept it, and indexed it, and wrote your reasons on the line the form provides for reasons, which is the most damning thing a man in your position has ever done in my presence, because it means you told yourself the holding was not the lie.

I have not found your motive. I do not need it. But I have found the temperature, and the count, and the one cold paper you keep at the cold end of the rack while everything of hers stays warm by the stove, and I know that a man's reasons are usually shelved at whatever distance from the heat he can bear. You keep her warm and the truth cold. I have not decided what that means. You have eleven days, perhaps fewer, before I do.

I am told the town calls this office the last thing that works. Make it true. Conclude the matter as the magistrate writes it. Take your hand off the scale. I will see it if you do not, and I will see it if you do.

S.D.
[no number; cold paper; folded once, hard]


[Deputy Sorter's Declaration of Candidature — Mihail Brânză, on a District Postal Union grievance-and-personnel form, the boxes filled in his small upright hand, copied to the file as is his practice]

DISTRICT POSTAL UNION — FORM PU/11 — DECLARATION OF CANDIDATURE FOR OFFICE
(to be lodged where a registrar's continuance is under review)

NAME OF DECLARANT: Mihail Brânză, Deputy Sorter, Vâlcov Central
YEARS OF SERVICE AT THIS REGISTRY: eleven
OFFICE FOR WHICH CANDIDATURE IS DECLARED: Registrar, Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov
GROUNDS:

That the declarant has, on four occasions, logged and copied to the Union irregularities in the registry's conduct: the unrecorded-necessity hold of Cycle 1; the acceptance "in good order" of a Declaration of Posting filled outside its boxes; the holding of a child's witness note pending, in the registrar's own words, "the order in which it can be true"; and the maintenance of unregistered correspondence at the office stove. That each was logged in advance of the Directorate's interest. That the declarant would conduct the registry, if appointed, strictly by the order of receipt, no document held but for operational necessity recorded at the time. That the declarant restores confidence.

DECLARANT'S COMMENT (optional): I bear the registrar no ill will. I have worked beside him eleven years and learned the trade from him, including the parts he does not know he taught me, which are the parts I report. He keeps a record so that he may feel honest while doing the thing the record describes. I keep a record so that someone may be held to it. These are not the same trade. One of them is the post.

SIGNATURE: M. Brânză
Copied to: the file; the District Postal Union; the Internal Order Directorate (delivered by hand, this office, 09:20, during the four hours).


[REGISTERED No. 0586]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 11th of January — received 09:45, by foot, carried in against the cold inside the bearer's coat; filed warm]

To the registry, and to the one who holds my letters before the registry does —

I will be brief, the cold being against long letters and against long anything, the school shut nine days and the ink half ice in the well.

Something has changed in the order. I cannot read the letters that are not sent to me, but I can read the *weather* of the ones that are, and a person who has spent four months being heard at exactly the right moment learns the feel of a hand that has begun to hesitate. My letters used to arrive — I am told, by the way the court answers them — as if someone had chosen the hour. Lately they arrive as if someone has been told to stop choosing, and is trying to learn how, the way a person who has carried a thing a long way tries to learn to set it down without it falling.

I want to say one thing to you, whoever you are, before whatever is coming comes. I have guessed, this whole winter, that I was being arranged. I am not a fool, and a teacher who could not tell when a child's homework had been done in the wrong order would not last a term. I knew. I want you to know that I knew, and that I let you, and that letting you was not weakness. I decided, somewhere in the autumn, that if I was to be heard at all in this republic it would be by one careful reader or by no one, and I chose the one, and I have never once regretted the choosing, even now, when the air has gone strange and the answers come slower and I think you are being made to set me down.

So set me down, if you are made to. But set me down in the order that is true, and not the order that is easy. You taught me you could tell the difference. Do not unlearn it now, when it is mine.

I remain, in the cold, exactly,
DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school, the chimney out


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu (Cycle 23)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.  | DATE RECEIVED | FROM            | MATTER                          | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 0586 | 11 Jan.       | D. Albu         | Defense Letter No.8             | Released — Cycle 23
 [IO] | 13 Jan.       | Insp. Drăgan    | Preliminary Findings (Memo 03)  | Filed — internal; to the file
 —    | 13 Jan.       | M. Brânză       | Declaration of Candidature      | Logged — internal; copied as marked
 [eng]| (held)        | ex-Aurora eng.  | Statement re: filtration        | HELD — cold end of rack
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Twenty-three cycles into the proceeding of The State v. Domnica Albu. The Directorate has filed its preliminary findings. The deputy has filed for my chair. The accused has filed to tell me she knew all along and forgave it in advance, which is the only one of the three I cannot answer, the form having no column for it. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0588.
Held: one statement, at the cold end. Released: the accused's letter, by itself, and the rest logged where it falls.
Reason of record:

I am required to record my reasons. The Directorate has, this cycle, recorded mine for me, more accurately than I have managed in four months of trying. The inspector has done my arithmetic. She has shown her work in a schedule ruled with a straightedge, and the answer at the bottom of the column is the answer I wrote on the very first slip of this proceeding, in violet, as a boast: *I am the order.* She has proven it the way you prove a theorem, against me, and entered it to the file, and the file outlives us both, and she is right.

Let me certify the indictment against me while I still have the only purple ink in Vâlcov to certify it with.

She is right that I bent the proceeding by time, wholly in the sequence, not one word forged or destroyed — the one boast I am still entitled to, and which she has correctly identified as no defence at all, since a man who arranges true sentences into a lie has not been honest, only fastidious. She is right that Cycle 9 was a test, and crueler in her one clause about it than I have been in four months of my own slips: *a man does not test a lever he does not know he holds.* I held it. I knew I held it. I tested it on a living woman to learn whether I loved her or only loved the holding, and the test came back inconclusive, and I have been delivering the inconclusiveness as mercy ever since.

And she is right — this is the clause I have read most, in the Schedule, not the memorandum — that the one exception to my pattern is where the truth of the pattern is kept. I have bent everything that bends two ways *toward* her. I have withheld, in silence, the one paper that bends only one way: the engineer's, the slow-poison, the plant. She cannot yet read why a registrar who tilted the whole file toward the accused would withhold the paper that most clears her.

I will write the why here, where she will eventually read it, because she reads everything, and I would rather she have it from me in violet than infer it cold.

I withhold the engineer's statement because it does not clear *her*. It clears her *case*. It is the one document that would let Lupu write *the plant did this*, close the file, send the green card, and have her cleared, gone, walking out of Aleea Salciilor into a republic that does not contain me. Every other document I tilted toward her kept the question open, and the open question kept her *here*, in the file, being read, by me, the only reader she ever asked for. The engineer's paper frees her out the far door of the proceeding and shuts it behind her. I have at last understood that *undecided* is the only address at which she and I can both be reached — and that the engineer's statement is a letter to a different house, the one where she is innocent and free and I am no longer the man who decides when she is heard.

So the inspector found her warm by the stove and the truth cold at the end of the rack and could not read what it meant. It means I kept the woman and shelved her freedom at the distance from the heat I could bear — the cold end, as far as a man can put a thing and still walk past it forty times a day.

I have eleven days, she says. To save the office — the last thing that works, the certifier of the births and the deaths and the deeds, which is also Mihail's chair and the town's only proof that anything happened — I must conclude the matter as the magistrate writes it, deliver the verdict by itself, take my hand off the scale. And I find that the price of the registry's life and the price of my own honesty are, for once, the same coin: both demand I stop arranging her and let the order fall however it falls. The inspector thinks she is asking me to choose the office over the woman. She does not know — it is the one thing I have not filed — that the held paper she cannot account for *is* the woman, and that to release it is to lose her, and to withhold it is also to lose her, and that there is no order, true or easy, in which I keep what I have spent four months learning to read.

Mihail has filed for my chair. Let him. He would have hanged her in Cycle 9 and called it the order of receipt and slept. The town does not need a registrar who can be read by the accused. It needs one who cannot. He restores confidence. I have only ever restored *her*, cycle after cycle, into the one position where she stays a question, and the confidence is the office's, and the office is owed it back, and I am the debt.

She wrote, this cycle, *set me down in the order that is true, and not the order that is easy* — not knowing the inspector had, the same week, named the easy order and the true order and the third order, which is mine, the order that keeps the case open so the reader is not done reading. The inspector has the conduct and not the reason. The deputy has the chair and not the soul. The magistrate has the trust and not the truth. And I have all three of their best documents on my rack, and the woman's eight letters, and the ninth she does not know is by the stove, and eleven days, and no order left that is both true and mine.

I will conclude the matter as the magistrate writes it. I have decided that much. I have not decided what to do with the cold paper at the cold end of the rack, the one the inspector could not account for, the one that is the woman.

That decision is not for this slip. This slip is for the inspector's findings, which I hereby certify, against myself, as accurate.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the inspector's personal note, before it went to the cold end of the rack:]
She wrote *make it true* — the town calling this the last thing that works. She means: conclude cleanly, the office lives, the words become true. She does not hear the other reading, that the last thing that works is the part of this office that has spent four months reading one woman in the order that is true — and that to make *that* true I must do the one thing she forbids, and to make the *office* true I must kill it. I have folded her note once, hard, the way she folded it, and put it at the cold end of the rack beside the engineer's: the two coldest papers in the building, the truth and the warning, shelved together at the same distance, which the inspector, when she reads this slip, will know exactly how to measure.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the engineer's statement, cold end, pending nothing the registrar can yet name]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9

CHAPTER 24 — "The Post Is the Last Thing That Works"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 24    ·    Late January, the Casimca locked bank to bank but groaning at night where the current still runs under the ice, the willows on Aleea Salciilor furred white, the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție at 11:40 under a second winter's frost, the school shut twelve days, the town burning fence-rails now the firewood is gone
────────────────────────────────────────────────

  1. POSTAL-UNION CIRCULAR No.6 — M. Brânză, Deputy Sorter, for the District Postal Union → all registries of the district, copied to the file — [internal; logged, not registered to the proceeding]
  2. Collective Letter of the Inhabitants of Vâlcov — forty-one hands → "the Sorting Office, and whoever now answers for it" — [REGISTERED No. 0598]
  3. Supplementary Statement — T. Negoiță, smallholder, Drumul Aurora → The Proceeding (re: the goat, again; and re: the office) — [REGISTERED No. 0599]

  6. Routing Slip 0602 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

[POSTAL-UNION CIRCULAR No.6]   [delivered by internal pouch; no postmark; the Union franks its own paper, a grey rosette, smudged]

DISTRICT POSTAL UNION — CIRCULAR No.6
TO: All Registries and Sorting Offices of the District
FROM: The Office of the Acting Secretary pro tem (M. Brânză, Deputy Sorter, Vâlcov Central)
SUBJECT: On the Restoration of Confidence in the Registry Function

Colleagues —

It has come to the notice of the Union that the conduct of certain proceedings under Provisional Order No.9 has occasioned an examination by the Internal Order Directorate. The Union does not comment upon the findings, the findings being the Directorate's. The Union comments upon confidence, confidence being the Union's.

A registry holds the only unbroken chain of custody left to the state in the affected districts. When a citizen brings us a birth, a death, a deed, or a verdict, he brings it because he believes the office will record it as it is and deliver it as it stands. This belief is the whole of our capital; we have no other. The connection runs four hours and serves the state; the courthouse is in the river; the bank has been a shuttered window two years. The post is what is left. If the citizen ceases to believe a thing is delivered *as received* — in the order received, by the date stamped, without a thumb upon it — then the office certifies nothing, and a republic that certifies nothing is not a republic but a weather.

The Union therefore affirms the principles, to which all registries are invited to recommit:

(a) That a document is delivered in the order of its receipt, save for operational necessity recorded at the time of the hold and not after.
(b) That no registrar's private judgment of the merits may inform the order, speed, or manner of any delivery.
(c) That confidence, once a registry is known to have weighed where it should only have carried, is not repaired by the man who lost it.

The Union records its full faith in the registry function and its readiness to assist in the orderly transfer of any office found, upon conclusion of the examination, to require it.

For the Union,
M. BRÂNZĂ
Acting Secretary pro tem, by declaration lodged Cycle 23
[hand-note at foot, his small upright hand:] Copied to the file at the registrar's invitation — I asked him whether he wished it logged and he said the form has a line for it. So it does. — M.B.


[REGISTERED No. 0598]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 19th of January — received 09:35, brought to the window by a delegation of three who would not leave until they saw it stamped]

To the Sorting Office, and to whoever now answers for it —

We are the undersigned of Vâlcov, and we have written this together at the back of the church, where there is one stove still lit, passing the pen along the pew, and we ask that it be read in one voice though it is in forty hands, because what we have to say none of us would say alone.

We are told a man has come from the capital to inspect the post office, and that the findings are against the registrar, and that the office may be taken from him, or taken from the town and carried to the seat. We are not lettered in the law, most of us; the one of us who reads the law best is the woman the law is sitting on, which is a sentence we wrote and read back and let stand, because it is true.

We wish to put on the record — the record being the only thing in this republic that outlasts the winter — what the office is to us.

When my husband died on the ice road in the second year of the rationing, it was the office that wrote it down, and the date it wrote down is the date on the stone, and it is the right date, and that is the only thing about his death that is in order. — *the widow Crețu, Strada Făgădău*

We have heard what the man from the capital found — that the letters in the schoolteacher's matter did not always come in the order they came, that there was a hand on the scale. We have talked of it three evenings, and concluded that we do not want the office the man from the capital wants. He wants an office that weighs nothing and carries everything exactly as it falls, and we understand this is called confidence, and that in the capital, where there are doctors and wires and a courthouse with a roof, it may be the right thing. But we have lived a long time where everything meant to weigh us fairly has gone into the river or onto the ration, and the one office left has, by all accounts, weighed one woman more gently than the order required — our schoolteacher, who taught half the names at the foot of this letter to write the names at the foot of this letter, and who, the night the water went wrong, was the only soul in Vâlcov who went *toward* the water instead of away.

We do not know if she poisoned the water or saved it. We cannot decide, and we have noticed that the people surest of her guilt are the plant, and the man it owes nothing to, and the prosecutor who has never drunk from our well. We who *have* drunk from it are sure of nothing except that she went toward it. And we would rather be served by an office that could not bring itself to hang a woman in the wrong order than by one that could, and would, and would call it confidence.

We know this is not a thing the law can hear. We write it anyway, because the office taught us, by forty years of writing down our dates correctly, that a thing set down in the record is a thing that happened, even if no one acts on it, and we want it on the record that the town asked.

We remain, the inhabitants of Vâlcov, by our own hands or by our marks where the cold has taken the fingers —

[here forty signatures and marks, in many inks and two pencils, ruled into rough columns; among them:]

  · the widow Crețu (her hand) · D. Pavel · V. Suciu · the brothers Olah, X and X · M. Crăciun, who keeps the church stove · A. Pop (and, beneath, in a child's violet: *Ilinca Pop, age 9, my mama let me*) · T. Negoiță, his mark X, *and re: the goat, see my other letter* · F. Dumitru · the sisters Vâlceanu · I. Borza, who cannot sign and has had his name set down by his neighbour and confirms it · . . . [thirty-one further hands and marks] . . .

— forty-one in all, the goat's owner counted once though he has written twice.


[The following is NOT registered to the proceeding. It was folded inside No.0598, written after the signatures, in a hand that did not sign the front. No number. Retained at the Hold, by the stove. — G.E.]

To the one who answers for the office, and not to the rest —

I did not put my name on the front of this letter, since you are the only one who will read this side of it. I taught the children to write the names that are on the front; the schoolteacher taught the rest. Between us, the two teachers of this town, we taught every hand on that page. She is the better teacher; I will say so once, here, where it cannot be used.

I have sat three evenings listening to forty people decide they would rather have a crooked office than a cold one, and have not had the heart to tell them what you already know — that the law does not let you keep an office by being loved. I taught long division too, before she did. I know what it is to carry a number you cannot set down, and to be unable to show your working. Show yours, when you can. Not to me. To the record. It is the only one of us that keeps.

— a hand you know, that has decided not to be a name


[REGISTERED No. 0599]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 18th of January — received by foot, the bearer having walked the river ice from Drumul Aurora because the bridge road is drifted]

To the Proceeding, care of the Sorting Office —

It is me again, Negoiță, of the third holding past where the bridge would be if the road were open, the one whose goat got loose the night of all this trouble and got into the State's case, though I never asked her to.

I am writing for two reasons, in order, the office being particular about order, as everyone now knows.

The first is the goat. Steluța is dead. She did not die of the water; I want that on the record, the plant having put it about that my goat is a witness for them — that the water was fine since the goat drank it and lived. She drank it in September and lived. She died in January of being a goat in a winter with no hay, which is nobody's poisoning. She was loose the one night and a witness the one night and that is the whole of her public service, and I am burying her under the frozen pear tree, where, if anyone wants her deposition, they may dig.

The second reason is the office, and I will say it plain because I am told plain is allowed.

When I sold the lower meadow eleven years gone, the buyer's man tried to write the boundary at the second willow and not the third, which over a man's life is a cow. It was this registrar who held the old deed to the window and read the third willow, plainly, in the light, and the buyer's man — who was the plant, the same plant — went away. Now I am told he read the schoolteacher's letters in a better order than the law allows, and asked to be troubled by it, and I am not: a thumb that has only ever pressed on the side of the worse coat is the thumb I want at the window, having worn the worse coat my whole life.

I cannot read the law. I can read a coat. Yours,
T. NEGOIȚĂ, his mark below being the same X he has made on every deed, debt, and dead goat these forty years
[X]


[IO-Memo 04]   [delivered by state courier the 20th of January; received cold; the directorate's seal entire this time, the road having frozen too hard to crack it]

MEMORANDUM — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE
Ref: IOD/Vâlcov/04 — NOTICE OF DEADLINE
From: Inspector S. Drăgan, seconded to the matter of The State v. Domnica Albu
To: The Registrar, Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov
Classification: internal; to the file.

1. This memorandum sets a date. The examination opened in IO-Memo 01; the findings issued in IO-Memo 03. The Directorate now fixes the term for conclusion.

2. NOTICE. The proceeding *The State v. Domnica Albu* shall be concluded — the ruling delivered to the accused, the acknowledgement returned, the file closed — not later than the close of the second delivery cycle following this memorandum. The registrar will deliver the ruling, when the magistrate commits it, *in the order the magistrate writes it, by itself, on the cycle it is committed*, with no hold, no matter timed to colour it, and no document of the proceeding withheld or sequenced by the registrar's discretion thereafter.

3. The Directorate has read the Collective Letter this day registered as No.0598. It observes, without heat, that a town's affection for a registrar is not a finding of fact, that confidence in an office and confidence in a man are different instruments measuring different things, and that the inhabitants have, in forty hands, certified the very irregularity the Directorate was sent to correct. The Directorate files their letter as a deposition, by the beneficiaries, to the existence of the bias. It does not assist the registrar. It completes the record against him.

4. An office that certifies the births, deaths, and deeds of a town that has nothing else is a load-bearing thing, and the Directorate did not come to pull a wall down for the pleasure of the dust. But a wall that bears the roof and also, when no one is looking, leans on the people sheltering under it is not a sound wall, however warm. The remedy is not to admire the lean; it is to true it. The choice before the registrar is therefore not *the office or the woman*, as the town has framed it. It is *the office honest, or the office at all.* The registry survives only if it concludes as though the registrar's preference had never existed — which it can now do for exactly one document, the ruling, every other being already delivered and unsequenceable. The registrar has one clean delivery left in which to be the office the town believes it already has.

5. Upon timely and regular conclusion, the Directorate will report the registry "irregular but rehabilitated," and the office continues. Upon failure, the proceedings remove to the seat, and the wall comes down, with whatever it was bearing. The Directorate would prefer the former, and its preference is not affection, the connection for such things being also, in its experience, on ration.

For the Directorate,
S. DRĂGAN, Inspector
[beneath the signature, smaller, not part of the numbered text:] I read the goat's letter too. The man cannot read a deed and has read you exactly. Mind that the town reads you better than the Directorate does, and loves what it reads, and that neither fact is admissible, and that you have two cycles.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu (Cycle 24)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.  | DATE RECEIVED | FROM             | MATTER                        | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 0598 | 19 Jan.       | Inhab. of Vâlcov | Collective Letter (41 hands)  | Released — Cycle 24
 0599 | 18 Jan.       | T. Negoiță       | Suppl. Statement (re: goat/office) | Released — Cycle 24
 [IO] | 20 Jan.       | Insp. Drăgan     | Notice of Deadline (Memo 04)  | Filed — internal; to the file
 [PU] | 17 Jan.       | M. Brânză        | Union Circular No.6           | Logged — internal; copied as marked
 [eng]| (held)        | ex-Aurora eng.   | Statement re: filtration      | HELD — cold end of rack
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Twenty-four cycles. The deputy has circulated my replacement to the district before it is decided. The Directorate has given me two cycles and a date. And the town, which is the only party to this proceeding the law forgot to invite, has written in to forty-one hands to say it would rather have me crooked than not have me at all — which is the one document in four months I would have given my office not to receive, because it is the only one I cannot bear to be worthy of. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0602.
Held: the engineer's statement, cold end, again, by name unasked. Released: the town's letter and the goat-keeper's, together, in the order received, which for once is also every other order — there is nothing this cycle to time against anything, the documents being all on the one side, the side that wants me kept.
Reason of record:

I am required to record my reasons, and the difficulty this cycle is that the things requiring reasons are reasons I have no answer to, only weight.

The Union circular wants confidence restored and offers, in the same breath, to transfer my chair to the man who wrote it. I logged it — in good order, in violet, the violet still mine for two more cycles — because Mihail asked, at my own window, whether I wished it logged, and the only honest answer to that is that the form has a line for it. He believes you can keep the office by removing the man. He has not learned that an office is only ever as honest as the worst day of the man at the window, that the worst day comes for everyone, and that in my chair he will one day either hold something he should not or hang someone in the order of receipt and sleep — and the town will get the office it can trust and the verdict it cannot bear, and call it confidence, and be colder.

The town's letter I cannot file the way I file the rest. I have read it four times — I will record four — and it is the only document in this proceeding that has made me put the pen down, because every other has been *about* the case and this one is about me. The town has told the record what the office is *for*, the way she told me, in the autumn, what she was *for* — and the rhyme is not lost on me: the accused and the town have both declined to be weighed by what they did and asked instead to be read for what they were for, and I am the man both are asking, and the inspector is right that neither request is admissible, and I will honour neither, because honouring either is the thumb, and the thumb is what they love me for, and the thumb is what kills the office they need.

The sum, the form asking for *Particulars of Item*: one weight is the town — forty-one hands, one school, one stove still lit, no bank, no doctor, no wire but the four hours, no court but the river took it — whose only working instrument is this office; without it a town barely a town becomes a weather, as the circular says, for once, truly. The other weight is one woman, behind a shut school, the chimney out, who wrote *set me down in the order that is true and not the order that is easy*, whom I have spent four months arranging into the one position — undecided — where she stays a question I am answering and not a woman answered and gone.

And the cruelty of the sum is that the two weights do not, this time, oppose; they agree. To save the office I must conclude as written, hand off the scale, deliver the ruling by itself; to be the honest man the town wrote in to call me — wrongly, praising the lean and naming it standing straight — I must do the identical thing. The office's life and my honesty are the same coin, the woman is on the other side of it, and there is no way to spend it that does not spend her.

So I have decided I will conclude as the magistrate writes it. The town's letter has not unmade it; it has set it harder, because the one thing I will not do to the town that wrote me that letter is take from it the office in the act of trying to keep, for myself, the woman. The deadpan of it is that I am to save the office by performing, for one delivery, the precise honesty I have lacked the whole proceeding — competent to it only because I watched honest men do it all winter from across a window, the way a forger learns a hand he means never to use.

What I have not decided is the engineer's statement — the cold paper at the cold end, that I told the inspector, in slip 0588, *is the woman.* The Notice forbids me to sequence any document *of the proceeding* after the ruling. It does not — they always forget the clause that turns out to matter — say what I must do with a document that has never been *on* the proceeding. The engineer's statement carries no number; it came addressed ambiguously; I have never entered it. By the plain reading of the Notice it is not among the papers I am forbidden to move, because it is not among the papers at all — it is, like envelope 0431, like the leaf folded inside the town's letter, like Negoiță's goat under the pear tree, a thing that exists in this building and not in the file. The inspector has fenced the proceeding. She has not fenced the rack. There is a country still, between the file and the stove, and I am its only inhabitant, and the deadline does not run there.

I will not write tonight what I will do in that country. I have found the one move the inspector's clauses do not reach — and I am recording that I have found it, and not which way I will make it, because the form has a line for what a man has found and no line for what he is afraid of, and tonight those are the same item.

Forty-one hands. Two cycles. One coin. One cold paper in a country with no deadline.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the town's letter, No.0598, before it went into the file:]
I am letting it stand in the permanent record of the Republic that the town of Vâlcov asked, in forty-one hands, for exactly the crime the Directorate came to prove, and praised it, and signed it, the goat's owner twice. The inspector reads it as a deposition to the bias. She is right. It is also the kindest thing anyone has ever filed about me, and the two readings sit on the one page, the way the magistrate's trust and my withholding sit on his. The forty-second hand — the other teacher, who taught the names that praise me and would not set her own among them — wrote *show your working.* I have shown it. To the record. It is the only one of us that keeps, and it is going to keep this, and I find — no one reads this line but me, and now the inspector — that I am no longer entirely sure I want it to.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the engineer's statement, cold end, pending the two cycles the Directorate has allowed and the one country it has forgotten]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 25 — "Drafts of the Ruling"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 25    ·    Late January, the thaw refusing to come, the Casimca still walkable at the banks and black in its middle channel, the willows on Aleea Salciilor sheathed in a second coat of ice, the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție at 11:40 with a beard of frost, the school shut a fortnight, the magistrate's stall in Piața Lipsei selling green wood by the armful because the dry is gone
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 25. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Covering Query — Magistrate T. Lupu → the registry (NOT to a party; to the Sorting Office itself, improperly, "in confidence") — [REGISTERED No. 0603]
  2. DRAFT of the Ruling (Proiect de Hotărâre) — Magistrate T. Lupu → the registry, "to confirm the evidence is complete and in order before I commit it" — [enclosed with 0603; NOT a delivery to the accused; office exhibit]
  3. Memorandum — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE — Insp. S. Drăgan → the registrar — [IO-Memo 04-bis — REMINDER OF TERM]
  4. Deputy Sorter's Note (5th) — M. Brânză → file + District Union — [internal; logged]
  5. Registration Log — Central Sorting, Vâlcov (leaf for Cycle 25)
  6. Routing Slip 0606 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (not released this cycle):
  · The registry's reply to Query 0603 — held one cycle — slip 0606 — reason of record: "the magistrate has asked the registry a question the registry cannot answer truthfully without ending the proceeding tonight, and a thing this consequential should not be answered by lamplight after a memorandum"
  · The Engineer's Statement — the slow-poison narrative — cold end of the rack — never on the proceeding — the document on which the draft below silently leans
  · Envelope 0431 — D. Albu — never on the proceeding — Hold, by the stove

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion):
  · One firewood receipt enclosed by mistake inside 0603, being the magistrate's own unpaid account at his own stall — retained, by the stove

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No. 0603]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 22nd of January — received by foot, the magistrate having walked it up the hill himself rather than entrust it to the bag, and stood at the window until it was stamped, and not stayed to talk]

MAGISTRATUL TOADER LUPU
to the registry of The State v. Domnica Albu — not to a party, but to the office, and to the man in it —

A query, and I know it is irregular, and I am sending it anyway, because the regular channels in this proceeding all run through you, and the thing I need to ask is *about* you, and there is no clause in Order No.9 for a magistrate who needs to ask the postman whether he has been told everything.

I am writing my ruling. I enclose the draft. I should not — a draft ruling is the magistrate's alone until he commits it, and to show it to the registry before it is sealed is to let the chain of custody see the verdict before the accused does, which is precisely the disorder the inspector came to cure. I am doing it anyway. Hear my reason and then burn the impropriety with the rest of the bad wood.

I have built the ruling, these three weeks, around a paper I was promised and have not received. The matter from the capital — the plant's filtration, the slow business, the engineer's account I was told had come into the district. The prosecutor mentioned it. The defence requested it, plainly, in a letter I have here. I framed three paragraphs of my reasoning upon the expectation of it, because if the plant fouled the water across a season then the schoolteacher's one night is a different night, and a magistrate who has the slow poison in front of him cannot rule the fast one in isolation without lying.

The paper has not come to me.

So I ask the registry, which under Order No.9 §2 holds the whole file and has read, by its office, every leaf of it — is the evidence *complete and in order*? Is there matter received into this proceeding, on the plant, that has not reached my hand? I am not asking you to judge it. I am asking you whether it *exists.* A magistrate may rule on thin evidence; he may not rule on evidence he was not told he had. Tell me there is nothing further and I will strike the three paragraphs and rule on what I can stand on, tonight, and end this before the river takes the back room too. Tell me there is something further and I will wait for it, deadline or no deadline, because I would rather be dissolved late than sealed wrong.

I trust you. I am aware this is itself a finding, and that I have no business entering findings about the officer who carries my findings. I enter it anyway. You have held this file four months and never, that I can see, lied in it. I am asking the one man in the Republic positioned to deceive me whether he has, and asking it because I cannot conceive that he would, which I understand is exactly the position in which men are deceived.

Answer when you can. Not by the deadline — by the truth.

By my hand, cold,
TOADER LUPU, Magistrate
[in the margin, the letters wandering:] I enclosed a thing by mistake, the office being out of forms and my pockets being all receipts now — leave it where it falls, it is only my own debt to my own stall, which is the funniest thing I own


[ENCLOSED with 0603 — NOT a delivery to any party — office exhibit, the magistrate's working draft, written on the reverse of seven firewood receipts pinned together at the corner, the hand visibly worsening leaf to leaf]

PROIECT DE HOTĂRÂRE — DRAFT RULING (not committed)
In the matter of THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU

[leaf 1, reverse of "STALL 6 — PIAȚA LIPSEI — 2 ster birch, dry, PAID":]

That the water at the intake of the Uzina "Aurora Nr.4," on the night of the 14th of September, was made noxious, is not in dispute. Persons drank and were made ill. So much the State has proven and the defence has not contested.

That the accused went to the intake that night, and introduced the compound named, I find on her own account, she having declined throughout to deny it. She does not say she did nothing. I hold this proven.

[leaf 2, reverse of "STALL 6 — 1 ster, green, sold cheap, winter early":]

There are two waters in this matter and the State has tried only one.

The first water is the night water — the fast thing, the accused's hand, the compound, the children sick by morning. The second water is the season water — the slow thing, the plant's intake running a season without a working filter, the sludge the management is said, by the matter from the capital, to have let back into the common aquifer to spare the cost of trueing it, while keeping the licence alive on one shift a week. If that second matter is proven, then —

[leaf 3, reverse of "STALL 6 — kindling, a sack, PAID under protest":]

— then the question before me is not *did the schoolteacher poison the water* but *did the schoolteacher, finding a water already poisoned across a season by the men who hold its licence, do a reckless and unlicensed thing in the panic of a sick child, which may have cleaned it or may have fouled it further, no man being able to say which* — and that is not the crime the State has charged. The State has charged a wilful poisoner of a clean well. I find no clean well. I find a well already in question, and a woman who went toward it when the whole town went away from it, and a plant that has not been asked a single hard thing because it holds the documents and the prosecutor found the teacher nearer.

I therefore find, conditional upon the matter from the capital being in the file —

[leaf 4, reverse of "STALL 6 — 3 ster, the last of the birch, PAID, with thanks":]

— that the charge of *wilful* endangerment is not sustained; that what the accused did was an act done in extremity, its outcome unknowable; that the gravamen of the harm lies, on the balance of what the season shows, with the management of the plant, against whom the State has not proceeded; and that the accused be —

[leaf 5, reverse of a receipt where the figures are smudged with what may be melted ice:]

[here a long passage struck through and rewritten twice, the first version illegible, the second reading:]

— that the accused be **acquitted of the charge as laid**, the State having proven an act but not the wilful and noxious *intent* that is the whole of the crime, and the slow poison of the plant supplying, at the least, a doubt no honest man can rule past.

This is the ruling I want to write, and I tell the registry plainly that it is, so the registry understands what hangs on its answer. If the matter from the capital is in the file, I write the lines above, a woman goes free, and a plant is at last looked at. If it is not in the file — if I have built four leaves on a paper I do not in fact possess — then I have no standing to find the slow poison, and must strike all of it, and rule only on the night water, the fast thing, her hand, the compound, the children sick by morning, on *that* alone, with no second water to raise a doubt —

[leaf 6, reverse, the hand now bad:]

— and on that alone I do not see how I avoid a finding of the act proven and the intent presumed from it, which is a conviction, which I would sign because the law would leave me nothing else, and hate, and sign.

So the same hand writes two rulings on the backs of the same week's firewood, and which one I commit depends entirely on whether one paper sits in the registry's rack. I have asked the registry whether it does. I await the answer. I have left both drafts pinned together so that whoever reads this after me — and someone always reads it after, that is what the registry is *for* — will see that the magistrate knew, at the end, that his verdict was not his to decide. It was the post's.

[leaf 7, reverse, barely legible, the courtesy formula faithful to the last:]

By the authority vested — vested, I will say it one final time, by no one currently paying me, and shortly by no one at all — I append nothing further until the registry answers. The court is adjourned to the rack.

T. LUPU, his hand, what is left of it


[IO-Memo 04-bis]   [delivered by state courier the 23rd of January; received cold; a half-sheet, the directorate economising]

MEMORANDUM — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE
Ref: IOD/Vâlcov/04-bis — REMINDER OF TERM
From: Inspector S. Drăgan
To: The Registrar, Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov
Classification: internal; to the file.

1. This is not a new instruction. It is the old one, counted.

2. IO-Memo 04 fixed the term at the close of the second delivery cycle following its receipt. One cycle has run. One remains. The registrar will deliver the magistrate's ruling, when committed, by itself, on the cycle it is committed, no document of the proceeding sequenced thereafter.

3. The Directorate is aware that the magistrate has not yet committed his ruling. The Directorate does not instruct the magistrate; his deliberation is his own and the Directorate would not presume to hurry a man toward a verdict, hurry being how verdicts go wrong. The Directorate instructs only the *carriage* of the ruling once made. What the magistrate decides is justice. How it travels is the registry. The Directorate has only ever been here about the travelling.

4. The registrar will note that the term runs on the calendar and not on the magistrate's pen. If the ruling is not committed within the cycle remaining, the proceeding is nonetheless concluded by removal to the seat, and the registry dissolved, the Directorate being unable to distinguish, from the capital, between a registrar who awaits a slow magistrate and a registrar who has found a use for the delay. The remedy for that inability is the deadline. It is a blunt instrument. The Directorate did not design the weather that made blunt instruments necessary.

For the Directorate,
S. DRĂGAN, Inspector
[beneath the numbered text, smaller:] I am told the magistrate carried something up the hill himself this week and would not give it to the bag. A magistrate who will not trust the post with a paper, in a proceeding conducted *by* the post, has either lost faith in the registry or placed too much. I cannot tell which from here. You can. That is the whole of your advantage and the whole of your danger, and they are, as ever in your office, the same thing.


[Deputy Sorter's Note (5th), M. Brânză, copied to file and to the District Union — his small upright hand, on union grievance stock:]

NOTE FOR THE RECORD — internal.
The magistrate, T. Lupu, attended at the window on the 22nd and lodged a registered item, No.0603, addressed not to a party but to the registry itself, marked "in confidence," with an enclosure he declined to describe and the registrar declined to open at the window, taking it instead to the back room.

I record, for the file and the Union: a magistrate may not correspond *privately* with the chain-of-custody authority about a live proceeding. Either the item is on the proceeding, in which case it is not "in confidence" and I am entitled to its description; or it is off the proceeding, in which case the magistrate and the registrar are exchanging private papers about a case the one is judging and the other is carrying, which is the exact intimacy the Directorate has come to dissolve.

The registrar logged the item. I will say that for him: he logs everything, including the things that hang him. I asked whether he wished the *enclosure* logged separately. He said the enclosure was the magistrate's and not the registry's to log, and that the form has a line for the covering letter and no line for what a man encloses with it. I have noted that there is, in fact, no such line, and that "there is no line for it" has become, in this office, the formula by which the registrar files whatever he does not wish examined.

Logged. Copied to the Union. For the record. — M.B.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu (Cycle 25)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.  | DATE RECEIVED | FROM             | MATTER                          | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 0603 | 22 Jan.       | Mag. Lupu        | Covering Query (in confidence)  | Logged; reply HELD — Cycle 25
 [encl]| 22 Jan.      | Mag. Lupu        | Draft Ruling (not committed)    | Office exhibit; not delivered
 [IO] | 23 Jan.       | Insp. Drăgan     | Reminder of Term (Memo 04-bis)  | Filed — internal
 [dep]| 22 Jan.       | M. Brânză        | Deputy's Note (5th)             | Logged — internal
 [eng]| (held)        | ex-Aurora eng.   | Statement re: filtration        | HELD — cold end of rack
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Twenty-five cycles. The magistrate has, this day, walked up the hill in the cold and handed me, across the window, the one question whose true answer empties his draft of four leaves and whose easy answer empties it of mercy — and walked away without waiting, because he trusts me to answer it the hard way. I have his whole verdict in my rack now, in two versions, pinned at the corner, and the second version is mine to choose by a single word at the window. The most powerful man in this proceeding has reduced himself, in writing, to a man waiting on the post. He always was. He has only now written it down. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0606.
Held: the registry's reply to Query 0603, one cycle. Held also, as ever, the engineer's statement at the cold end, and the matter at the stove that was never the proceeding's at all. Released: nothing of weight this cycle — only the magistrate's query, logged, and the inspector's count, and the deputy's note, which logs that I log too much, which I have logged.
Reason of record:

I am required to record my reasons, and tonight the reason and the thing it is a reason for are the same object, and I am going to turn it over slowly because it is the last time the turning will be private.

The magistrate has asked the registry whether the evidence is complete and in order. He has asked it of the one office that knows it is not, and built his question on the faith that the office would not let him sign a lie. And he has enclosed, so that I should feel the whole weight of the question, the verdict itself — two verdicts, pinned at the corner on the backs of his own unsold wood, the one branching from the other on a single fact: whether a paper at the cold end of my rack is *in the file* or only *in the building.*

It is only in the building.

The engineer's statement came addressed ambiguously, in the autumn; I never entered it; it carries no number; it has never been on the proceeding. This is true. It is the kind of true I have spent four months perfecting — true the way Câmpeanu's walls are true, true to a man who does not know there is a room behind it. When Lupu asks *is there matter received into this proceeding, on the plant, that has not reached my hand,* I can answer, with my hand on Order No.9, *there is no such matter on the proceeding* — and it will be true, and it will be the wall, and on the far side of the wall is a paper that would let an honest man write four leaves he wants to write and a woman go free.

He has put it in writing that the verdict is mine — *which one I commit depends entirely on whether one paper sits in the registry's rack* — and the paper sits in the rack because I put it there and have kept it there. The branch he thinks he is choosing by his reasoning is chosen by my answer to one question at one window, and he does not know it, and has thanked me in advance, and walked home cold.

If I say *the file is complete,* he strikes four leaves, rules on the night water alone, and writes the conviction he says he would sign and hate — a woman found a wilful poisoner of a well that was never clean, the post office saved by my honest answer, the registry filed *rehabilitated,* and her killed with a true sentence, which is the only weapon I have ever needed.

If I say *there is further matter, on the plant, held by the registry,* and release the engineer's statement — then I have, in the last cycle, put my hand on the scale one decisive time against the inspector's express order, and sequenced a document to land exactly where it saves the woman I have spent four months arranging; the magistrate writes his acquittal; the inspector, who is not a fool, sees the registry produce a season-changing document at the precise moment it changes the season, and dissolves the office; and I have saved one woman by drowning a town's last certainty and called it, again, mercy.

That is the choice, and the slip is for the *because,* and tonight the *because* is mechanical and I will keep it so: the verdict is armed. Lupu has built two rulings that branch on a single fact, and the fact is a question he has put to my window, and the answer to it is one word, and the word is mine. Say *complete* and the gun fires one way. Say *incomplete* and it fires the other and takes the office with it. The magistrate thinks his reasoning chooses the branch. His reasoning is the trigger. My word at the window is the firing pin. I have built, this winter, without once meaning to build it, a machine in which a woman's life turns on whether a registrar lifts a weight he himself set down — and tonight the machine is loaded, cocked, and waiting on a syllable.

So I have held the reply. One cycle. The Notice gives me one cycle more and I have spent the first of two doing nothing but standing in front of the loaded thing, which the inspector will read, correctly, as a registrar finding a use for the delay. Let her.

I will not write tonight which way I will answer the magistrate. I will write only that I have found, in the gap between the file and the rack, the room the inspector forgot to fence — and that I am standing in it with two verdicts pinned at the corner and one cold paper that decides them, and the stove behind me where a letter from the autumn keeps warm, in which a woman who taught arithmetic wrote *take the steps in the order that is true,* and that I am no longer sure the registry can tell the true order from the easy one when its own answer is the firing pin.

The magistrate's own unpaid firewood bill fell out of the envelope. PAID, three of them say. Under protest, one says. The man who is to judge whether a woman wilfully poisoned a town cannot afford to heat the room he judges it in, and pays his own stall for green wood, under protest, against himself. I would laugh. I find I have mislaid the laugh somewhere in the rack, in the room with no deadline, where I am keeping it warm with everything else I cannot send.

One cycle left. Two verdicts. One word at one window. I know which word is true and which word is kind and that they are, this once, perhaps the same word — and that I no longer trust the man who would be the one to say it.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the draft ruling, leaf 7, before it went back to the rack pinned at the corner:]
He wrote *the court is adjourned to the rack.* He meant it as the dark joke of a freezing man — that his bench is now a shelf of pigeonholes and his bailiff a postman. He does not know how exactly true it is. The court *is* adjourned to the rack. The verdict is sitting in it, in two versions, waiting on whether I move my hand or hold it, and the law that vested Lupu — vested by no one, he keeps saying, and he is closer to right than he knows — has, by the plain operation of Order No.9 and the high water of four springs, vested the whole of this woman's life in the answer I give at a window to a question about a shelf. I am leaving his line in. *Adjourned to the rack.* Let the record show the magistrate named, in a joke, the exact court that is going to decide her: not a room, not a bench, not a man in a robe — a rack of oak pigeonholes, a stove, and a postman who has stopped being able to tell his mercy from his hand.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the reply to Query 0603, one cycle; the engineer's statement, cold end, pending the one cycle the Directorate has left and the room it has not]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 26 — "The Inspector Offers a Clean Conclusion"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 26    ·    Late January, the thaw still withheld, the Casimca gone hard at the banks and knocking under the ice in its middle channel like a thing trying the lid, the willows on Aleea Salciilor furred white, the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție at 11:40 with frost in the numerals, the school shut sixteen days, the magistrate's stall in Piața Lipsei shuttered two days running for want of stock, the four hours opening on dead air and the terminal showing only the word AȘTEPTAȚI — WAIT
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 26. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Memorandum — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE — Insp. S. Drăgan → the registrar — [IO-Memo 04 — TERMS OF CONCLUSION] — with annexed acknowledgement form
  2. Form IO-7 "Acknowledgement of Warning" — annexed to IO-Memo 04 — returned this cycle by the registrar, signed, one box left blank — [office copy retained]
  3. Defence Letter (the last) — D. Albu → the registry — [REGISTERED No. 0607]
  4. Registration Log — Central Sorting, Vâlcov (leaf for Cycle 26)
  5. Routing Slip 0608 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (not released this cycle):
  · The registry's reply to Query 0603 — released THIS cycle to the magistrate, in two words, by foot — see slip 0608
  · The Engineer's Statement — slow-poison narrative — cold end of the rack — never on the proceeding — slip 0608
  · Envelope 0431 — D. Albu — never on the proceeding — Hold, by the stove

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no registration number; office discretion):
  · One pressed willow-leaf, fallen from inside 0607 when the envelope was opened — retained, by the stove

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[IO-Memo 04]   [delivered by state courier the 25th of January; received cold, the courier not dismounting; a full sheet this time, the directorate having decided the matter merited the paper]

MEMORANDUM — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE
Ref: IOD/Vâlcov/04 — TERMS OF CONCLUSION
From: Inspector S. Drăgan
To: The Registrar, Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov
Classification: internal; to the file; one copy retained at the seat.

1. This memorandum sets the terms upon which the Directorate will close its inquiry into *The State v. Albu* without recommending the dissolution of this registry. It is offered once, and numbered, so there can be no later dispute as to what was offered, to whom, and when.

2. FINDINGS, STATED PLAINLY, THAT THE REGISTRAR MAY DISPUTE BY RETURN OF POST OR ACCEPT BY SILENCE:

  2.1. The Directorate finds the order of delivery in this proceeding irregular. It does not find, and declines to find, that any document was forged, destroyed, or falsified. The record is, on its face, complete.

  2.2. The irregularity lies in the *sequence* and the *holds* — in what was released before what, and what was retained "in good order" for reasons the registrar logged in his own slips, which the Directorate has not read and does not wish to, having no clause for a man's reasons, only for his deliveries.

  2.3. The Directorate cannot prove 2.2 to the standard of a charge and will not attempt it. A registrar who logs everything cannot be convicted of hiding anything; that is the perfection of the trap, it is the registrar's own, and the Directorate salutes it on its way past.

3. TERMS. The registry will be reported "irregular but rehabilitated," and spared, upon the following, each a single delivery observable from the capital, requiring no judgement of the registrar's heart, only of his hand:

  3.1. The magistrate's ruling, once committed, shall be delivered to the accused **by itself**, on the cycle of its committal, registered, the aviz-de-primire card dispatched for signature in the same carriage.

  3.2. **No document of the proceeding shall be sequenced before, beside, or after the ruling.** Nothing held shall be released in its company, nor to alter the ground on which it stands. The ruling shall travel naked, as the men who wrote Order No.9 imagined every ruling travelling, in the days when they had a courthouse and could not conceive it travelling any other way.

  3.3. The registrar shall make no further hold, in this proceeding, for any reason of record whatsoever, the time for the registry's discretion being, by this memorandum, ended.

4. THE COROLLARY, WHICH THE DIRECTORATE WRITES OUT BECAUSE IT WILL NOT HAVE THE REGISTRAR SAY HE WAS NOT TOLD:

  4.1. There may exist, in this building, matter relevant to the proceeding the registry has not entered upon it. The Directorate does not ask whether there is. It has no clause to compel a man to register a paper he swears he never received, and will not invent one for the pleasure of being lied to precisely.

  4.2. The registrar will understand 3.2 and 3.3 read together: whatever such matter is, if it exists, it is now **frozen where it sits.** To release it breaches 3.2 and dissolves the registry. To withhold it lets the ruling stand on the ground the magistrate built. The Directorate has taken the registrar's hand off the scale by the only instrument it owns — a deadline and a rule — and has not thereby freed the woman or doomed her. It has merely fixed which registrar decides her: the one who can no longer act. The Directorate finds this an improvement. The registrar may not.

5. ACKNOWLEDGEMENT. The registrar will sign and return, this cycle, the annexed Form IO-7. The form is not an admission; it is a postmark on a warning — evidence that the warning was *delivered* — which the registrar, of all men, will appreciate the Directorate troubling to obtain. A warning undelivered is of no force; the registrar taught the Directorate that, without meaning to, four months ago, by being so very good at it.

6. The Directorate adds nothing further. It commends the registry, as before, for its record, which is exemplary, and which is how the Directorate found it.

For the Directorate,
S. DRĂGAN, Inspector
[beneath the numbered text, smaller, in the same cold hand:] You will deliver the ruling as the magistrate writes it, touch nothing else, and be spared; the post goes on, the town keeps its chain of custody, the deputy keeps his window. The only price is that the woman is decided by a ruling built on whatever the magistrate could reach — which is less than you could have handed him, and we both know it, and neither of us will ever write down what *it* is, because you have no line for it and I have no clause. We are the only two officers in this matter who understand that the whole of justice, in this republic, has come down to one paper a man is choosing not to register. I respect you more than is comfortable, and I am ending your power anyway, because respect is not a clause either. Conclude it. Let her be heard once, in the order the law imagined, and stop being the order. It is the kindest thing I have the authority to make you do.


[Form IO-7, annexed to IO-Memo 04 — the directorate's printed boilerplate, the boxes ruled in the cold blue-grey of state stock — completed and returned by the registrar this cycle, office copy retained:]
