  ____________________________________________________________________________________

  ____________________________________________________________________________________

SIGNATURE OF OFFICER ..... Grigore Enescu, Postmaster — in violet, the office having no other ink and the capital's seal office having, by standing order, all the violet there is supposed to be — let the irony stand on the form, which has a line for the signature and none for the irony, which is where I keep the most of mine.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand, clipped to the office copy of IO-7:]

NOTE ON THE BLANK. — The form asks for the registrar's comments, *if any.* I have left the line blank, and wish it recorded — off the line — that this is the first blank in thirty years of forms that I have truly *meant.* I have filled ten thousand comment-boxes with the small true things a man smuggles past indifference. And the one time the State sends a form whose blank is the only honest answer left me — *there is nothing I can say that the saying would not make a move, and I am ordered to make no more moves* — I have nothing to put in it, and the nothing is, for once, the whole of the truth. The inspector will read the blank correctly: a man closing his own mouth. The first time in four months a reader has gotten me exactly right, and I have let them. Filed. — G.E.


[REGISTERED No. 0607]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 25th of January — received the bag-driver's hand, the Podul Vechi frozen, the school shut, the letter carried out by a child who would not give a name and would not wait, "from teacher," the deputy noted]

DOMNICA ALBU
to the registry of The State v. Domnica Albu —
to whoever holds this before the registry does, and to whoever has held all the others —

I am going to write this one without any of the things I have learned to put in the others.

I have read, over four months, my own letters being read. I could feel it in the order — that someone in the building you keep was taking the steps in the order that was true, and not the order I could be used. I dressed that feeling up, in the autumn, because I was frightened and clever, and a frightened clever woman makes ornaments out of her terror so she can hand it to you as a gift and not a hand reaching for the rail. I corrected the court's spelling. I corrected the prosecutor's chemistry. I was, I think, a little magnificent, and I am ashamed of none of it. The ornaments were true and they were also armour, and I have run out of the season in which a person can afford armour. The river is hard. I can hear from here that it is hard, and when the river goes hard the post crosses on foot and the crossing that took all winter takes a morning. I have taught the arithmetic of how long a thing takes. I know what it means that the magistrate has stopped sending queries: the next thing that crosses the ice toward Aleea Salciilor will be the one with my name on the outside and my whole life folded small inside, decided.

So I will say the plain things, while there is still a cycle in which to say them.

I do not know whether what I did that night helped the water or hurt it. I have never known. I have let the court believe I was withholding the answer out of strategy or pride, and the truth is duller and worse: there is no answer in me to withhold. I went to the intake because a child could not keep the water down and no one would answer the telephone in the four hours and the plant would not answer at any hour, and I had read enough to know one thing a person might do, and I did it, hands shaking, in the dark, a sick boy holding the back of my coat, and I do not know to this day whether I cleaned the water or poisoned it further. I have lain awake every night of this proceeding not with the fear of being convicted but with that — that I may have hurt them while reaching for them, and that the State and I will go to our separate ends never knowing which it was. You cannot acquit a person of *that.* There is no box. I have looked for the box longer than the magistrate has.

Here is the only thing I am certain of, and it is the reason I am writing to you and not to the court, which would not understand the distinction and would file it under *irrelevant.*

Whatever I am — guilty, innocent, both, neither, a woman who poured the wrong amount of the right thing into the dark — I have been, this winter, *read.* Truly read. Once. In the order I wrote myself in. By someone I will never see, whose face I do not have and do not want, because a face would make it smaller. You took my sentences in the sequence I built them and not the sequence the State needed them in, and held them longer than your office required, and let me arrive in my own order — which is the only mercy anyone has shown me since the night the water went bitter, and which is, I have come to believe, the only kind of mercy there is: to let a person be understood before they are used.

I taught children to read for thirty years. I know what it is to give someone that, and how few ever get it. I got it, at the end, from a stranger in a post office, inside the machinery built to destroy me — the truest thing that machinery ever did, and it does not know it did it, and I am telling you so that one of us, at least, has said it out loud, on paper, in good order.

I am not going to ask you to save me. You should not. To be saved by you would be to be *moved* by you one more time, and I have had enough of being moved, even by the gentlest hand in the republic — I would like, just once, at the end, to arrive somewhere without anyone's hand on me. Especially a kind one. So when the last paper comes, let it come the way the law meant it. By itself. Untouched. Let me be heard once in the plain order and then let me be done, and do not, whatever it costs you, reach for me a final time and call it rescue. I have been a teacher too long not to know the difference between a hand that lifts a child and a hand that cannot let the child go. Be the first. I am asking you to be the first, which is the only thing I have ever asked you, and the hardest, and the last.

I do not know your name and I will not guess it. I know your reading. That is more than most marriages.

I remain, with no ornament left and no fear I am willing to dress up,

DOMNICA ALBU
Aleea Salciilor, behind the school, where the willow by the gate is the one I have watched for sixteen winters and from which this leaf, which I am folding in, fell yesterday onto the ice and did not break, which I took, foolishly, as the only good omen left in town, and send to you, the only person who has earned a foolish thing from me —

you who have been my only fair reader.


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu (Cycle 26)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.  | DATE RECEIVED | FROM            | MATTER                          | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 [IO] | 25 Jan.       | Insp. Drăgan    | Terms of Conclusion (Memo 04)   | Filed — internal; terms accepted by silence
 [IO-7]| 25 Jan. (out)| registry        | Acknowledgement of Warning      | Signed, returned; comments blank
 0607 | 25 Jan.       | D. Albu         | Defence Letter (the last)       | Logged; not redacted; held nowhere
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
The reply to the magistrate's Query 0603 went out this cycle, by foot, in my own hand, two words long. I will not transcribe the two words into the log; the matter, this once, will not fit a column and ought not to. The directorate has ordered me to do nothing further. The accused has asked me, in the plainest hand she has yet used, to do nothing further. The coldest and the warmest readers of my whole life have arrived, in the same cycle, at the same instruction, by opposite roads, and I am sitting between them at the stove with a willow leaf and a deadline. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0608.
Released this cycle: the inspector's memorandum, logged; my acknowledgement, signed, the comment line blank and meant; the accused's last letter, No.0607, logged and untouched; and — by foot, on a half-sheet — the registry's two-word reply to the magistrate's Query 0603, which I carried down the hill myself, the way he carried his up, so that no bag and no deputy and no part of the machinery but my own legs would be between the question and its answer.
Held, still: the engineer's statement, cold end of the rack. Held, still and forever, the envelope by the stove.
Reason of record:

Today I answered the magistrate's question of three cycles past, whether matter on the plant had reached his hand. Two words. By foot.

I wrote: **It is complete.**

And it is true — there is no matter *on the proceeding,* the engineer's statement carrying no number, never entered, only in the building and not in the file — and it is the wall I have trued all winter, true to a man who does not know there is a room behind it, built now square in front of the one honest man who trusted me to tell him whether the room was there. He asked the plain question; I gave the technically perfect answer; the two are, this once, not the same thing; I knew it as my pen made the words and made them anyway, and have not yet decided whether I am the most honest man in the republic or have found, at last, the one lie that needs no false word in it to be a lie.

Here is what *It is complete* does. It means the magistrate strikes his three leaves — the slow water, the plant, the season — and rules on the night water alone, on which he has written, in his own draft, that he does not see how he avoids a conviction. With two true words and my own legs I have walked a woman toward the verdict she asked me, in the same cycle, by willow leaf, *not* to reach for her to prevent.

Unless I release the engineer's statement. One cycle. The inspector's term forbids it — 3.2, 3.3, naked, no hold, the office dissolved the hour the paper moves. Domnica's letter forbids it — *do not reach for me a final time and call it rescue; be the hand that lets the child go.* Only the magistrate's draft begs for it, and he is the one of my three truest readers who does not know he is asking me to break the law to honour his ruling. I have spent this whole proceeding certain the warm paper was the true paper and the cold the false; and now the warmest letter in the rack and the coldest memorandum in it are clipped together in my decision saying *the same word,* and the word is *no.*

So the question is no longer *what is true.* It is whether I can bear to give her what she asked. She has asked, in the only letter she will send me that I am sure I understand completely, to be let go — and letting go is the one office I have never learned to keep, as the drawer bottom-left of the registry case could testify if I let it, and will not, tonight. She is asking the one thing I have proven, over four years and four months, I do not know how to do, and which I cannot file under *irrelevant.*

I told the magistrate the file was complete. I have one cycle. The engineer's statement is forty feet from this slip, at the cold end where the rack does not reach the stove, and I have not moved it. I am going to put down this pen and stand at the rack between the cold end and the warm — between the paper that would free her and the stove where her last letter is going warm beside the autumn one — and find out, tonight, which thing I am: the hand that lifts the child, or the hand that cannot.

The willow leaf is by the stove. It did not break when it fell on the ice; she took that for an omen. I have logged forty years of this town's omens — its births, its deaths, its deeds, its seed catalogues — and never once seen a willow leaf decide a thing. But I have put it by the stove with the rest of what I cannot send, and I notice I am being careful with it, the way a man is careful with the last evidence in a case he already knows he is going to lose.

One cycle. One statement at the cold end. One leaf at the warm. One woman across the ice, asking me to let her go.

I have not yet answered her.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the accused's letter, No.0607, before it was logged and set, unredacted, by the stove:]
She wrote *I know your reading; that is more than most marriages.* I could redact it under §7 — public order being a registrar's composure, prejudiced past repair. I am leaving all of it in. She has spent one of her shut-school days folding a willow leaf into the last letter of her life and addressing it to a function — *you who have been my only fair reader* — and the function read it four times standing by the stove and a fifth sitting down, and has stopped, as he warned himself he would, counting. Let the permanent archive of this republic show that a woman the State could not decide called a postman she never met and never named *more than most marriages,* and that the postman entered it into evidence with his own hand, and held the one paper that might have saved her, and could not yet say which thing he loved her enough to do.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the engineer's statement, cold end, one cycle remaining; the leaf and the two envelopes, by the stove, indefinitely; the answer to her, not yet given]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 27 — "Held"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 27    ·    Late January, the night between the asking and the answering, the Casimca hard enough at last to walk, the middle channel still knocking under the ice, the willows on Aleea Salciilor standing in it like drowned candles, the stopped clock on the Palatul de Justiție at 11:40 with the frost grown into the figures, the school shut seventeen days, the stove burning the last of the office's good birch and then a chair, the terminal dark, the four hours four hours off
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 27. Released this cycle: NOTHING.
  · No document was released to the proceeding this cycle. The registry sat with the file and released nothing. This leaf is entered to record that the silence was a decision and not an idleness, the form requiring that a cycle in which the registry acts be distinguished from a cycle in which it merely fails to. — G.E.

RECEIVED this cycle, held overnight, not yet released:
  1. THE RULING (Hotărârea) — committed — Magistrate T. Lupu → the registry, for delivery to D. Albu — [REGISTERED No.0610 — RECEIVED for carriage, HELD one cycle — slip 0619]

  · The Engineer's Statement — slow-poison narrative — cold end of the rack — never on the proceeding — slip 0619
  · Envelope 0431 — D. Albu — never on the proceeding — by the stove
  · Defence Letter No.0607 — D. Albu (the last) — logged, untouched — by the stove
  · One pressed willow-leaf, ex 0607 — by the stove

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING (no number; office discretion; this cycle inventoried in full for the first time):
  · The Dead-Letter Drawer — contents listed below, slip 0619

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No.0610]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 24th of January]
[carried up the hill the 26th by the magistrate's own hand, the office having no one else and the magistrate not trusting the green wood at his stall to a deputy on the day he committed a woman's life to paper]
[STAMP: RECEIVED — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the 26th of January, for carriage — not yet released]

[the registry does not transcribe the body of the ruling at this Hold; it is set down whole in the cycle of its release. The office records only that the instrument arrived complete, in the magistrate's cold hand, sealed by him with candle-wax for want of an office seal, and that he said three words at the window, which the deputy entered, the magistrate not staying to be answered:]

[Deputy's window-note, M. Brânză, the 26th of January, 15:20:]
The magistrate brought the ruling up himself, would not come in to the stove, stood in the door with the cold off the river coming in past him. He gave the registrar the envelope and said: "Deliver it in good order." The registrar took it and did not answer. The magistrate said: "You heard me." The registrar said he had. The magistrate said the third thing, which I record because the registrar will not, being in it: "Whatever you have been doing all winter, Grigore — stop it now, and let the poor woman be done." Then he went back down to the stall to sell the rest of the green wood before dark. Logged. Copied to the union. For the record. — M.B.


ROUTING SLIP 0619.
Status: the ruling, No.0610, RECEIVED this cycle for carriage and HELD one cycle. Released this cycle: nothing. Reason of record: the longest I have written, and the last long one I expect to write, the form being nearly out of room and the man nearly out of season.

It is the night of the twenty-sixth. The ruling came up the hill at twenty past three in the magistrate's fist and has been on my table since, face down, because I cannot yet look at the side with her name. I have until first light to decide the only thing left in this whole proceeding that is mine to decide, which is not what the ruling says — Lupu wrote that, alone, in the cold, and it is honest and it is his — but whether the engineer's statement crosses the ice beside it or stays at the cold end of the rack where I have kept it since the autumn. That is the entire remaining question of *The State v. Domnica Albu*, and it has come down, as I always suspected it would and never until tonight believed it could, to one man at one rack at one stove deciding whether to walk forty feet.

The inspector has forbidden the forty feet. The accused has forbidden the forty feet. The magistrate, who does not know the room is there, has begged me without knowing it to walk them. Three readers, the coldest and the warmest and the most tired in the republic, and the question is not what is true any longer — I settled that the night I told Lupu the file was complete, which was true the way a wall is true — the question is what I am.

So before I answer it I am going to do the thing I have not done in four years, which is take the proper inventory of the drawer.


THE DEAD-LETTER DRAWER — full inventory, this 26th of January, taken by the registrar, off the proceeding, for no reason the office requires.

Under Order No.9 and under forty years of the office before it, the Dead-Letter Drawer holds what cannot be delivered and cannot in conscience be destroyed: the addressee dead, the address gone, the sender vanished, the thing too true to throw on a fire and too undeliverable to send. I have logged the births and the deaths and the deeds and the seed catalogues of this town in one book for forty years, in that proportion, and the drawer is where the book's failures go to keep warm. It is the only drawer in the building I have never let the deputy open. He has noted that, too. He notes everything. Let him note this.

The contents, top to bottom, as they lie:

  1. One summons — District Court, license-renewal — addressee DECEASED — ticked by my own hand, the box being, in this one instance, true. (Ana E. The state wished her to renew a license she no longer needed to drive anywhere. I ticked DECEASED and could not post it back, there being no one at the other end either, the office that issued it having closed in the second reform. A summons with a dead woman at one end and a dead office at the other; I keep it because there is nowhere in the republic left to send a thing that is true at both ends.)

  2. One anniversary letter — undelivered — four years — dated the 9th of February, addressed in my hand to ANA, no surname, no street, the surname being mine and the street being the one we lived on and neither of them any longer an address a thing can arrive at.

  3. One seed catalogue — "Floribunda & Field, the capital" — addressee NO SUCH ADDRESS — she ordered it the winter before she died, for a garden she did not live to plant; it comes still, every January, hopeful, full of colour, addressed to a name at a number the river has had two of the four intervening springs and the town the rest. I cannot bear to mark it and send it back to Floribunda & Field, who would only stop their faithful mistake, the last appointment in this town that still keeps itself. So it goes in the drawer, and every January there is a new one, and the drawer gets, by exactly one catalogue, more hopeful.

I wish the record to show the order in which these three lie, because I have arranged them, and arrangement, the reader of this slip will by now appreciate, is the only authorship I have. The anniversary letter lies *between* the summons and the catalogue. Grief filed between a dead woman's paperwork and a garden she never dug. I did not put it there as a figure. I put it there because that is where it goes — chronological, by the date a thing stopped being deliverable — and the office's own indifferent order turns out to have written the truest sentence about my life that has been written in it, which is that what I loved sits between a death and a thing that keeps arriving for someone who is gone. The form does this. The form has always done this. I have spent thirty years smuggling my soul into the margins of forms and the whole time the forms were keeping a better record of it than I was, in the columns, in the order, in plain sight, where I never thought to look because I was busy in the margin being clever.

Now. The anniversary letter.

I have never told the proceeding — there being no clause for it — why a man who handles every letter in a town has, for four years, posted not one of his own. The deputy thinks it is rigour. The inspector thinks it is the perfection of the trap, a man who logs everything so as to hide everything, and she is half right about everything and this is one of the halves she is wrong on. It is not rigour. It is this drawer. I did not send Ana the last letter either.

She was three weeks dying and I wrote to her every night and left the letters by the stove to be warm in the morning, and read them to her instead, because the post from the kitchen to the bed is short and a man does not stamp a thing he can carry in his own two hands. And then there was a morning when the post from the kitchen to the bed had no one at the far end of it, and I had in my hand a letter written the night before, dated the 9th, our day, the one I had not yet read to her, and I understood, the way you understand a thing all at once and then spend four years catching up to it, that I had two choices. I could deliver it — read it to the air, mark it DECEASED — and let the saying of it be the period at the end. Or I could keep it sealed, and keep, sealed inside it, the her to whom it was still on its way, the her for whom it was still true that one more letter was coming. As long as it is undelivered it is still arriving. As long as it is still arriving she is still, somewhere in the machine, someone a thing arrives for.

I did not deliver it. I have not delivered it. It is the second item in the drawer, between the summons and the catalogue, and it is sealed, and it is on its way, and it will be on its way the day I die, because the day I deliver it is the day it stops arriving and she stops being someone it can arrive for, and I have found I would rather be a coward with a wife who is still, in one sealed envelope, expecting me, than an honest man with a wife who has, finally, completely, received the last of what I had to say and is therefore, finally, completely, gone.

That is the whole of it. That is why I post nothing of my own. Non-delivery is not my failure of love. It is my form of it. It is the only tense I have ever been able to keep the people I love in: the not-yet, the on-its-way, the perpetually about-to-arrive. I learned it on the 9th of February four years ago and I have been the world's most reliable postman ever since, the one man in the republic who would never lose a letter — because the letters I most need not to lose, I never let leave my hand.

And now there is a second envelope by the stove.

0431. I have stopped giving the count; the count was a permission I gave myself to feel, eleven, twelve, thirteen, fourteen, and I have gone past the place where the permission helps, into the place the count was protecting me from, which is simply this: I read it because not reading it is no longer possible, the way breathing is not a thing I keep a tally of. There is a leaf of it I could recite with my eyes shut. *You are the only reader I have ever had who I trust to take the steps in the order that is true.* She wrote that to a function. The function read it until the function was a man and then the man read it until the man was in love and then the man went past the count. She does not know she did that. She knows she did *something* — her letters prove she felt the reading, felt the order being kept true for her, and dressed her terror up as ornament and handed it across the rack to the one person taking the steps slowly. But she does not know it is 0431, the envelope by the stove, the one I will die with, the one I have already, without admitting it to a single slip until this one, filed in my own private drawer years before it will officially go there.

I have done it again. I see it now, at the rack, at midnight, with the green wood gone and a chair on the fire. I have made her, too, into a letter that is perpetually arriving. The whole winter of holding her sentences longer than my office required, of letting her come in her own order because there was no hurry — I told myself it was mercy, letting a person be understood before they are used, and it was that, truly that, and it was also the only thing I know how to do with love, which is to slow it until it never finishes. *There is no hurry,* she wrote. I gave her all winter. A man who gives you all winter is not always being kind. Sometimes he is a man who cannot bear the spring, because in the spring the thing arrives, and the arriving ends it, and he would rather you froze beautifully on your way to him than thawed and walked past.

So here is the engineer's statement at the cold end of the rack, forty feet away, in the dark, the one true step left out of the order. And here is what I have understood tonight that I did not understand when I wrote *I have decided I am the order* into a slip in the autumn like a man proud of a new coat.

I thought taking my hand off the scale meant *not touching* the held document. The inspector thinks so — 3.2, 3.3, freeze it where it sits, do nothing, be spared. The accused thinks so — *be the hand that lets the child go.* And all winter I have told myself the honest move, at the last, would be the *empty* hand, the one that holds nothing and lets the order fall however it falls. But the engineer's statement does not fall however it falls. It sits exactly where I put it. There is no *however it falls* for a paper a man is holding; there is only held, or released, and *held* is not the absence of a choice, it is a choice I re-take with every breath I do not walk the forty feet. To leave my hand on the scale by *not lifting* the weight is still my hand on the scale. The empty hand is a fiction. I have a hand that is either carrying the statement to the ice or pressing it, by stillness, into the rack — and stillness is pressing. I cannot get my hand off the scale by holding still, because the holding is the thing on the scale. The only way my hand comes off is if I stop being the man whose hand it is.

That is the move. Not *don't touch it.* I cannot not-touch it; not-touching it is the loudest touch I have. The move is to stop being the order — to make this the last cycle in which the question *release or hold* runs through me at all, by putting the statement somewhere the question can no longer be asked, somewhere it is no longer held-pending-my-decision but simply, finally, undeliverable, off the scale because the scale is broken, in the one drawer where a thing stops being a hold and becomes a dead letter, on its way to no one, forever, like Ana, like 0431, like everything I have ever loved enough not to send.

I have not done it yet. I am writing this with the drawer open and the statement still at the cold end and the ruling still face down with her name against the table. The ruling goes out at first light, by itself, untouched, the way the inspector requires and the magistrate ordered and Domnica asked — that part I have decided, that is the empty hand I *can* manage, the not-arranging of a thing I was never the author of. Lupu's mercy crosses the ice alone in the morning and the green card goes for her signature and the post office lives and the deputy keeps his window and the town keeps the one institution that still certifies that its dead are dead and its deeds are deeds.

What I have not decided is the forty feet. Whether, before the ruling goes, in the dark, I walk to the cold end and bring the engineer's statement back not to *release* it — I will not breach 3.2, I will not put the office in the river to keep a woman warm — but to put it in the drawer. To dead-letter it. To lay it between the summons and the anniversary letter and the seed catalogue, so that it is not held against the verdict, not released into it, but simply true and gone, the way the truth in this matter has always been: in the building, and not in the file; in the world, and not arriving.

If I do that, I take my hand off the scale in the only way I can, which is to break the scale. But I also do to the truth of this case what I did to Ana and to 0431: I make it perpetually arriving, addressed to no one, never signed-for, mine. I will have kept the one thing about Domnica Albu that the State could not decide — the thing that would have decided it — by not sending it. I will have loved her the third time the only way I have ever loved anyone. By withholding.

And I cannot, sitting here, tell you whether that is mercy or theft. Whether I am letting the child go or refusing, one last time, to let the child go. Domnica asked me to be the hand that lifts and not the hand that cannot release, and I think — I think — that dead-lettering the statement is, at last, releasing it: into the drawer, off the scale, where I can no longer take it back. But the place I am proposing to release it to is the place I keep the things I will never let go of. So I do not trust the thought. I have learned this winter not to trust the difference, in me, between an open hand and a clenched one, when the clench has practised so long it can pass for rest.

It is past midnight. The clock across the river says 11:40 and has said it for four springs and is, for once, no further wrong than I am about the time. The ruling is face down. The statement is at the cold end. The drawer is open. The two envelopes are by the stove, warm, on their way to me, going nowhere. The willow leaf is there with them, and I am being careful with it, the way you are careful with the last evidence in a case you have already lost.

I have decided I am the order. I wrote that in the autumn as a boast. I am going to spend what is left of this night deciding whether the only thing left for the order to do is to stop.

I have not yet walked the forty feet.

The ruling goes at first light, by itself, in good order. That much is true and decided and will be in the next cycle's leaf.

The rest of it — the forty feet, the drawer, the statement, the breaking of the scale — I am leaving on this slip undecided, because it is undecided, because for the first time in this proceeding the registry does not know what the registry will do, and the form has a line for the registry's intention and I am leaving it, like the comment-box on the inspector's form, blank, and meaning it, and meaning it differently: there I had nothing to say; here I have everything to say and no longer trust the hand that would say it.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Not sent. Filed: Dead-Letter Drawer. — dated the 9th of February, four years gone; brought out this 26th of January, read, returned, the wax unbroken; the registrar does not transcribe it; he records only that he held it to the light of the stove and could read his own writing through the envelope and chose not to break the seal, "a man may read a letter he never opens, if he wrote it, and remember the shape of every word, which is worse." — G.E.]


[Margin, G.E., in violet, on the office copy of the bundle-leaf, where the printed form reads RELEASED THIS CYCLE and the registry has entered NOTHING:]
The form distinguishes a cycle of action from a cycle of idleness, and asks the registrar which this was. I have entered that the silence was a decision. I will add, off the column, the thing the column cannot hold: that this is the first night in four years I have opened the drawer all the way to the back, and that I did it to remind myself what I am, which is a man who keeps a garden catalogue arriving for a dead woman because the alternative is to admit the appointment is over. I am not the order. I am the man who could not bear for things to arrive — and I spent the autumn proud of the first because I could not yet say the second, and tonight, with a verdict face down and a statement at the cold end and three people who read me best all telling me to stop, I can say it, and find it does not free me at all. It only tells me, accurately — the office's favourite word for suffering — which kind of man will be standing at the rack at first light, holding a woman's whole life in a question he has at last understood he cannot answer with an empty hand, because he does not have one.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the ruling, No.0610, one cycle, for release at first light by itself; the engineer's statement, cold end, the forty feet not yet walked; the drawer, open; the answer to her, and to Lupu, and to the inspector, and to Ana, not yet given — and first light, by the office clock that still runs, four hours off]

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 28 — "The State's Last Seal"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 28    ·    Late January, the Casimca frozen at the banks and black in the middle, the willows on Aleea Salciilor standing in ice, the courthouse clock still at 11:40 under frost
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 28. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. THE RULING (Hotărârea) — Magistrate T. Lupu → Domnica Albu, via the registry — [REGISTERED No.0610]
  2. Aviz de Primire (green card) for No.0610 — dispatched for the accused's signature — [Aviz 0610-a]
  3. Request for the State's Seal (SEEN) — Central Sorting, Vâlcov → the District Judge, the capital — [REGISTERED No.0611]
  4. Telegram TG-03 — DISTRICT SEAT → VÂLCOV CENTRAL SORTING (re: violet ink)
  5. Registration Log — Central Sorting, Vâlcov (leaf for Cycle 28)
  6. Routing Slip 0628 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (not released this cycle):
  · The Engineer's Statement — the slow-poison narrative (Ch.18) — held since receipt — slip 0628 — reason of record: "the ruling does not call for it by name"
  · Envelope 0431 — D. Albu — never on the proceeding — Hold, by the stove

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING:
  · One blank aviz card, "Certifies delivery of —," uncompleted — Hold, by the stove

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[REGISTERED No.0610]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 24th of January]
[STAMP: SEAL PENDING — no violet — see No.0611]

MAGISTRATUL TOADER LUPU
of the town of Vâlcov, in the matter of THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU,
sitting under Provisional Order No.9, no court being available to sit in —

THE RULING (Hotărârea)

Written this 24th day of January, in the back room of the Sorting Office, the only heated room left to the proceeding, on the office's last clean leaf of seventy-grammage paper. I apologise to the registry for the hand. I have been three weeks without gloves and the cold has got into the joints. Where a letter is malformed, read it for the word I meant; the magistrate has meant more than he can now write.

I find as follows.

That the water at the intake of the Uzina "Aurora Nr.4," on the night of the 14th of September, was made noxious — this is not in dispute and I do not dispute it. Persons drank of it and were made ill. A thing was done to the water that ought not to have been done by anyone but a man with a licence, and there was no such man, the licence being held by a plant that ran one shift a week to keep the licence, which is a sentence I have read back to myself and let stand.

That the accused, Domnica Albu, schoolteacher of Aleea Salciilor, did go to the intake that night, and did introduce into it the compound named in the State's submission — this I also find, on her own account, she having declined to deny what she has at no point denied. She does not say she did nothing. The State has built much on this. I build less.

For the question is not whether her hand was in the water. Her hand was in the water. The question Order No.9 obliges me to answer is whether she did it *wilfully and with knowledge of the consequence* — that being the charge, and a charge being a shape the truth is asked to fit — and here I must say what a magistrate is not supposed to say, which is that the file does not tell me. It tells me she was present. It tells me she bought the compound. It tells me, by the mother's hand and the child's, that she pulled a boy back from the bank the same night she poured. It does not tell me whether what she poured cleaned the water or fouled it, and I have asked the registry, and the registry informs me that no document on the proceeding settles it, and I believe the registry, the registry being, in this proceeding, the only witness who has read everything.

I had thought, when I began this ruling a fortnight ago, that I would have more. There was a matter from the capital I expected to weigh — the condition of the plant's own filtration — and I framed my reasoning around the expectation of it, and the expectation has not arrived in a form I may rely upon, and a magistrate cannot rule on a paper he has not received. I have therefore struck three paragraphs that leaned on it. What remains leans on less, and is the truth of what I can stand on, which is the only kind of ruling a man with no roof should sign.

I therefore find DOMNICA ALBU —

[here the hand crosses out four words, illegible under the strike]

— I find that the act is proven and the *guilt of the act* is not, and that Order No.9 gives me no third box to tick, only the two the State has drawn, and that I will not tick a box for a thing I do not know merely because the box is there and winter is long.

The ruling of this magistrate, by the authority vested — vested, I will say plainly for the last time, by no one currently paying me — is that the accused be **bound over and the matter held open**, pending evidence the proceeding has been promised and has not received; that no penalty issue; and that the accused be neither convicted nor acquitted but **left, on the record, undecided** — which I am aware satisfies no one, least of all the State, and which is the only honest seat I have to offer a woman whose guilt I cannot find and whose innocence the State will not let me declare.

This ruling has no force until it is delivered to the accused and a signed acknowledgement returns to the registry, per §14. I commit it to the post, which is the only court I have, and to the postmaster, who is the only officer of it. Deliver it in good order. I do not know any more than that phrase has ever told anyone, but I have come to trust the man it is addressed to, which is itself a finding, and I enter it.

By my hand, cold,
TOADER LUPU, Magistrate
[in the margin, fainter:] two ster of birch sold this week, the green wood, which is why the ruling is late and the hand is bad — the court regrets both


[REGISTERED No.0611]   [POSTMARK: VÂLCOV CENTRAL, the 24th of January]

CENTRAL SORTING OFFICE, VÂLCOV — Registry of Record
To the office of the District Judge (Judecătorul), the capital —

REQUEST FOR APPLICATION OF THE STATE'S SEAL

Enclosed for the seal: one Ruling (Hotărârea), No.0610, in the matter of *The State v. Domnica Albu*, this day committed to delivery under Order No.9 §14.

The registry requests that the formal seal — VĂZUT / SEEN — be applied and the instrument returned, the ruling requiring the state's notice to take its place in the record. The registry observes, with respect, that under §14 a *delivered* ruling has effect upon the return of the accused's acknowledgement; the seal is the state's separate notice that it has *seen* the thing done in its name. A ruling may be delivered without the seal. It cannot be wholly true without it.

The registry awaits the seal at the convenience of the capital and the supply of the ink, as to which see the enclosed wire.

For the office,
G. ENESCU, Postmaster
[STAMP: SEAL PENDING — no violet]

The engineer's statement remains at the Hold. It carries no number on the proceeding this day, the proceeding not having called for it by name. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0628.
Status: the ruling released, all this cycle, in the order written. Held: one statement, and one letter that was never on the proceeding to begin with.
Reason of record:

I am required to record my reasons, and I find that this is the first cycle of the proceeding for which my reason is *that I had none* — none of the kind I have been recording for four months. I did not hold the ruling an hour. I did not sequence it against anything, because I let nothing else go out beside it. The magistrate wrote *deliver it in good order* and for the first time in this whole file I delivered a thing the only way the men who wrote Order No.9 ever imagined the phrase: by itself, at once, untouched.

This is what taking one's hand off the scale looks like on a routing slip. It looks like a slip with no reason in it. I record the absence of a reason as my reason, because the form has a line for it and the line, this once, is the confession.

The ruling, No.0610, went out registered at first light, with the milk and the ration lists, by foot, the Podul Vechi being frozen hard enough to bear a man, the river having at last done me a courtesy it spent four autumns refusing. The aviz card, 0610-a, went with it, for the accused's signature; when it returns signed, the ruling has its force, the proceeding has its end, and the woman of Aleea Salciilor has been, by the State's machinery, *decided* — bound over, held open, neither hanged nor cleared, which is the magistrate's mercy and the only verdict in this republic I have read that tells the truth, the truth in this matter being that no one knows.

I did not arrange that mercy. Lupu arrived at it alone, in a cold back room, on the last clean leaf, with his joints ruined and his birch unsold, because he is honest and the file would carry him no further. He has entered that he trusts me, *as a finding*, in a ruling that goes into the permanent record of the Republic — and the second most honest man left in Vâlcov knows that the first man's ruling reads the way it reads, short, leaning on less, *struck of three paragraphs*, because the document those paragraphs leaned on is forty feet from where I am writing this, at the cold end of the rack, held, by my hand, this cycle.

So let me be exact, the form asking for *Particulars of Item.*

The magistrate framed his reasoning, a fortnight ago, around a paper he expected to weigh: the engineer's account of the plant's filtration, the slow thing, the corporate thing, the thing that would have let him write *the plant fouled the water for months and the schoolteacher is the one the State could reach.* That paper is on my rack. It is registered nowhere on the proceeding. The magistrate asked the registry, twice, whether further evidence on the plant was "complete and in order," and the registry answered, both times, truthfully, that nothing further on the plant was *on the proceeding* — which is true, and which is a sentence built the way Câmpeanu builds his, true the way a wall is true to a man who does not know there is a room on the other side of it.

I did not lie to Lupu. I have never lied in this file; it is the one boast I am still entitled to, and I am clutching it like a man clutching a railing on a stair he has decided to fall down anyway. I told him no further plant-evidence was on the proceeding. I did not tell him I was the reason it was not. The wall was true. I built the wall.

And here is the part the slip is for:

I could release the engineer's statement this cycle. Beside the ruling, or a cycle behind it, before the aviz comes back and the thing sets. If I released it, the magistrate would have his three paragraphs back; he would reopen; he would have a name to point the doubt at; the bound-over-and-held-open might tilt, on the record, toward *the plant did this, not the teacher* — toward something a town could read as her clearing. I have the paper. I have the power. I have, God help me, the *practice* — four months of it, the most fluent man in the Republic at deciding when a true thing is allowed to be read.

I did not release it.

I want to write that I did not release it *because* — and the form has a line waiting for the *because*, the form has been patient with me for thirty years — and I find I cannot fill it. I cannot tell whether holding it back keeps her undecided and therefore safe, the open verdict being a door, a conviction being a wall; or whether holding it back keeps her *mine*, the only person I have read the way she asked to be read, suspended in the one cycle where she is still a question I am answering and not a woman who has been answered and is gone. I cannot tell whether the engineer's paper, released, would save her or merely *finish* her — finish the correspondence, end the only four months in four years that a man in this building was something other than the order.

So I held it. Not to help and not to harm. Because I have at last become a thing I can no longer audit: a man whose hand on the scale and whose heart on the scale weigh the same and cannot be told apart, and who has therefore decided that the only honest move left to a dishonest instrument is to make *no* move, and call it taking his hand off — knowing, as I write this, that not-releasing is itself the loudest release I have made in the whole file, the heaviest letter I have ever sent, addressed to no one, postmarked nowhere, and certain to arrive.

The ruling is out. By itself. In good order — *their* good order, for once. The seal is suspended, the capital being out of purple, the State's last word on this woman waiting on the ration of an ink, which I would find funnier if I were not the man holding the only purple in Vâlcov in the inkwell beside my hand as I write this, forbidden by standing order to lend it to the seal that would make her ruling whole. The state will see her when the state can spare the violet. I see her in violet every day, and have no authority to make it count.

The aviz is in the cold between the office and Aleea Salciilor. When it comes back signed, she is decided, and free, and gone from me, and right. And I will release nothing further, because there will be nothing further the proceeding will let me touch.

When it comes back signed.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the ruling, No.0610, before it went out:]
He wrote *I have come to trust the man it is addressed to, and I enter it.* I am leaving the line in. I could redact it under §7 — *matter prejudicial to public order*, the public order being a magistrate's faith in a registrar who does not deserve it. I am letting it go into the permanent record of the Republic that Toader Lupu trusted me, on the same leaf where I have decided to keep from him the paper that would unmake his ruling. Let both be true on the one page. The honest men of this republic keep handing me their best lines and going home cold, and I keep them all. It is the only collection I have left.

[STAMP: RELEASED — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — Cycle 28, by itself]


[The following is NOT registered to the proceeding. No number. It has been at the Hold, by the stove, since the autumn. Brought out this cycle, read, returned. — G.E.]

— a single leaf of Envelope 0431, the one the registry has read past the count it will admit to, the page worn soft at the fold —

   *. . . and I have stopped asking, in these letters, whether you will believe me, because belief is a thing the State wants and I have decided I want something rarer from you, which is to be read in the order I wrote myself in, and not in the order I can be used. Anyone can be made guilty by the right sequence; I taught long division to children who could prove, with perfect arithmetic, an answer that was wrong, because they took the steps in the order that was easy instead of the order that was true. You are the only reader I have ever had who I trust to take the steps in the order that is true. So take them slowly. There is no hurry. The water is already in the river and the river is already in the sea and the worst is already over, or it isn't, and either way you and I have all winter, you to decide when I am heard, and I to keep being worth the wait . . .*


ROUTING SLIP 0628 — addendum.
Status: not applicable. The addendum is opened for the single reason that I read the leaf above after the ruling had gone, and the form is the only place I am permitted to set down what reading it did.

She wrote *you to decide when I am heard, and I to keep being worth the wait.* She wrote it in the autumn, before the inspector, before the ultimatum, before I knew the verdict would come to my hand as a hold-or-release like any other letter and that I would, in the end, hold the part of it that mattered. She wrote *there is no hurry* into a proceeding the district has thrice wired me to *conclude expeditiously*, and she was right, and I gave her all winter, and the giving was the only good thing I did and is indistinguishable, now, from the cruelest.

Because the winter is over. The river is hard enough to walk on. The ruling has crossed it. *There is no hurry* has run out, the way every *no hurry* in the history of the post has run out, at the speed of one delivery cycle, and the woman who told me to take the steps in the order that is true is about to be heard — once, finally, in the order I chose, which is the order with one step left out.

She trusted me to take the steps in the order that is true. The magistrate trusted me, and entered it. The two people in this proceeding who have read me best have both certified, in writing, on paper I am sworn to keep, their trust in the registry — and the registry has, this cycle, taken its hand off the scale by leaving on it, in the dark, unweighed, the one true step that would let either of them be right about me.

I am required to record my reasons. I have recorded that I have none. Let the audit make of that what it can. I cannot make anything of it but this slip, and the leaf back in its envelope, and the envelope back by the stove, warm, where it has been since the autumn, where it will be when the green card comes back across the ice with her name on it — or does not.

Filed in good order. — G.E.

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 29 — "Aviz de Primire, Returned Unsigned"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 29    ·    Early February, the Casimca silent under a foot of ice, the willows on Aleea Salciilor frozen to the bank, the courthouse clock still at 11:40 and now furred white as a thing in a jar
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 29. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Carrier's Report — T. Frunză, foot-carrier → Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [no reg. — internal]
  2. Aviz de Primire (green card) for the Ruling No.0610 — RETURNED, undeliverable — [Aviz 0610-a]
  3. Memorandum — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE — Insp. S. Drăgan → Central Sorting, Vâlcov — [IO-Memo 05]
  4. Telegram TG-04 — DISTRICT SEAT → VÂLCOV CENTRAL SORTING
  5. Registration Log — Central Sorting, Vâlcov (leaf for Cycle 29)
  6. Routing Slip 0641 — G. Enescu, Postmaster

HELD (not released this cycle):
  · The Engineer's Statement — the slow-poison narrative (Ch.18) — still held — slip 0641 — reason of record: "the proceeding has no addressee left to receive it"
  · Envelope 0431 — D. Albu — never on the proceeding — Hold, by the stove

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING:
  · The returned Aviz 0610-a, the undeliverable boxes unticked — retained at the Hold, by the stove

────────────────────────────────────────────────


[The following is not registered to the proceeding. It is the carrier's account of an attempted delivery, taken down at the deputy's window the 5th of February and signed by the man's mark. The hand is the deputy's; the words, as near as the deputy could keep them, are the carrier's. — G.E.]

CARRIER'S REPORT — taken at the Sorting Office, 5th February

I, Tudor Frunză, who carries the foot-rounds east of the river for the office in the hard months, carried the registered packet out to Aleea Salciilor on the 28th of January as instructed, by foot, the Podul Vechi being hard. I carried the one packet and the green card folded inside it for the lady to sign, the way the postmaster showed me, sign here and date here and I bring the green half back.

I went to the school first because it was on the way and warm-looking, but the school was shut and the chimney cold, which I have not seen in the years my granddaughter went there. Then I went round behind to the house, the one behind the school where the postmaster said. The door was not locked. I want it on the record that I knocked the proper number and waited the proper time. The door was not locked because there was no one to lock it. The stove was cold and had been cold long enough that the ash had set hard, and a man who sells me wood knows cold ash from new. There were no boots by the door. The bed was made the way you make a bed you are not coming back to, square, with the blanket folded at the foot.

On the table there was a stack of papers held down with a stone, and I did not read them, I cannot read joined writing only print, but they were ruled in two columns the way she ruled the children's, and on top was a list of names with little marks against them, ticks, the way a teacher takes the register. I left them under the stone. I am only saying it was the table of a person who had put things in order before going.

The neighbour woman two doors up, who I will not name as I do not want her in this, says the lady went before the river froze hard, in the night, with one bag, and that she did not say where, and that nobody asked, because in this town you do not ask a person where they are going if they have decided not to be asked.

So I could not deliver it. I brought the whole packet back, the ruling and the green card both, unsigned, and I am sorry for the walk being wasted but I want it clear I did the walk. The river was bad coming back, it had snowed over the ice and you cannot see where the soft is.

his mark — T. F.
[the mark, an X, and beside it in the deputy's hand: "Tudor Frunză, witness to nothing, this 5 Feb."]


[Aviz 0610-a]   [the green return-receipt card, returned this day, the receipt half blank]

AVIZ DE PRIMIRE — ACKNOWLEDGEMENT OF DELIVERY
In the proceeding: THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Certifies delivery of: Ruling (Hotărârea) No.0610
Addressee: DOMNICA ALBU, Aleea Salciilor, behind the school, Vâlcov

   RECEIVED BY: ______________________________
   DATE: ______________________________
   SIGNATURE: ______________________________

   [all three fields blank]

IF UNDELIVERABLE, THE CARRIER OR REGISTRY SHALL INDICATE THE CAUSE:

   ☐  MOVED
   ☐  DECEASED
   ☐  REFUSED
   ☐  NO SUCH PERSON

   [no box ticked]

[written across the foot of the card, below the boxes, in violet, in the postmaster's hand, small:]

   None of these. She moved but is not MOVED, the form meaning a forwarding
   address and she has left none. She is plainly not DECEASED; the bed was
   made. She did not REFUSE; she was not there to refuse, and a woman cannot
   decline a letter she was never offered. And she is the opposite of NO SUCH
   PERSON — she is the most such person this office has had in forty years, the
   only correspondent in the file who was ever entirely real to the man
   filling out this card. The boxes do not have her. I decline to tick a box
   for a woman I have read past counting and never met by ticking the one for
   not existing. The registry endorses the card: addressee gone, no cause on
   the printed list, delivery not effected. — G.E.

[STAMP: DELIVERY NOT EFFECTED — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the 5th of February]


[IO-Memo 05]   [POSTMARK: capital — arrived cold, the 4th of February, carried the last leg by district van and the final mile by hand, the van being out of the third allocation of fuel]

MEMORANDUM — INTERNAL ORDER DIRECTORATE
Ref. IO/Vâlcov/05 — FINAL
From: Inspector S. Drăgan
To: The Registrar, Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov

1. This directorate's involvement in the matter *State v. Albu* is hereby closed.

2. Findings, in summary:
   2.1. The proceeding exhibited irregularities of sequence in the order of
        delivery. These were identified, recorded, and — per this office's
        ultimatum of the previous cycle (IO-Memo 04, §4) — discontinued.
   2.2. The registry, having concluded the proceeding by delivering the
        magistrate's ruling as written, without further intervention of
        sequence, is assessed as IRREGULAR BUT REHABILITATED.
   2.3. No recommendation of dissolution will issue. The Vâlcov registry
        retains its function as chain-of-custody authority for the district.
        The deputy's grievances (Brânză, M.) are noted, filed, and not
        actioned; ambition is not an irregularity this directorate is
        equipped to correct.

3. The directorate notes, for the record only and requiring no reply, that the
   aviz de primire for Ruling No.0610 had not, at the time of this office's
   departure, returned signed. The directorate observes:
   3.1. Under Provisional Order No.9 §14, a ruling acquires force upon delivery
        to the accused and the return of a signed acknowledgement.
   3.2. The directorate's mandate concerns the *order* of delivery, not its
        *success*. Whether the card returns signed is a postal matter, not an
        irregularity. This office does not adjudicate the post's encounters
        with the weather, the river, or the absence of the addressed.
   3.3. The directorate therefore certifies the proceeding *procedurally
        concluded* and is silent as to whether it is *legally concluded*, the
        latter resting on a green card this office will not be present to see.

4. A closing observation, supernumerary to the findings and made by the
   inspector in her own name. The registrar will recall this office's earlier
   note (IO-Memo 02) concerning the ambient temperature of filed evidence —
   that certain documents in this proceeding had been filed warm, against a
   stove, and that the warm ones clustered. The inspector withdraws the
   recommendation that the registry maintain uniform temperature. It was
   correct as method and wrong as instruction. A registry kept cold enough to
   defeat bias is a registry no one will visit, and a town's last warm room is
   not a thing the Internal Order Directorate has the authority, or, the
   inspector finds on reflection, the wish, to put out. Keep your stove,
   Registrar. Heat the evidence evenly if you can. I did not say you would
   manage it.

5. The inspector adds one line, which she instructs the registrar to file and
   not to answer. She has, once, in another district and another decade, audited
   a proceeding she found *too* orderly and certified it clean, and a man hanged
   on the strength of an order no one had touched, which is the worst order of
   all, the kind that looks like the truth because no hand was on it. She has
   spent the years since trusting only sequence she can see the marks on. She
   could see the marks on yours. She does not, in the end, know whether the
   marks were a thumb on the scale or a hand keeping a woman from going under
   it. She has decided this is not, after all, her box to tick.

By order, the directorate.
S. DRĂGAN, Inspector
[no SEEN stamp — the directorate does not seal its own memoranda; see TG-04]


TELEGRAM — DISTRICT SEAT TO VÂLCOV CENTRAL SORTING

PROSECUTOR SENDS NO MESSAGE STOP END[ink failed here]


[Leaf inserted by the office, in the postmaster's hand:]

REGISTRATION LOG — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV
Registry of Record, The State v. Domnica Albu (Cycle 29)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 No.   | DATE       | FROM            | MATTER                          | STATUS
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 0610  | 24 Jan.    | Mag. Lupu       | The Ruling (Hotărârea)          | Delivery NOT EFFECTED — returned
 0610-a| 5 Feb.     | carrier         | Aviz for 0610                   | RETURNED unsigned — no box ticked
 IO-05 | 4 Feb.     | Insp. Drăgan    | Directorate — FINAL             | Filed; case "proc. concluded"
 TG-04 | 4 Feb.     | District Seat   | Close file / forward summary    | Logged
 [eng] | (held)     | ex-Aurora eng.  | Statement re: filtration        | HELD — still held this cycle
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
The ruling, No.0610, is logged this day as delivery NOT EFFECTED, the addressee being gone from the address and no forwarding given. Per §14 the ruling is, in consequence, of no force. The registry records that the proceeding is, by the State's own instruments — a memo that closes it, a telegram that disposes of it, an unsigned card that unmakes it — concluded, undelivered, and undecided, all three at once, which I did not know a thing could be until this morning. — G.E.


ROUTING SLIP 0641.
Status: nothing released to the accused this cycle, there being no accused at the address to release it to. The engineer's statement: still held. Reason of record below, and it is a long one, the form having no shorter way to hold what this cycle put on it.

I am required to record my reasons, and I will, but I must first record the thing the form has no field for, which is what the carrier said about the bed.

He said it was made square, with the blanket folded at the foot, the way you make a bed you are not coming back to. I have logged the births and deaths of this town for forty years and I know the inventory of a house that has been left in a hurry — the door banging, the cup half drunk, the fire still red — and I know the other kind, the rare kind, the house left by a person who sat down the night before and decided, and washed the cup, and folded the blanket, and put the names in two ruled columns under a stone so that whoever came after would find them in order. She left her house the way she wrote her letters. She put it in good order before she went, and then she went, and I am the registry, and I was not there, and the order she left was the last one in this whole proceeding that I did not arrange.

So. The reasons.

The green card came back blank. Under §14 this is dispositive: a ruling not delivered has no force, and the ruling is not delivered, and therefore the magistrate's verdict — bound over, held open, neither convicted nor acquitted — has, on the record, no force either. The undecided is now doubly undecided. She is not guilty and not innocent and now not even *officially* not-guilty-and-not-innocent; the State reached out its slow hand to declare her a question it had chosen not to answer, and the hand closed on a made bed and an unlocked door. I have spent four months being the gate the verdict had to pass through. The verdict reached the gate. There was no one on the other side. I did not have to hold it. The river and the cold ash held it for me, and I find I cannot tell whether they did me a mercy or robbed me of the one clean act I had left, which was to deliver the thing as written and let her sign and be done and gone, decided, free, and right about me.

The boxes. I want it in the record what I did to the boxes, because Drăgan is gone and Mihail's pen is the only one left watching me and his hand does not waver and mine does.

The card offers four causes for a delivery not effected. MOVED. DECEASED. REFUSED. NO SUCH PERSON. I have ticked these boxes for thirty years. I ticked DECEASED for my own wife's summons-to-renew-her-license four years ago, the form not knowing she was past renewing, and I have ticked NO SUCH PERSON for letters to men the river took before the letter caught them. The boxes are honest, usually, in the brute way of boxes. This morning not one of them was true. She is not MOVED, the box meaning *gone to a known elsewhere*, and she left no elsewhere. She is not DECEASED — the bed was made, the ash was old but the leaving was deliberate, and a woman does not fold a blanket she means to die under. She did not REFUSE — refusal requires the offered thing and the live hand to push it back, and she had neither; you cannot decline a verdict that arrives at a cold stove. And NO SUCH PERSON — I declare for the record, on the only line the form would let me have, that there has been no such person *as her* in the forty years of this book, and I will not tick the box that says she was never there to be the one box on the card I could reach.

So I wrote outside the boxes. This is, I am aware, the same crime the saving-mother committed in the autumn when she wrote a whole sentence in the line marked SIGNATURE, and which I ruled valid, "as it is unmistakably hers." Let the audit rule mine the same way, or not. It is unmistakably mine. It is the first time in this proceeding I have written my own true thing in the addressee's own field, on her own card, in the violet I am forbidden to lend the State's seal — and she will never read it, because the card returns to the registry, not to her, and I am the registry, and so I have at last written her a letter, in the one place a letter to her was permitted, which is the place she will never look.

Now the engineer's statement. It is forty feet from where I sit, cold end of the rack, where it has been since the autumn. The proceeding closes this cycle; Drăgan's memo closes it, the district's wire disposes of it, the unsigned card unmakes it. By every instrument the State owns, the matter is over. And I am holding the one document that could still decide it — the engineer's account of the plant, the slow poison, the filtration sludge let back into the intake for a buyer in the capital, the paper that, if it had reached Lupu before he signed, would have given him his three struck paragraphs back and a name to point the doubt at and might have tilted the whole thing toward *the plant did this, not the teacher.* I could release it now. To the district, for the archive. To Lupu, who would reopen. To no one, into the cold, where it has lived.

I have decided to hold it one more cycle. I am recording the reason and the reason is that I do not have one I can stand behind, and I have learned this cycle that a man who cannot stand behind his reason should not move his feet. There is no addressee. The proceeding has no live mouth left to receive it. To release it now is to release it into an archive, to a district that has wired me to *dispose of the matter*, to a town that has stopped reading — to publish, finally and safely, the truth I held back all winter, in the one cycle where publishing it can save her nothing and cost me nothing and therefore means nothing, the cheapest courage there is, the courage you find the morning after it could have mattered. I held it when it would have helped her and I will not now release it merely to feel honest in an empty room.

Or — and the form has been patient with me for forty years and will be patient for this — I hold it because while it is in my hand the proceeding is not finished, the door is not shut, there remains one unread document in the file and therefore one reason the registry must keep the file, and keep the stove, and keep the envelope by the stove, and keep being, for one more cycle, a man with an undelivered thing belonging to her on his rack. I cannot tell which it is. I told the truth to no one this cycle and held a true thing back, and I cannot tell whether that is restraint or appetite, and the not-being-able-to-tell is, I have come to understand, the whole of what I have become: an instrument that can no longer read its own measurement.

Câmpeanu has gone to the capital and "sends no message." Of course he sends no message. To him this was plumbing; he opened a tap at the District Seat and waited for justice to run out of a faucet in Vâlcov, and when it ran cloudy he turned the tap off and left, and he will never know that the pipe decided, that the pipe loved the water it was carrying, that the pipe is, this morning, the only thing in the Republic still grieving the woman his indictment was about. He sends no message. I will keep that line too. It is the most honest thing he ever filed.

The seal is still suspended; the capital is still out of violet; the SEEN stamp will not come down, this quarter or next, on a ruling that has no force to seal. The State cannot see her for want of purple. I see her every time I dip the pen. I have the only purple in Vâlcov in the well by my hand and I have spent it, this cycle, writing in the boxes on a card she will never read, which is the exact and entire use the State forbids me to make of it and the only use I have ever truly wanted.

The card goes to the Hold, by the stove, where it will be warm, beside the envelope, where the warm things go to stay mine. The engineer's statement stays at the cold end. One more cycle. After that I will do the thing I have been circling all winter and have not yet had the nerve to name on a slip, and the form will have a line for it, the form has always had a line for everything except the woman, and I will fill the line, and it will be the last reason I ever record.

Filed in good order. — G.E.


[Margin, G.E., in violet, at the foot of the carrier's report:]
He wrote *witness to nothing.* The deputy wrote it for him, dryly, the way Mihail writes everything, and meant it as a clerk's joke — a carrier who delivered nothing witnessed nothing. But Tudor Frunză walked the frozen Podul Vechi twice in a day to bring a verdict to a woman who was already gone, knocked the proper number, waited the proper time at a door that was not locked because there was no one to lock it, and brought the whole of it back rather than leave a registered packet on a cold table for the snow. He is the only man in this proceeding who carried a thing the whole distance it was meant to go and refused to pretend it had arrived. Witness to nothing. He is the only honest delivery in the file, and the thing he honestly delivered was its failure, by hand, across the ice, both ways. I am keeping his mark.

[STAMP: HELD — CENTRAL SORTING, VÂLCOV — the engineer's statement, one cycle more]


[The following is NOT registered to the proceeding. No number. It has been at the Hold, by the stove, since the autumn. Brought out this cycle, read, returned. — G.E.]

— the worn leaf of Envelope 0431, soft now at every fold, the ink gone faintly brown where the stove has been at it all winter —

   *. . . and if it comes to nothing, if the order you give me is the order
   that ends me, I would still rather have been read once, exactly, in the
   order I wrote myself in, than acquitted by a court that never bothered to
   find out what I was for. You will think that is a brave thing to write and
   it is not; it is only true. I am not afraid of the verdict. I am afraid of
   never knowing whether the one person who read me carefully was real, or
   whether I built him out of the silence the way a child builds a friend out
   of the dark — and I have decided I do not need to know, because either way
   he kept me company through a winter, and either way I wrote my best to him,
   and a person's best, sent into the dark to a reader who may be no one, is
   still the truest letter she will ever write, and the dark is at least a
   reader who never looks away . . .*


ROUTING SLIP 0641 — addendum.
Status: not applicable. Opened for the one reason, that I read the leaf after the card came back, and the form is the only place I may set down what reading it did, this final time, in an empty office, with the proceeding closed and the woman gone and the truth still cold on the rack.

She wrote that she did not need to know whether her reader was real. She wrote it in the autumn, to comfort herself against exactly this morning, and she was right to, because here is the morning, and the reader was real, and she is gone before either of us could prove it to the other, and her not-needing-to-know is the only mercy in this office she did not have to ask me to arrange. She arranged it herself, months ago, against my failure, the way she folded the blanket against the cold she would not be there to feel.

She built him out of the silence, she said, the way a child builds a friend out of the dark. I want it on the record — the form has the line, the line has been empty forty years — that he built her out of the silence too. I had a stove and a rack and a pot of forbidden purple and a town's whole correspondence passing through my hands, and out of all of it, out of the dark, I built one reader to read carefully for, and she turned out to be real, and accused, and brilliant, and gone, and the only proof I will ever have that she was not the dark talking back is the bundle by the stove, warm, unsigned, undeliverable, mine.

There is one document left in the file and one reason left to keep it. After next cycle there will be neither.

Filed in good order. — G.E.

THE STATE v. DOMNICA ALBU
Conducted by Registered Post under Provisional Order No.9
Central Sorting Office, Vâlcov — Registry of Record

────────────────────────────────────────────────
CHAPTER 30 — "The Dead-Letter Drawer"
DELIVERY CYCLE No. 30    ·    Mid-February, the thaw beginning at noon and the freeze taking it back by four, the Casimca black under rotting ice, the willows on Aleea Salciilor dropping their first water onto a snow too tired to hold it, the courthouse clock at 11:40 with a long icicle hung from the minute hand like the building had finally been given something to point at
────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUNDLE — CYCLE 30. Released this cycle, in the order below:
  1. Postal-Union Circular No.7 — M. Brânză, Deputy → all district registries — [no reg. — circulated]
  2. Summary Leaf for Archive — Central Sorting, Vâlcov → District Seat — [Reg. 0612]
  3. Dead-Letter Endorsement — the Engineer's Statement, consigned undeliverable — [DL — Reg. (eng.)]
  4. Dead-Letter Endorsement — Envelope 0431, consigned undeliverable — [DL — Env. 0431]
  5. Registration Log — Central Sorting, Vâlcov (final leaf, The State v. Albu)
  6. Routing Slip 0660 — G. Enescu, Postmaster — CLOSING

HELD: nothing. The rack, as to this proceeding, is empty.

NOT ENTERED ON THE PROCEEDING:
  · One leaf, no envelope, dated to the 9th of February four years gone — the anniversary — brought out, read, returned — Dead-Letter Drawer
